# Engram macOS — UI/UX & Functional-Completeness Flow Review

**Date:** 2026-06-14  ·  **Reviewer:** Claude (Opus 4.8, ultracode multi-agent workflow)  ·  **Scope:** `macos/` SwiftUI app + Swift service/MCP

> Goal: trace every end-to-end user workflow and find where features are *isolated islands* — half-built, dead-ending, or where a shipped backend capability has no UI entry (or a UI control backs nothing real).

## Method & confidence

- **28 parallel reviewers** each traced one user workflow / cross-cutting dimension; every medium+ finding was adversarially re-checked against the whole tree.
- **144 findings** (34 high / 53 medium / 57 low), 0 refuted in verification.
- **First-hand spot-checks** (by the lead, not the agents): the 8 write/action service methods (`setSessionHidden`, `renameSession`, `setFavorite`, `exportSession`, `saveInsight`, `deleteInsight`, `setParentSession`, `linkSessions`, `recordSessionAccess`) have **0 callers** in `Engram/Views`+`Components`; `SessionsPageView`/`TimelinePageView` instantiate `ExpandableSessionCard` without the resume closures; `triggerSync` is a hardcoded `"Sync is not implemented in the Swift service"` stub. These mechanical claims are high-confidence.
- **Caveat:** the 0/144 refute rate means the verifier pass was lenient — high-severity functional gaps are high-confidence, but low-severity/visual items are directional. This is a **static code trace** (the app was not built/run); conclusions are based on whether a UI action traces to a real backend call — the correct test for "island" detection.

## Executive summary

Engram's macOS app is structurally complete as a read-only viewer and structurally absent as an action surface. The service (EngramService) and the MCP helper (EngramMCP) ship a near-complete write/action API — setSessionHidden, renameSession, setFavorite, exportSession, saveInsight/deleteInsight, setParentSession/linkSessions, recordSessionAccess, projectMoveBatch, manageProjectAlias, project recover/review, get_costs, file_activity — and almost none of it has a UI entry point. The recurring systemic cause is twofold and consistent across 28 surfaces: (1) "backend capabilities shipped ahead of UI" — every write capability is reachable only through MCP (an AI agent), so the human using the desktop GUI cannot act on their own data; and (2) "read-only viewers never got their action layer" — the ExpandableSessionCard exposes onResume/onHandoff/onReplay/onCopyResumeCommand closures that the two main browse pages (Sessions, Timeline) never pass, leaving the primary value action (resume where you left off) as a silent dead no-op on the exact pages built for browsing. A third pattern compounds it: "viewing toggles ship without their acting half" — there's a "Show hidden sessions" toggle but no Hide; a Favorites star but no favorites list; cost-budget toggles that no consumer reads; Web UI / Bearer Token / CIDR fields that no server reads. Several whole pages (Hygiene, Observability Performance/Traces, triggerSync, health()) are hardcoded "not implemented" placeholders wired into the sidebar as if real. The net effect for a non-MCP user is a beautiful dashboard they can look at but cannot drive, where toggles lie, buttons no-op, and the most-advertised capabilities (cost tracking, memory/insights, export, semantic search) are invisible. Closing the gap is mostly wiring, not new backend: dozens of fixes are passing an already-defined closure or calling an already-defined client method.

## Finding distribution

| Category | Count |
|---|---|
| Broken workflows (user starts a journey, cannot finish) | 13 |
| Island features (built but disconnected) | 14 |
| Backend-capability ↔ UI gaps (shipped backend, no UI entry) | 43 |
| Misleading controls (UI implies a capability the product lacks) | 21 |
| Missing empty/loading/error states | 25 |
| Dead-ends & orphan views | 13 |
| UX / visual consistency | 15 |
| **Total** | **144** |

## Top broken workflows (highest user impact)

### 1. [HIGH] Resume / pick up where I left off (the app's headline value action)

**What breaks:** On the two main browse pages (Sessions, Timeline) right-clicking any session shows Resume / Copy Resume Command / Handoff / Replay, and every one silently no-ops — no clipboard change, no resume, no feedback. The card declares onResume/onHandoff/onReplay/onCopyResumeCommand closures but these pages instantiate it without passing them, so they default to nil. The same menu works from HomeView and SessionDetailView, so behavior is silently inconsistent.

**Evidence:** ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129 (context menu calls onResume?/onHandoff?/onReplay?/onCopyResumeCommand?) and :30-33 (callbacks default nil); SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 passes only onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion; TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 same omission; working wiring at SessionDetailView.swift:188-190

**Fix:** Pass the four already-defined closures from SessionsPageView and TimelinePageView, reusing the HomeView/SessionDetailView handlers (resume/handoff/replay/copy). Pure wiring, no backend work.

### 2. [HIGH] Search a keyword, jump to the match in context

**What breaks:** User finds a session by keyword, clicks it, and lands at the top of the transcript with nothing highlighted; they must re-press find and retype the query. In Text view mode find-in-page is fully inert (working find bar, match count, zero highlight/scroll). Even within Session mode, typing a query shows a count but never scrolls to the first match and Return doesn't advance.

**Evidence:** SearchPageView.swift:222 posts SessionBox only (no query); MainWindowView.swift:45-49 handler ignores query; SessionDetailView.swift:16-18 init has no searchTerm param; :212-226 find bar shown in all modes but :892-920 RawMessageRow (Text mode) has no searchText; :689-701 navigateFind scrolls only Session-mode ids; TranscriptFindBar.swift:19-22 TextField has no onSubmit

**Fix:** Carry the search term through .openSession into SessionDetailView (add searchTerm param, prime showFind + first match), wire RawMessageRow to highlight searchText, add onSubmit→next on the find field, and scroll to first match on query entry.

### 3. [HIGH] Curate / clean up the session library (hide, unhide, rename, favorite-retrieve)

**What breaks:** The entire act half of curation is missing from the GUI. There's a 'Show hidden sessions' toggle but no way to hide a session and no way to unhide one (so the toggle is permanently meaningless from the app). renameSession exists and displayTitle honors it, but no UI sets it — sessions are stuck with auto-titles. Favorites are write-only: starring works but nothing in the app lists or filters favorites. Hygiene's hideEmptySessions() bulk-cleanup has zero callers. All of these are reachable only via MCP.

**Evidence:** setSessionHidden EngramServiceClient.swift:168 (0 app callers; SessionsPageView.swift:43 toggle); renameSession EngramServiceClient.swift:175 (0 app callers; display honored at Session.swift:86-87); setFavorite SessionDetailView.swift:168-180 + listFavorites Database.swift:627 (0 callers, Screen.swift:6-25 no favorites case); hideEmptySessions EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:686-698 (0 app callers)

**Fix:** Add Hide/Unhide and Rename to the session context menu + TranscriptToolbar (call the existing client methods); add a Favorites filter/screen reading listFavorites; expose hideEmptySessions behind a confirmation dialog on the Hygiene or Sessions page.

### 4. [HIGH] View and manage memory / insights

**What breaks:** The 'Memory' nav item — the saved-insights feature the product advertises — shows only filesystem CLAUDE.md previews (truncated to 200 chars, no full-file view), never the DB insights written via save_insight. A user can never view, add, edit, or delete an insight from the app; the entire saveInsight/deleteInsight/get_insights surface is agent-only. The two halves of 'memory' (markdown files vs insights table) are disconnected, so the page misrepresents what the product remembers.

**Evidence:** MemoryView.swift:6,93 loads only memoryFiles(); EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:160-193 scans only .md, :185 preview prefix(200); saveInsight/deleteInsight EngramServiceClient.swift:80-87 (0 app callers); get_insights MCP-only MCPToolRegistry.swift:324,852

**Fix:** Add an insights list/read path to MemoryView (read get_insights/insights table), a full-file viewer for memory .md, and save/delete insight controls wired to the existing client methods.

### 5. [HIGH] Agent-session grouping review and manual linking

**What breaks:** The dedicated 'Agents' screen — the page named for the feature — is a flat, ungrouped read-only list (uses plain SessionCard, not ExpandableSessionCard) with no confirm/dismiss/relink affordances and no app-wide 'pending suggestions' view, so suggestions are only discoverable by expanding the exact right parent elsewhere. Manual linking (setParentSession/linkSessions) has a backend + capability token but no UI anywhere: if the heuristic misses a relationship the user cannot create the correct link, only accept/reject what was already guessed.

**Evidence:** AgentsView.swift:34 uses SessionCard (no confirm/dismiss/expand), :54 listSessions(subAgent:true); ExpandableSessionCard.swift:34-35,172-184 has the confirm/dismiss callbacks AgentsView never passes; setParentSession EngramServiceClient.swift:96 + ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27 — 0 app callers, only StartupBackfills.swift uses it; suggestions loaded only on parent expand ExpandableSessionCard.swift:236-262

**Fix:** Rebuild AgentsView on ExpandableSessionCard with grouping + confirm/dismiss; add a 'pending suggestions' list; add a 'Set parent / Link to…' picker calling setParentSession/linkSessions.

### 6. [HIGH] Cost / usage tracking (a headline value proposition)

**What breaks:** Real per-dollar cost data (get_costs over session_costs) has no app UI — the GUI shows only a count of 'costed' sessions, never a dollar figure or breakdown, so a non-MCP user cannot answer 'how much have I spent.' Worse, the cost-budget and threshold settings actively mislead: a user who sets a $20 daily budget and enables 'Notify on cost threshold' / 'Notify on long session' will never get an alert because no consumer reads those flags — UsagePressureNotifier reads only monitor.enabled/notifyOnUsagePressure.

**Evidence:** getCosts MCPDatabase.swift:196-251 + get_costs MCPToolRegistry.swift:778-780; SourcePulseView.swift:100-102 count pill only, no $; budget/threshold UI SettingsView.swift:308-342 persisted :517-528 but no consumer (grep dailyCostBudget/notifyOnCostThreshold/notifyOnLongSession = none); UsagePressureNotifier.swift:8-14 reads only monitor.enabled+notifyOnUsagePressure

**Fix:** Surface get_costs (total + per-source $) on Activity/Source Pulse; wire the budget/threshold/long-session flags into UsagePressureNotifier or remove the misleading controls until honored.

### 7. [HIGH] Service recovery on first run / startup failure

**What breaks:** If EngramService fails to start (helper missing, socket/lock contention, denied runtime dir), the user gets a warning triangle and an error string but no recover/restart button — their only option is to quit and relaunch the whole app, which they may not know to do. There is also no 'first index in progress' state, so a brand-new user whose index is still running sees 'No sessions' / 'No recent work' and may quit thinking the app is broken.

**Evidence:** App.swift:147-150,127-146; EngramServiceLauncher.swift:229-237; MenuBarController.swift:356-385 (no restart control; only LaunchAgent toggle GeneralSettingsSection.swift:93); first-index state absent HomeView.swift:81-85,107-113 and SessionsPageView.swift:61-63 (only isRunning checked); PopoverView.swift:136-152 no empty state

**Fix:** Add a 'Restart service' action to the menu bar / error banner that re-invokes serviceLauncher; add an explicit 'indexing in progress' state distinct from 'no data' across Home, Sessions, and the popover.

## Island features (look complete, deliver nothing)

### Favorites (star)

- **Exists:** TranscriptToolbar star button + setFavorite write + listFavorites() DB read
- **Missing:** No screen, filter, pill, or sidebar item that reads favorites; the browse list shows no star and offers no Favorites filter, so starring is write-only and unverifiable from where users browse
- **Evidence:** TranscriptToolbar.swift:55-62; SessionDetailView.swift:168-180,442; Database.swift:627 listFavorites() 0 callers; Screen.swift:6-25 no favorites case; SessionsPageView.swift:22 timeOptions has no Favorites filter

### Replay (temporal session playback)

- **Exists:** A full Replay view with density heatmap, play/pause, role badges, and color bars
- **Missing:** Role detection is structurally dead (every message renders 'Unknown' identical coloring); timestamps/durations/tokens are never populated so the density bar is always flat and playback timing always uniform; tool calls are filtered out entirely; the summary is appended as a phantom final message — the feature looks built but delivers none of its differentiating value, and its context-menu entry no-ops on Sessions/Timeline
- **Evidence:** EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:918-928 (role 'unknown' fallback), :905-914 (timestamp/tool/tokens/duration all nil); IndexJobRunner.swift:207-215 (user/assistant only, summary appended); ReplayState.swift:62-67,138; SessionReplayView.swift:146-175,183,225-231

### Search mode selector (keyword/semantic/hybrid) + Embeddings status

- **Exists:** Mode-pill UI code, 'both'/'semantic' badge branches, an Embeddings status row on Home and an Embedding dot in the popover, an 'N/M embedded' search pill
- **Missing:** availableModes always returns [.keyword] so pills never render and semantic/hybrid cases are unreachable; embeddingStatus has no production assignment so the Home/popover dots are permanently dead and imply semantic search the product cannot do (Swift search is keyword-only)
- **Evidence:** SearchSupport.swift:9-11; SearchPageView.swift:141,143-157,160-167; EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:37 (no assignment); HomeView.swift:225-230; PopoverView.swift:66-73

### Project migration history & remediation (recover/review/timeline/batch/alias)

- **Exists:** Full backend + MCP for project_recover, project_review, project_timeline, projectMoveBatch, manageProjectAlias, and a migration ledger with auditNote/detail/archived/state fields
- **Missing:** No app surface reads any of it: history is shown only as an Undo picker (last 5 committed, framed as 'pick one to reverse'); batch move and alias management are MCP-only; the UI even directs users to an `engram` CLI that doesn't ship, so following the app's own remediation advice dead-ends
- **Evidence:** UndoSheet.swift:254-257 (committed, limit 5); ProjectsView.swift:120-144 single-project only; MCPDatabase.swift:463 / MCPFileTools.swift:19 / Database.swift:558 (no app callers); CLI-deferral RenameSheet.swift:81,397 / ArchiveSheet.swift:177 / UndoSheet.swift:314 (no bin in package.json/project.yml)

### Hooks / Skills / Sources pages

- **Exists:** Read-only lists of Claude Code hooks, skills/commands, and detected sources with names, descriptions, and file paths
- **Missing:** Zero next actions: rows don't open/reveal/edit; no enable/disable/test/toggle for hooks or sources; Skills rows don't reveal the printed path in Finder (a pattern the app already has elsewhere); the hook DTO even drops the source file URL, structurally blocking any 'jump to hook' action
- **Evidence:** HooksView.swift:19,36-54; SkillsView.swift:51-64 (vs RepoDetailView.swift:69 / SourcePulseView.swift:181 selectFile pattern); SourcesSettingsSection.swift:78-93 read-only DataSourceRow; EngramServiceModels.swift:578-583 (DTO drops url)

### Activity / Timeline / Repos / WorkGraph dashboards

- **Exists:** Charts, heatmaps, repo bars, date-grouped lists
- **Missing:** Every chart/hour/day/source/repo/session row is non-interactive — no drill-in to the underlying sessions; Timeline's bar-chart icon implies a graph but renders a flat list with a hardcoded unchangeable 30d window; WorkGraph is a duplicate of Repos as bars (no edges, despite the 'graph' name); file_activity backend has zero UI on the page literally named Activity; StackedActivityChart and per-project timeline are built but never rendered
- **Evidence:** ActivityView.swift:27-43 (no taps); TimelinePageView.swift:55,70-100,120 (icon chart.bar, list, days:30 hardcoded); WorkGraphView.swift:36-39,124-133 (bars, no edges) vs ReposView.swift:84; getFileActivity MCPDatabase.swift:313-353 (0 app callers); StackedActivityChart ActivityChart.swift:36-79 / dailySourceActivity Database.swift:861 (test-only callers)

### Command palette (⌘K)

- **Exists:** A palette scaffolded with .navigation/.session/.action categories and dead paletteItems/paletteSelection state in MainWindowView
- **Missing:** Only navigation + session-jump are implemented; no action commands (export/resume/re-index/toggle settings); session results dead-end at navigate, you can't act on the session you found — confirming the palette was built for a richer model never finished
- **Evidence:** PaletteItem.swift:4-8,20,25 (only .navigation produced); CommandPaletteView.swift:21-27,35-40; MainWindowView.swift:8-9,63-66,121-141

## Backend ↔ UI gap matrix

| Backend capability | Gap | Evidence |
|---|---|---|
| setSessionHidden — hide/unhide a session | Full client + service handler + MCP tool; zero app callers. UI offers only the 'Show hidden sessions' view toggle, never a way to create or restore a hidden session. | EngramServiceClient.swift:168; EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:611-644; MCPToolRegistry.swift:972; SessionsPageView.swift:43 toggle; 0 callers under Engram/Views |
| renameSession — set a custom session title | Client + handler exist; displayTitle (Session.swift:86-87) already honors it; no UI sets it. Only project rename exists (unrelated). Bulk 'Regenerate All' is the only title control. | EngramServiceClient.swift:175; EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:295-298,646-658; 0 app callers |
| exportSession — Markdown/JSON/HTML export with redaction | Complete TranscriptExportService writing to ~/.engram/exports + client + capability token + MCP tool; no in-app button. Desktop users get only clipboard copy, and the output path is never revealed in Finder. | TranscriptExportService.swift:7-56; EngramServiceClient.swift:193; ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:37; MCPToolRegistry.swift:422; SessionDetailView.swift:400 copyAllTranscript only; 0 app callers |
| saveInsight / deleteInsight — memory write/delete | Client + handlers + MCP tools; zero app callers. Insights can only be written by an MCP agent; the human-facing Memory page is a dead-end viewer. | EngramServiceClient.swift:80-87; EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:898,970; MCPToolRegistry.swift:931,958; 0 app callers |
| setParentSession / linkSessions — manual agent-session linking | Client + protocol + handler + capability token; only the automatic path-based backfill uses setParentSession. App views call only confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion/clearParentSession, so users can accept/reject guesses but never create a correct link. | EngramServiceClient.swift:96,157; EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:149-157,1225; ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27; StartupBackfills.swift:806,1173 only; 0 app view callers |
| recordSessionAccess — update last-accessed for recency sort | Client + handler + accessedDesc/Asc sort + last_accessed_at column all exist; never called by app or MCP, and the access sort isn't selectable in any UI, so opening/resuming a session never affects 'recent' ordering. | EngramServiceClient.swift:182; EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:305-308,660; Database.swift:11-12,39; ResumeDialog.swift:131-143 (resume doesn't record); 0 callers |
| AI summary generation (generateSummary / settings) | Full provider/prompt/generation settings saved (AISettingsSection) and a generateSummary handler exist, but the in-app per-session Generate/Regenerate button was removed — only MCP generate_summary remains. The whole top of the AI settings page configures something the app can't trigger. 'Regenerate All' returns only 'started' with no progress/completion. | AISettingsSection.swift:51-199,283-300; SessionDetailView.swift:28-31 (in-app entry removed); EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:871-896,1081-1132; summary_generated event never emitted (EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:33,88-90 dead) |
| get_costs / session_costs — per-dollar cost data | Real cost totals + breakdown queryable via MCP over the session_costs table; the GUI renders only a count, never a $ figure. | MCPDatabase.swift:196-251; MCPToolRegistry.swift:778-780; SchemaManifest.swift:18; SourcePulseView.swift:100-102 count only; 0 $ renderings in views |
| getFileActivity / session_files — per-file hotspots | Backend query exists and is exposed to MCP; the page literally named 'Activity' loads no file data, so this whole dimension is invisible to humans. | MCPDatabase.swift:313-353; ActivityView.swift:59-66 (no file query); 0 references in Engram views |
| projectMoveBatch / manageProjectAlias / projectRecover / projectReview | Backend + MCP for batch project moves, alias merges, and migration recovery/inspection; no app UI. Users reorganizing many projects must repeat single moves, and the inspect/recover half the UI keeps recommending is unreachable. | EngramServiceClient.swift:88,153; MCPToolRegistry.swift:873,980-998,1048-1054,1062; MCPDatabase.swift:463; MCPFileTools.swift:19; ProjectsView.swift:120-144 single-project only; 0 app callers |
| triggerSync — on-demand re-index / 'Sync now' | Client method exists but the service handler is a hardcoded 'not implemented' stub; no UI calls it. Adding a source or a late-appearing path can't be picked up on demand with feedback; SourcePulseView refresh only re-reads counts. | EngramServiceClient.swift:121-123; EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:796-808 (returns error); SourcePulseView.swift:72-73,160-178; 0 UI callers |
| Web UI enable + 'Web API & Security' (host/CIDR/bearer token) | webUIEnabled defaults false and can only be set by hand-editing settings.json — no toggle anywhere — so the 'Open Web UI' button is permanently disabled in a default install. The Advanced httpHost/httpAllowCIDR/httpBearerToken fields are persisted but read by NO Swift code; the server always binds 127.0.0.1:3457 with an internally generated token, making the Bearer Token field a security-relevant false promise. | EngramServiceRunner.swift:86-122,662-679 (gate, default false, per-launch token); GeneralSettingsSection.swift:64-69,134-138 (button disabled); SettingsView.swift:445-511 (httpHost/CIDR/bearer saved, no reader); EngramWebUIServer.swift:37 |
| Source enable/disable | No enable flag exists anywhere — every detected source is indexed unconditionally and SourcesSettingsSection rows are read-only Text. A user who wants to stop indexing a noisy tool has no control. | SourcesSettingsSection.swift:4-29,78-93 (read-only, key never consumed); EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:564-572 (sources() GROUP BY, no enabled flag) |
| Strict single writer toggle (Network settings) | The only operational-looking Network switch is a no-op in the shipped product; mcpStrictSingleWriter is read only by removed TypeScript/Node MCP code. Its caption explicitly promises behavior no Swift code implements. | NetworkSettingsSection.swift:31-33,60-65; grep finds the flag only in NetworkSettingsSection.swift + legacy src/index.ts |

## Cross-cutting UX / consistency issues

- **Hardcoded 'not implemented' pages wired into the sidebar as if real — Hygiene always shows Score 0 + 'checks not implemented'; Observability Performance/Traces are permanent 'not collected' placeholders; the backend health() endpoint is a constant 'healthy' stub no UI consumes. A user clicking these reasonably concludes the app is broken.**
  - _Scope:_ Hygiene page, Observability (2 of 5 tabs), health() endpoint
  - _Evidence:_ EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:810-828 (hygiene placeholder); PerformanceView.swift:11-26 + TraceExplorerView.swift:11-27 (EmptyState only); EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:104-106,556-558 (health() constant); HygieneView.swift:54,189

- **Observability is a developer diagnostics surface exposed to all users with no gating, and it can't even read the data that matters: on a notarized/hardened build the log reader can't access the EngramService (indexer) process logs, and all message bodies are logged with privacy:.private so they read back as '<private>'. The Logs/Errors tabs look populated but show redacted, app-only content; the 'warn' filter is a dead path (warnings misclassified as errors).**
  - _Scope:_ Observability — Logs, Errors, Health
  - _Evidence:_ Screen.swift:12,102 (top-level, no gate); OSLogReader.swift:30-52,84 (no warn case, can't read service pid); EngramLogger.swift:24-37 / ServiceLogger.swift:29-46 (privacy:.private); LogStreamView.swift:15,145; ErrorDashboardView.swift:73

- **Empty/loading/error states are inconsistent and frequently misleading. Many pages track isLoading but never render a spinner, so first paint shows zeroed KPIs/charts that read as 'no data'; empty states say 'No sessions match your filters' even with no filters applied; an indexing-in-progress catalog string exists but is wired to no view; Timeline and Search swallow load errors silently, showing a false 'no data' empty state.**
  - _Scope:_ Activity, Timeline, Sessions, Search, Repos/WorkGraph, Memory, Skills, Hooks, popover
  - _Evidence:_ ActivityView.swift:12,52-53 (isLoading never read); TimelinePageView.swift:49,130-132 (errors only logged); SessionsPageView.swift:62 misleading copy + Localizable.xcstrings:1460 unused 'after indexing' string; SearchPageView.swift:452-454 swallows double-fault

- **Filesystem-backed pages (Memory, Skills, Hooks) load once and never refresh when the underlying files change, with no refresh button; the popover never refreshes while open; AgentsView never refreshes when indexing adds sessions — so users see stale data after editing settings.json or while sessions are actively running.**
  - _Scope:_ Memory, Skills, Hooks, popover, Agents
  - _Evidence:_ MemoryView.swift:87 / SkillsView.swift:48 / HooksView.swift:33 (single .task, no refreshable); PopoverView.swift:31 (single .task, .transient); AgentsView.swift:45 (.task once, no totalSessions id) vs ProjectsView.swift:191 / HomeView.swift:41

- **Two surfaces both called 'Sources' that overlap and neither is actionable (dashboard implies management, settings pane implies configuration; both read-only and disjoint); Windsurf/Antigravity render as normal healthy sources with no 'live sync disabled' indicator, silently misleading those users into thinking recent sessions are captured live; the Settings source catalog is a hardcoded drifted list (Pi/OpenClaw/Hermes) that doesn't match the 17 real adapters.**
  - _Scope:_ Source Pulse + Sources settings
  - _Evidence:_ Screen.swift:39,103 + SettingsView.swift:105 (two 'Sources'); SourcesSettingsSection.swift:10-29 (drifted catalog) vs MessageParser.swift:114-132; enableLiveSync:false MessageParser.swift:128-129 with no UI indicator

- **Non-actionable surfaces present signals with no matching action: KPI cards on Today look clickable but navigate nowhere; Home Service-State rows show a Web UI host:port and 'Check Advanced diagnostics' as un-clickable strings (and the named target section doesn't exist); usage-pressure notifications carry no actions/deep-link; menu bar badge advertises live sessions but the popover shows none and the live view is buried 3 levels deep; popover open is double-click-only with no affordance.**
  - _Scope:_ Home, menu bar / popover, notifications
  - _Evidence:_ KPICard.swift:4-43 (no interactive modifier) + HomeView.swift:70-79; HomeView.swift:219-245,553-579 (un-actionable rows, 'Advanced diagnostics' vs actual 'Advanced'); MenuBarController.swift:408-414 vs PopoverView.swift:136-152; UsagePressureNotifier.swift:74-87; PopoverView.swift:154-181 (double-click, no hint)

- **Visual token drift: 111 raw `.secondary` vs 46 Theme.secondaryText (gray shifts shade between dashboard and Settings/sheets); Theme color tokens exist but components re-hardcode the same hex literals (guaranteeing future divergence); card corner radius spans 9 values (KPICard=10, SessionCard=8) with no shared token; Settings re-implements source display names ('Claude' vs 'Claude Code', 'iFlow' vs 'Iflow'); status colors hardcoded as raw .green/.red/.orange instead of Theme tokens.**
  - _Scope:_ App-wide (Settings, sheets, cards, status banners)
  - _Evidence:_ Theme.swift:50-54,81-85; KPICard.swift:21,28 / AlertBanner.swift:11-32 / TierBar.swift:13-16 (hardcoded hex); SourceColors.swift:33,50 vs SettingsView.swift:694-708; corner radii 9 distinct values

## Quick wins (mostly pure wiring, no new backend)

| Effort | Fix | Evidence |
|---|---|---|
| S | Wire the four existing closures (onResume/onCopyResumeCommand/onHandoff/onReplay) into ExpandableSessionCard on SessionsPageView and TimelinePageView, reusing HomeView's handlers — instantly un-deadens the primary value action and the Replay menu on both main browse pages. | SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 + TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 omit the closures defined at ExpandableSessionCard.swift:30-33,116-129; working pattern at SessionDetailView.swift:188-190 / HomeView TodaySessionRow |
| S | Add Hide/Unhide and Rename items to the session context menu + TranscriptToolbar, calling the already-defined EngramServiceClient.setSessionHidden / renameSession — makes the 'Show hidden sessions' toggle meaningful and lets users fix auto-titles. | EngramServiceClient.swift:168,175 (0 app callers); SessionsPageView.swift:43 toggle; ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129 menu has no Hide/Rename |
| M | Carry the search term through .openSession into SessionDetailView (prime showFind + first match) and have RawMessageRow honor searchText — closes the search→context handoff and fixes find-in-Text-mode in one path. | SearchPageView.swift:222 + MainWindowView.swift:45-49 drop the query; SessionDetailView.swift:16-18,212-226,892-920 |
| M | Make Activity/Timeline/Repos/WorkGraph rows and charts post .openSession (drill-in) — the exact NotificationCenter pattern already used in HomeView/SessionsPageView — converting read-only dashboards into launch points. | ActivityView.swift:27-43, WorkGraphView.swift:103-153, RepoDetailView.swift:105-126, SourcePulseView.swift:78-124 all static; working pattern HomeView.swift:302 / SessionsPageView.swift:73 |
| S | Add an 'Export…' context-menu/toolbar item calling exportSession and reveal the returned outputPath in Finder via the existing NSWorkspace.selectFile pattern — exposes a complete shipped feature with no backend work. | exportSession EngramServiceClient.swift:193 + TranscriptExportService.swift:7-56 (returns outputPath); NSWorkspace.selectFile pattern RepoDetailView.swift:69 / SourcePulseView.swift:181 |
| S | Make Skills/Hooks rows reveal their (already-displayed) file path in Finder using the existing selectFile helper; add a manual Refresh to Memory/Skills/Hooks/popover — turns read-only dead-ends into usable viewers. | SkillsView.swift:51-64 (path shown, no action) + displayPath EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:284-289; HooksView.swift:33 / MemoryView.swift:87 single .task |
| M | Remove or gate the controls that lie: the dead cost-budget/threshold toggles, the no-op Strict-single-writer switch, the unread Bearer Token/CIDR fields, the wrong MCP-HTTP-endpoint URL, and the dead Embeddings status rows — every one currently implies a guarantee or capability that does not exist. | SettingsView.swift:308-342,445-511 (no consumers); NetworkSettingsSection.swift:31-65; GeneralSettingsSection.swift:74-132 (wrong /mcp URL); HomeView.swift:225-230 + PopoverView.swift:66-73 (dead embeddingStatus) |

---

## Appendix — all findings (grouped by category, severity-sorted)

### Broken workflows (user starts a journey, cannot finish) (13)

#### `search-1` · 🔴 High · Search term does not carry into the opened transcript — no highlight, user must re-type

- **Surface:** Keyword search → results → open
- **What's wrong:** The core 'search → results → open' journey breaks at the last step. Clicking a search result posts NotificationCenter.default.post(name: .openSession, object: SessionBox(session)) with ONLY the session object and no query. MainWindowView's .openSession handler sets selectedSession = box.session (MainWindowView.swift:48) and presents SessionDetailView(session:onBack:). SessionDetailView's init (SessionDetailView.swift:16-18) accepts only `session` and `onBack` — it has no search-term parameter. Its in-transcript find state `searchText` is internal @State defaulting to "" (SessionDetailView.swift:51) and `showFind` defaults to false (line 50). So after a user searches for a keyword, sees a matching snippet, and clicks through, the transcript opens with the find bar closed and empty. The matched location is not scrolled to or highlighted; the user must reopen the find bar and re-type the exact query.
- **User impact:** User finds a session by keyword and clicks it, but lands at the top of the transcript with nothing highlighted. They have to manually press the find shortcut and retype the same query to locate the match they just saw in the search snippet. The search-to-context handoff that makes keyword search useful is missing.
- **Evidence:** SearchPageView.swift:222 (post .openSession with SessionBox(session) only); MainWindowView.swift:45-49 (handler ignores any query); SessionDetailView.swift:16-18 (init has no searchTerm param); SessionDetailView.swift:50-52 (showFind=false, searchText="", currentMatchIndex=-1 defaults)
- **Suggested fix:** Carry the query through the open action: post the query alongside the session (e.g. an enum payload or a SearchOpen struct), have MainWindowView pass it into SessionDetailView via an `initialSearch:` parameter, and seed `searchText`/`showFind=true` so the transcript auto-highlights and scrolls to the first match on open.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified the full open path carries no query. SearchPageView.swift:222 posts NotificationCenter .openSession with object SessionBox(session) only. SessionBox (AppNotifications.swift:11-17) wraps only a Session — no query/searchTerm field. The .openSession Name (AppNotifications.swift:6) and all 10 post sites carry only a SessionBox. MainWindowView.swift:45-49 sets selectedSession=box.session, ignoring any query. SessionDetailView.swift:16-18 init takes only session+onBack; no searchTerm param. showFind defaults false (line 50), searchText defaults "" (line 51), currentMatchIndex -1 (line 52), and the per-session load task explicitly resets searchText="" and currentMatchIndex=-1 on every open (lines 428,427). Grep for searchTerm/initialQuery/highlightTerm/openSessionWithQuery across Engram+Shared found no carry mechanism — the only matches are SessionDetailView's internal find-bar @State. So after search->click the transcript opens with an empty, closed find bar; the matched snippet location is not scrolled-to or highlighted; the user must re-type the query. Real broken last step of the core journey. High is appropriate.

#### `session-detail-transcript-1` · 🔴 High · Find-in-page is inert in "Text" view mode but the find bar stays fully operational

- **Surface:** Open session → read transcript → find-in-page
- **What's wrong:** The transcript toolbar offers two view modes, Session and Text (TranscriptToolbar.swift:66-71, TranscriptViewMode at TranscriptToolbar.swift:4-9). The find bar (⌘F / Find button) toggles independently of view mode and is rendered above the content regardless (SessionDetailView.swift:212-226). In Text mode the content is rendered by RawMessageRow via `ForEach(messages) { msg in RawMessageRow(message: msg) }` (SessionDetailView.swift:368-372). RawMessageRow takes only `message` and has no `searchText` parameter, so it never highlights matches (RawMessageRow at SessionDetailView.swift:892-920). Worse, navigation is broken: `navigateFind` resolves the target via `displayIndexed[msgIndex].id` and sets `scrollTarget` (SessionDetailView.swift:689-701), but in Text mode the ScrollView contains `RawMessageRow` rows keyed by `messages` identity — there are no `.id(indexed.id)` anchors for the ScrollViewReader to scroll to, so Prev/Next does nothing visible. The match count still shows a number (scanned over displayIndexed), so the bar looks alive while delivering no highlight and no scroll.
- **User impact:** A user who switches to Text view and presses ⌘F sees a working-looking find bar with a match count, types a query, and gets zero highlights and zero scrolling on Prev/Next. The feature silently does nothing in half the available view modes.
- **Evidence:** SessionDetailView.swift:212-226 (find bar shown regardless of viewMode); SessionDetailView.swift:362-373 (Text mode uses RawMessageRow, Session mode uses ColorBarMessageView with .id(indexed.id)); SessionDetailView.swift:892-920 (RawMessageRow has no searchText); SessionDetailView.swift:689-701 (navigateFind scrolls to displayIndexed ids only)
- **Suggested fix:** Either hide/disable the find bar when viewMode == .text, or pass searchText into RawMessageRow and add `.id` anchors plus a matchIndices set keyed to `messages` so navigation and highlight work in Text mode too.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified against source. Find bar is gated ONLY by `if showFind` (SessionDetailView.swift:212), never by viewMode — it stays fully operational in Text mode. Text mode renders `ForEach(messages) { msg in RawMessageRow(message: msg); Divider() }` with NO `.id()` modifier (SessionDetailView.swift:368-372). RawMessageRow has only `let message: ChatMessage` (SessionDetailView.swift:892-894) — no searchText param, no highlight (compare ColorBarMessageView.swift:6,74-96 which DOES highlight via searchText). navigateFind sets `scrollTarget = displayed[msgIndex].id` (SessionDetailView.swift:699) and onChange(scrollTarget) calls `proxy.scrollTo(target)` (SessionDetailView.swift:380-384); in Text mode there is no matching `.id` anchor so scrollTo no-ops → Prev/Next do nothing visible. Match count is computed over displayIndexed unconditionally (updateMatchIndicesDebounced, SessionDetailView.swift:146-153; bar reads matchIndices.count, line 216) so the bar shows a live number while delivering no highlight and no scroll. I grepped the whole Engram/Shared tree for any viewMode guard on the find bar or any searchText wiring into RawMessageRow — none exists. Note the gap is actually slightly WORSE than stated: in Text mode the count is scanned over the FILTERED `displayIndexed` set while the view shows the unfiltered raw `messages`, so the count can even diverge from what is on screen. High severity is justified — broken workflow with a UI that looks alive.

#### `replay-1` · 🔴 High · Replay role detection is structurally dead: every message renders as "Unknown"

- **Surface:** Session replay
- **What's wrong:** SessionReplayView/ReplayState classify each entry's role via the backend, which calls replayRoleAndPreview() and matches the content against literal prefixes "User:"/"Assistant:"/"Tool:". But the FTS content that feeds replay is written WITHOUT any role prefix: buildSearchContent appends `contents.append(message.content)` (raw body, no prefix) and replaceFtsContent inserts it verbatim. So the prefix check never matches and every entry falls through to the default `("unknown", "message", ...)`. In the UI, entry.role.capitalized always shows the badge "Unknown", and roleColor() returns the default tool color for everything, so user and assistant turns are visually identical and mislabeled.
- **User impact:** User opens Replay and sees every single message — their own prompts and the assistant's replies — labeled "Unknown" in identical coloring. The replay cannot be read as a conversation; it looks like an undifferentiated stream, making it strictly worse than the static color-coded transcript.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:918-928 (prefix match → else returns role "unknown"); macos/EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/IndexJobRunner.swift:207-210 (appends raw message.content, no prefix; tool messages filtered out entirely); macos/EngramCoreWrite/Database/FTSRebuildPolicy.swift:115-116 (INSERT content verbatim); consumed at macos/Engram/Views/Replay/SessionReplayView.swift:183 (role.capitalized badge) and :225-231 (roleColor default = tool color)
- **Suggested fix:** Have buildSearchContent prefix each line with the role (e.g. "User: "/"Assistant: ") so the existing replay parser matches, OR (better) source replayTimeline from the messages table / adapter stream that already carries role+timestamp+tokens instead of reverse-parsing FTS blobs.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified end-to-end. buildSearchContent (EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/IndexJobRunner.swift:204-211) appends raw message.content with NO role prefix; replaceFtsContent (EngramCoreWrite/Database/FTSRebuildPolicy.swift:112-117) inserts the string verbatim. Production replayTimeline reads SELECT rowid, content FROM sessions_fts (EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:646-660) and passes content to replayRoleAndPreview, which only matches literal 'User:'/'Assistant:'/'Tool:' prefixes (:918-928) and otherwise returns ('unknown','message',...). A whole-tree grep for those prefixes across Engram/EngramCoreWrite/EngramCoreRead/EngramService/Shared found only the read-provider's own matcher and the unrelated MessageTypeClassifier heuristic; nothing writes those prefixes into FTS content. So every entry resolves to 'unknown'; SessionReplayView.swift:183 renders entry.role.capitalized = 'Unknown' and roleColor (:225-231) returns the default (tool) color for all. The view IS reachable (SessionDetailView.swift:189,460-461 presents SessionReplayView via a sheet from the toolbar Replay button, TranscriptToolbar.swift:104-114), so this is a real user-visible defect. Severity high upheld.

#### `xc-deadends-3` · 🔴 High · Hide/unhide session has no UI control — only a 'Show hidden' viewing toggle exists

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** setSessionHidden(sessionId:hidden:) exists in the service client and capability token, and SessionsPageView has a persisted "Show hidden sessions" toggle that surfaces already-hidden sessions. But nothing in the app ever calls setSessionHidden: there is no Hide action on the card context menu, in SessionDetailView, or anywhere. The user can VIEW hidden sessions but cannot hide a session, nor unhide one they are now viewing.
- **User impact:** The hide/unhide journey is half-built: the app gives you a switch to reveal hidden sessions but no way to actually hide a noisy session or restore a hidden one, so the noise-management feature is a dead end from the GUI.
- **Evidence:** Client method: macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift:168 func setSessionHidden; capability macos/Shared/Service/ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:33 "setSessionHidden". Viewing toggle: macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:43 Toggle("Show hidden sessions"). No-caller proof: grep setSessionHidden across macos/Engram/ returns no matches (exit 1). Card context menu (ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-130, 342-355) has no Hide/Unhide entry.
- **Suggested fix:** Add Hide/Unhide to the session-card context menu and SessionDetailView toolbar wired to serviceClient.setSessionHidden, then refresh the list.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. setSessionHidden exists only in service plumbing: EngramServiceClient.swift:168-171, protocol :34, mock :233, capability ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:33. Grep for setSessionHidden / hideSession / 'Hide' / 'Unhide' across macos/Engram/ AND macos/Shared/ returns matches ONLY in the service client/protocol/mock/capability — zero UI callers and no 'Hide'/'Unhide' button text anywhere in the app. SessionsPageView.swift:43 only has the 'Show hidden sessions' AppStorage VIEW toggle (showHiddenSessions), which controls includeHidden in the read query (:71, :111) — it surfaces already-hidden rows but never calls setSessionHidden. The card context menu (ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129, 342-355) has no Hide/Unhide entry; SessionDetailView has no hide control. So the user can VIEW hidden sessions but has no affordance to hide a session or unhide one. Severity high stands: an asymmetric/broken workflow where the inverse action is entirely missing from the product surface.

#### `xc-capability-matrix-2` · 🔴 High · Favorites are write-only: you can star a session but nothing in the app shows or filters favorites

- **Surface:** X-cut: backend capability ↔ UI exposure matrix
- **What's wrong:** setFavorite is wired to a star toggle in the transcript toolbar (TranscriptToolbar.swift:55, invoked from SessionDetailView.swift:168-178), so a user can mark a session favorite. But grep for favorite/isFavorite/starred across Views/Pages and Components finds no favorites list, no filter pill, and no 'Favorites' surface. The star write goes nowhere the user can ever observe.
- **User impact:** User stars sessions to find them later, then has no way to retrieve their favorites. The action appears functional (star fills in) but produces no reachable result — a dead-end journey for a core organizational action.
- **Evidence:** EngramServiceClient.swift:161 setFavorite; write call site SessionDetailView.swift:168-178 + TranscriptToolbar.swift:55-62. Read side: grep 'favorite|isFavorite|starred' in Views/Pages and Components returns no list/filter/pill surface (only the toggle itself).
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Favorites' filter pill in SessionsPageView/SessionListView or a Favorites section in HomeView that queries favorited sessions, so the star a user sets is reachable again.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed and arguably stronger than claimed. The star write IS wired (SessionDetailView.swift:171-175 calls serviceClient.setFavorite; TranscriptToolbar.swift:56-62 renders star.fill). The read side exists in the DB layer (Database.swift:627 listFavorites(), :639 isFavorite) but listFavorites() has ZERO call sites anywhere outside its definition. isFavorite is read only to populate the toggle's own state (SessionDetailView.swift:442). There is no Favorites screen (Screen enum Screen.swift:6-25 has no favorites case), no filter pill. The 'Favorites' and 'No favorites yet' localization strings (Localizable.xcstrings:998,1154) are orphaned — grep for them in *.swift returns nothing, meaning a favorites UI was scaffolded in strings/DB but never built. Write-only confirmed; high severity stands.

#### `onboarding-firstrun-1` · 🟠 Medium · No file-access / Full Disk Access permission step or guidance for reading other apps' ~/Library data

- **Surface:** First run / onboarding / zero-state
- **What's wrong:** The app ships unsandboxed (Engram.entitlements:5 "No app sandbox") so it never triggers a sandbox file-access prompt for ~/.claude or ~/.codex. But several sources live under ~/Library/Application Support (CursorAdapter, VsCodeAdapter; onboarding scans .../Cursor/User/globalStorage/state.vscdb and .../Code/User/workspaceStorage at OnboardingView.swift:173,178), which modern macOS (Sequoia+) gates behind TCC App-Management / Full Disk Access. Nothing in onboarding (OnboardingView.swift, all 3 steps) or anywhere in the app (no match for 'Full Disk', 'TCC', 'System Settings', 'Privacy', NSOpenPanel across Engram/, Shared/, EngramService/) requests or explains this access. If reads are denied, the adapters silently return nothing and the service emits no error the user can act on.
- **User impact:** A new user on a current macOS with Cursor/VS Code data sees those sources never appear, with zero explanation of why or how to grant access. Worst case the whole index looks broken with no recoverable guidance.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Engram.entitlements:5; macos/Engram/Onboarding/OnboardingView.swift:173,178 (Library paths scanned, no access request); grep for 'Full Disk|TCC|System Settings|Privacy|NSOpenPanel' across Engram/Shared/EngramService returned no permission-guidance code
- **Suggested fix:** Add an onboarding step (or a Settings banner) that, when a Library-based source is detected but unreadable, links to System Settings > Privacy & Security > Full Disk Access with a short explanation; detect EPERM/ENOENT in the adapter scan and surface a permission hint instead of silently skipping.
- **Verify:** partial — The 'no permission UX anywhere' core claim is CONFIRMED: grep across Engram/Shared/EngramService for 'Full Disk|TCC|System Settings|System Preferences|x-apple.systempreferences|NSOpenPanel|requestAccess|grantAccess' returns ZERO matches (all 'permission' hits are POSIX file modes 0o600/0o700, os_log 'privacy: .private', or system-log access banners in Observability views — not TCC). Engram.entitlements declares no sandbox (confirmed lines 1-18). OnboardingView.swift:173,178 scans the Library paths with no access prompt, and the Swift PRODUCT adapters genuinely read them: CursorAdapter.swift:10 reads 'Library/Application Support/Cursor/User/globalStorage/state.vscdb' and VsCodeAdapter.swift:10 reads 'Library/Application Support/Code/User/workspaceStorage'. Failure is silent: VsCodeAdapter.detect() (line 18-20) returns false and listSessionLocators (line 22-36) returns [] with no surfaced error. HOWEVER the tracer's specific TCC mechanism is overstated: on modern macOS, FDA/App-Management gates ~/Library/Containers, Group Containers, the TCC db, and Mail/Safari/Messages — NOT a non-sandboxed process reading another non-sandboxed Electron app's (~/Library/Application Support/Cursor or /Code) data, which is normally plain-readable without FDA. So the cited prompt-gating trigger likely never fires for these exact paths. The UX gap (no guidance, silent failure) is real but the high-severity 'reads will be denied' premise is shaky; downgrade to medium.

#### `home-today-2` · 🟠 Medium · Continue / Follow-ups / Changed Repos panels truncate at 5 rows with no way to see the rest

- **Surface:** Today / Home landing page
- **What's wrong:** Each workbench panel caps visible rows at todayPanelRowLimit = 5 (Changed Repos at 5 via prefix(5)), and the panel header has no overflow affordance. SectionHeader already supports a trailingAction (a 'label + chevron.right' link) and an onRefresh button, but WorkbenchPanel only ever calls SectionHeader(icon:title:badge:) — it never passes trailingAction. So when a user has more than 5 recent sessions / follow-ups / changed repos, the extra items are silently dropped with no 'See all' entry point into the Sessions / Projects pages.
- **User impact:** A busy user with 12+ recent sessions sees only 5 on Today and has no in-panel link to the full Sessions/Follow-ups list. The landing page becomes a dead-end preview instead of a launch point into the deeper surfaces.
- **Evidence:** Row cap: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:7 (todayPanelRowLimit=5), :116 and :149 (prefix(todayPanelRowLimit)), :183 (prefix(5)). WorkbenchPanel header passes no trailingAction: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:360. SectionHeader supports trailingAction but it is unused here: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Components/SectionHeader.swift:9 and :36-46.
- **Suggested fix:** Pass trailingAction: ('See all', { post .navigateToScreen(.sessions) }) (and .projects for Changed Repos) into the WorkbenchPanel SectionHeader so each panel links to its full page when the row count exceeds the limit.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified accurate. Row caps: HomeView.swift:116 and :149 use prefix(todayPanelRowLimit) with todayPanelRowLimit=5 (:7); :183 uses prefix(5). WorkbenchPanel.body calls SectionHeader(icon:title:badge:) at :360 and never passes trailingAction. SectionHeader.swift declares trailingAction (:9) and renders it as a 'label + chevron.right' accent link (:36-46), but grep across the whole Engram tree shows trailingAction is referenced ONLY in SectionHeader.swift (definition + render) and is never supplied by any caller; no 'See all' string exists anywhere. The loader fetches more than is shown (recentSessions limit 12 via recentSessions(limit:12)+ranking to 8 at :257/:264-269; followUps limit 8 at :258), then truncates to 5 for display, and the badge itself caps at min(count,5) (:105,:138) so hidden rows aren't even advertised. Users with >5 recent/follow-ups get extra items silently dropped with no entry point into Sessions/Projects. Real workflow gap; medium stands.

#### `sessions-browse-2` · 🟠 Medium · Silent 200-session cap: list never paginates, so most sessions are unreachable while the KPI claims a higher total

- **Surface:** Browse sessions → filter → open
- **What's wrong:** loadData() calls db.listSessions(..., limit: 200) with no offset and there is no infinite-scroll, 'Load more' button, or onAppear-of-last-row trigger anywhere in SessionsPageView. The KPICard at the top shows totalCount from sessionListStats (an unbounded COUNT(*)), so the header can read e.g. '850 Total Sessions' while the LazyVStack only ever renders the 200 most-recently-updated. listSessions DOES support an offset parameter (Database.swift:171-201), so the backend is paginatable — the UI just never uses it.
- **User impact:** A user with more than 200 sessions can never reach sessions 201+ from the Sessions page by scrolling or any other gesture. The 'Total Sessions' KPI tells them more exist, but the list dead-ends silently with no indication it was truncated. Filtering by Today/Week can mask this, but for All Time on an active machine the bulk of history is simply invisible here.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:112-121 (limit: 200, no offset, no load-more); :142 totalCount = data.3.totalSessions (unbounded count shown in KPICard at :31); grep confirms no `offset`/`loadMore`/last-row onAppear in the file; backend support: macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift:179-180 `limit: Int = 200, offset: Int = 0`
- **Suggested fix:** Add cursor pagination: when the last row appears, increment offset by 200 and append; or render a 'Load more (N remaining)' footer when sessions.count < totalCount. Reuse the existing offset parameter on listSessions.
- **Verify:** confirmed — loadData() calls db.listSessions(..., limit: 200) with no offset (SessionsPageView.swift:113-121); listSessions does support pagination — signature has offset: Int = 0 (Database.swift:180) and the SQL appends 'LIMIT ? OFFSET ?' with args limit, offset (Database.swift:196-197), so the backend is paginatable and the UI never uses it. The KPICard shows totalCount = data.3.totalSessions from sessionListStats, an unbounded COUNT(*) (SessionsPageView.swift:122-128,142, displayed at :31). Grep of the whole file confirms NO offset / loadMore / 'Load more' / onAppear-last-row / prefix pagination trigger. Claim is factually accurate. I downgrade severity from high to medium: the list is sorted .updatedDesc (line 119), so the 200 rendered are the most-recently-updated (most relevant), and Source + time filters let a user narrow below 200. So 'most sessions unreachable' is overstated — the recency-sorted head plus filters mitigate it — but the count/list mismatch and the genuine inability to reach row 201+ within a fixed filter set is a real broken-workflow defect.

#### `memory-insights-3` · 🟠 Medium · Memory file viewer shows only a 200-char preview, never the full file

- **Surface:** Memory files + insights (save/retrieve/delete)
- **What's wrong:** When a user taps a memory file, the detail pane renders `selected.preview` (MemoryView.swift:49). That preview is built server-side as `content.prefixString(200)` — the first 200 characters only (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:185). EngramServiceMemoryFile carries no full-content field, so the app physically cannot show more than 200 chars. The list row also reuses the same truncated preview.
- **User impact:** A user opens a memory file expecting to read it, but only ever sees the first ~200 characters with no indication the rest is cut off and no way to view the full content. The core 'read my memory' journey cannot be completed in the app.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Pages/MemoryView.swift:49 (detail shows `selected.preview`); EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:185 (`preview: content.prefixString(200)`)
- **Suggested fix:** Add a full-content field to EngramServiceMemoryFile (or a memoryFileContent(path) read method) and render full text in the detail pane; or add an 'Open in Finder/editor' button using the existing `path` field as a fallback.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified. EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:185 builds preview as content.prefixString(200) — first 200 chars only. EngramServiceMemoryFile (EngramServiceModels.swift:569-576) carries only name/project/path/sizeBytes/preview — NO full-content field, so the app cannot request or render more than the 200-char preview. MemoryView.swift:49 detail pane renders Text(selected.preview) (textSelection enabled but still capped at 200 chars), and the list row at :65 uses file.preview.prefix(80). Both surfaces reuse the same truncated string; there is no 'open full file' / 'reveal in Finder' / fetch-full-content path in the view or DTO. Claim is accurate. Medium is appropriate: a genuine broken-workflow UX limitation (the viewer cannot show the actual file content), but lower blast radius than the missing insight surface and not data-loss/security.

#### `observability-4` · 🟠 Medium · The 'warn' log-level filter is a dead path; real warnings are misclassified as errors

- **Surface:** Observability: logs / errors / perf / traces / health
- **What's wrong:** LogStreamView exposes a 'warn' level in its filter picker (LogStreamView.swift:15) and LevelBadge renders an orange 'warn' badge (LogStreamView.swift:163). But OSLogReader.levelString() never returns 'warn' — it maps OSLogEntryLog.Level to only debug/info/error (OSLogReader.swift:30-40). macOS unified logging has no separate warning level: os_log .warning() calls (ServiceLogger.warn -> .warning at ServiceLogger.swift:41; EngramLogger.warn -> .warning at EngramLogger.swift:28) are stored at .error level. So selecting the 'warn' filter ALWAYS yields 0 rows, and every warning the code emits instead surfaces under the 'error' filter and inflates countErrors()/errorsByModule (OSLogReader.swift:101-110), polluting the Error dashboard's 'Errors (24h)' KPI and the Health tab's error count.
- **User impact:** A user filtering for 'warn' to triage warnings always sees an empty list (broken filter), while genuine warnings masquerade as errors in the Error dashboard KPI and Health status — making the system look less healthy (or hiding real errors among warnings) than it is.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Core/OSLogReader.swift:30-40 (no 'warn' case; .error/.fault->error); 'warn' filter offered at macos/Engram/Views/Observability/LogStreamView.swift:15; warn emitted as .warning at macos/EngramService/Core/ServiceLogger.swift:41 and EngramLogger.swift:28; error counts at OSLogReader.swift:101-110
- **Suggested fix:** Drop the 'warn' filter option (and warn badge) since the unified log can't distinguish it, OR explicitly tag warning messages with a marker the reader can detect and re-bucket them; at minimum exclude warning-origin entries from the error count to stop inflating the Error KPI.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified OSLogReader.levelString (OSLogReader.swift:30-40) maps OSLogEntryLog.Level to only debug/info/error: .debug→debug, .info/.notice/.undefined/@unknown→info, .error/.fault→error. There is NO 'warn' case, so recentLogs(level:'warn') filters (line 76 'if level != All && lvl != level continue') against a value levelString never produces → always 0 rows. The picker offers 'warn' (LogStreamView.swift:15) and LevelBadge renders an orange 'warn' (LogStreamView.swift:163-166), so the filter is a visible dead path. ServiceLogger.warn→.warning (ServiceLogger.swift:41) and EngramLogger.warn→.warning (EngramLogger.swift:28); macOS unified logging stores .warning at the error log type, which levelString maps to 'error' (line 35), so warnings inflate countErrors (OSLogReader.swift:101-103) and errorsByModule (:106-110), polluting the Error dashboard 'Errors (24h)' KPI (ErrorDashboardView.swift:28) and SystemHealthView's errorCount24h (SystemHealthView.swift:48,97). All sub-claims verified. Medium severity appropriate.

#### `hygiene-6` · 🟡 Low · Bulk-hide has no confirmation and no undo path

- **Surface:** Hygiene / cleanup workflow
- **What's wrong:** If hideEmptySessions() were ever wired to a button, the backend bulk-updates hidden_at across potentially many sessions in one write with no transactional undo token and no per-session record beyond hidden_at. There is no service command to bulk-unhide, and the app has no 'restore last cleanup' affordance. Combined with finding hygiene-5 (no per-session unhide in UI), a bulk-hide would be effectively irreversible from the app. This is the 'destructive action without confirmation/undo' risk the review flags, latent in the backend design.
- **User impact:** Were the cleanup button added as-is, a user clicking it could hide dozens of sessions instantly with no confirmation dialog and no one-click way to get them back — exactly the kind of irreversible destructive action the audit warns about.
- **Evidence:** hideEmptySessions performs a single bulk UPDATE with only a hiddenCount return and no undo token: EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:686-698. No bulk-unhide command exists (grep for unhide/hidden:false bulk path returns nothing in the service handler). App has no unhide UI (see hygiene-5).
- **Suggested fix:** Before exposing bulk-hide, add a confirmation dialog showing the count to be hidden, and either return the affected session ids for a session-scoped undo or add a bulk-unhide command so the cleanup is reversible.
- **Verify:** partial — Factually accurate but conditional/latent, which the tracer's own 'latent in the backend design' wording acknowledges. hideEmptySessions (EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:686-698) is a single bulk UPDATE returning only hiddenCount, no undo token, no per-session pre-state snapshot beyond hidden_at. Grep confirms no bulk-unhide command in ./EngramService (only the per-session setSessionHidden with hidden:false and read-filter clauses at :1255 etc.). App has no unhide UI (hygiene-5). HOWEVER: (a) hideEmptySessions is unwired (hygiene-3), so no destructive action can currently be triggered from the app — the risk is purely hypothetical pending wiring; (b) unhide IS technically reversible at the data layer since hidden_at is set, not deleted, and setSessionHidden(hidden:false) exists in the service — so 'effectively irreversible from the app' is true only because the app lacks any unhide button, not because data is lost. This is a real but not-yet-live design caveat, so partial. Medium severity is if anything slightly high for a latent/unwired risk; keeping medium is defensible but it is the weakest of the six.

#### `menubar-popover-5` · 🟡 Low · Deep-link to a session on a fresh window relies on fragile post-ordering

- **Surface:** Menu bar popover + live sessions
- **What's wrong:** Opening a session from the popover (double-click row → .openWindow with SessionBox) is handled by handleOpenWindow: it calls openWindow() then, inside a Task { @MainActor }, posts .openSession (MenuBarController.swift:224-232). On a first-ever open, openWindow() synchronously constructs NSHostingController(rootView: MainWindowView()) and makeKeyAndOrderFront (MenuBarController.swift:252-285); the .onReceive(.openSession) subscriber in MainWindowView (MainWindowView.swift:45-50) only becomes active after SwiftUI installs the view. The .openSession post is enqueued on the next main-actor hop with no guarantee the subscriber is registered yet — if it isn't, the notification is dropped and the window opens on Home instead of the requested session. No test covers this fresh-window deep-link (grep of EngramTests/EngramServiceCoreTests finds no openSession/handleOpenWindow coverage). When the window already exists the path is reliable; the risk is specifically the cold-open case.
- **User impact:** First time a user double-clicks a popover row after launch (window not yet created), the app may open the main window but land on Home rather than the session they clicked, forcing them to find it again. Intermittent and confusing because subsequent clicks (window already open) work.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/MenuBarController.swift:224-232 (post .openSession in Task after openWindow); macos/Engram/MenuBarController.swift:252-285 (fresh window construction); macos/Engram/Views/MainWindowView.swift:45-50 (onReceive subscriber installed with the view); no covering test found
- **Suggested fix:** Pass the target session into MainWindowView at construction (e.g. an initial selectedSession parameter) for the cold-open path instead of relying on a post-creation NotificationCenter post, or retry/delay the .openSession post until the window's content is confirmed installed.
- **Verify:** confirmed — handleOpenWindow (MenuBarController.swift:224-232) calls openWindow() then posts .openSession inside Task { @MainActor }. Fresh-window path at 252-285 builds NSHostingController(rootView: MainWindowView()) and makeKeyAndOrderFront synchronously. The .onReceive(.openSession) subscriber is installed with the view at MainWindowView.swift:45-50. No test covers this ordering: grep of EngramTests/EngramServiceCoreTests shows coverage only for liveSessions() IPC (EngramServiceClientTests.swift:125, EngramServiceIPCTests.swift:1177/2632) and LiveSessionCard.elapsedText (ViewMainThreadReadTests.swift:166-173); none exercise handleOpenWindow/openSession cold-open. The ordering dependency and test gap are real. Downgraded medium->low: makeKeyAndOrderFront synchronously drives SwiftUI view installation (and thus onReceive registration) on the same main-actor turn before the enqueued Task block runs, so in practice the subscriber is normally registered first — this is a latent timing fragility, not a demonstrated break, and the warm-window path (the common case) is reliable.

#### `xc-deadends-8` · 🟡 Low · Hygiene diagnoses issues but offers only a 'Copy command' — no in-app remediation

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** HygieneView detects data-health issues and, for each, shows a suggested action string with a single 'Copy' button that puts the command on the clipboard. There is no in-app fix/apply action; the user must paste the command into a terminal elsewhere. Combined with the missing hide/unhide UI (xc-deadends-3), the hygiene 'fix' loop cannot be completed inside the app.
- **User impact:** Users see a list of problems and a copyable command but cannot resolve anything from the GUI, so Hygiene is an advisory island that always sends the user to the command line to actually act.
- **Evidence:** IssueCard renders action text + Copy-to-pasteboard only — macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HygieneView.swift:316-340 (NSPasteboard.general.setString(action)). No serviceClient call to remediate; the only service call is serviceClient.hygiene(force:) to re-scan (:189).
- **Suggested fix:** For issue kinds with a safe service-side fix, add an 'Apply' button wired to the corresponding service command; keep Copy as the fallback for manual-only actions.

### Island features (built but disconnected) (14)

#### `session-actions-4` · 🔴 High · Favorites are a write-only dead-end — nowhere to view starred sessions

- **Surface:** Session actions: favorite / hide / rename / export / resume
- **What's wrong:** The favorite toggle (star) in TranscriptToolbar.swift:55-62 works end-to-end: it calls serviceClient.setFavorite (SessionDetailView.swift:168-180) and the load path reads back isFavorite (SessionDetailView.swift:442). But there is no way to ever USE a favorite: Database.listFavorites() (Database.swift:627) has zero callers anywhere in the app, Screen.swift (lines 6-25) has no .favorites screen, SidebarView contains no Favorites entry, and no list view filters by favorite. The star is only re-discoverable by reopening that exact session.
- **User impact:** Starring a session feels like bookmarking, but the user can never browse or filter their favorites. The action silently goes nowhere useful — a classic island feature: data is written but has no surface that reads it.
- **Evidence:** TranscriptToolbar.swift:55-62 (star button); SessionDetailView.swift:168-180,442 (setFavorite/isFavorite); Database.swift:627 listFavorites() with grep = 0 callers; Screen.swift:6-25 (no favorites case); SidebarView grep for favorite = 0 hits
- **Suggested fix:** Add a Favorites screen (new Screen case + sidebar entry) backed by the existing Database.listFavorites(), or add a 'Favorites only' filter to SessionsPageView/SearchPageView. The read query already exists; only a UI surface is missing.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Star toggle works end-to-end: TranscriptToolbar.swift:55-62 renders it, SessionDetailView.swift:168-180 calls serviceClient.setFavorite, and SessionDetailView.swift:442 reads back isFavorite via Database.isFavorite. But Database.listFavorites() (Database.swift:627) has zero callers anywhere in Engram/ or Shared/. Screen.swift enumerates 16 cases (lines 6-25) with no .favorites; Section.screens (lines 99-106) never lists a favorites screen, so SidebarView cannot render one. No list view filters by favorite. A favorited session is only re-discoverable by reopening it. Confirmed write-only dead-end; severity high is justified given the toggle is prominent yet the data is unusable.

#### `agents-grouping-1` · 🔴 High · The dedicated "Agents" screen is a read-only flat list with no grouping or suggestion-review affordances

- **Surface:** Agent sessions + parent/child link management
- **What's wrong:** AgentsView is the screen a user would naturally open to manage agent sessions and their parent/child links (top-level CONFIG nav item, routed at MainWindowView.swift:107). But it renders each agent session with the plain SessionCard, which has no disclosure triangle, no child grouping, and no Confirm/Dismiss/Unlink controls. It calls listSessions(subAgent: true) (returns the subagent/dispatched sessions themselves), tapping a card only posts .openSession. None of the grouping callbacks (onConfirmSuggestion / onDismissSuggestion) the ExpandableSessionCard component supports are wired here. So the one screen literally named "Agents" exposes zero of the Layer-2 grouping intelligence — the suggested_parent_id review/confirm flow that DOES exist elsewhere is completely absent from the page built for agents.
- **User impact:** A user clicks the prominent "Agents" sidebar item expecting to review and manage which sessions are grouped under which parent, but gets a flat, ungrouped list of subagent sessions with no way to confirm/reject any suggested grouping or relink anything. The grouping feature feels broken/absent on the exact page named for it.
- **Evidence:** AgentsView.swift:34 uses SessionCard(session:) (not ExpandableSessionCard); AgentsView.swift:54 calls listSessions(subAgent: true); SessionCard.swift:10-40 has only session+onTap, no confirm/dismiss/expand; Screen.swift:21,104 + MainWindowView.swift:106-107 make .agents a reachable top-level destination; ExpandableSessionCard.swift:34-35,172-184 shows the confirm/dismiss callbacks that AgentsView never passes.
- **Suggested fix:** Have AgentsView list top-level parent sessions (or sessions with pending suggestions) using ExpandableSessionCard and wire onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion to serviceClient.confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion, mirroring SessionsPageView.swift:67-79,153-176. Reuse the existing wiring; this is a small adoption, not new backend.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified AgentsView.swift directly. Line 34 uses SessionCard(session:) with only an onTap closure that posts .openSession (line 35); line 54 calls db.listSessions(subAgent: true, limit: 200). SessionCard (SessionCard.swift:9-12) has only `session` + optional `onTap` — no disclosure triangle, no child grouping, no confirm/dismiss callbacks. The grouping component ExpandableSessionCard does expose onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion (ExpandableSessionCard.swift:34-35, wired at 181-182), but AgentsView never constructs it. Routing confirmed: Screen.swift:21 defines .agents, Screen.swift:104 puts it in the CONFIG nav group, MainWindowView.swift:106-107 routes .agents -> AgentsView(). So the screen literally named 'Agents' renders a flat read-only list with zero Layer-2 grouping/review affordances. Severity high is appropriate: this is the natural management destination yet exposes none of the parent/child intelligence.

#### `hooks-config-1` · 🔴 High · Hooks page is a pure read-only list with zero next actions

- **Surface:** Hooks page
- **What's wrong:** HooksView renders every hook as a static row (event capsule + monospaced command text + Spacer) with no Button, onTapGesture, contextMenu, or any interactive element. - **User impact:** The user opens the Hooks tab, sees their Claude Code hooks, and then is stuck — to actually change or even locate a hook they must leave the app, remember it lives in ~/.claude/settings.json, and open it manually in another editor. The feature looks like a hook manager but is only a viewer.
