No disable/test/toggle/enable hook symbol exists anywhere: grep over Engram/, EngramService/, Shared/ for disableHook/testHook/toggleHook/enableHook returned zero matches.
- **Suggested fix:** Add at minimum an 'Open settings.json' button per scope (the app already uses NSWorkspace.shared.open in 4+ places, e.g. GeneralSettingsSection.swift:66 and PopoverView.swift:123). Best: make each hookRow open/reveal its source settings file. This is the smallest change that turns the dead-end list into the start of an edit workflow.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified HooksView.swift:36-54 — hookRow is an HStack of Text(event capsule)+Text(command)+Spacer ending in .padding/.background/.overlay/.clipShape with NO action modifier. Grep of HooksView.swift for contextMenu|onTapGesture|.copy|NSPasteboard|NSWorkspace|openURL|Button returned empty. ForEach at lines 19/23 calls hookRow with no tap handler. Whole-tree grep for disableHook|testHook|toggleHook|enableHook|deleteHook|editHook returned zero matches across Engram/Shared/EngramService. The client protocol (EngramServiceProtocol.swift:3-41) exposes only read-only hooks() — no hook mutation method exists anywhere. Hook is referenced only in HooksView, Screen.swift (nav case), and MainWindowView.swift:111 — no command palette or alternate action surface exists. Severity stays high and is reinforced: MemoryView.swift:39,61 shows sibling config pages DO have interactive Button rows opening a detail view, so the static read-only hooks list is an inconsistency with an established codebase pattern, not a platform limitation. The 'isolated island' claim is fully substantiated.

#### `memory-insights-2` · 🟠 Medium · DB insights table is invisible in the app — MemoryView shows only filesystem .md files

- **Surface:** Memory files + insights (save/retrieve/delete)
- **What's wrong:** MemoryView is titled/treated as the app's 'Memory' surface but it exclusively lists filesystem markdown files under ~/.claude/projects/*/memory/*.md (EngramServiceReadProvider.memoryFiles, EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:160-193 — only `.md` files in each project's `memory/` dir). The curated DB insights written via save_insight (the insights / memory_insights tables, exposed by MCP get_insights at MCPToolRegistry.swift:324,852) are never read or displayed by any app view. There is no getInsights/get_insights consumer in the Engram/ target at all.
- **User impact:** An insight a user (via an agent) saved through save_insight never appears in the app's Memory page. The user sees a different, unrelated set of data (Claude Code per-project memory markdown) than the insights the rest of the product (MCP get_memory/get_insights) treats as 'memory'. The two halves of 'memory' are disconnected, so the Memory page misrepresents what the product actually remembers.
- **Evidence:** EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:160-193 (memoryFiles scans only `.md` under `/memory/`); MCPToolRegistry.swift:324,852 (get_insights exists for MCP only); grep get_insights/getInsights under macos/Engram/ = 0 hits; MemoryView.swift:6,93 loads only `memoryFiles()`
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) add a service read method to list DB insights and show them in MemoryView (a second section alongside filesystem memory files), or (b) rename/scope the page to 'Project Memory Files' to stop implying it shows saved insights. Option (a) is needed for end-to-end save→view parity with finding memory-insights-1.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified. EngramServiceReadProvider.memoryFiles() (:160-193) scans only ~/.claude/projects/*/memory/ and appends only files where pathExtension == 'md' — purely filesystem markdown, no DB query. MemoryView.swift:6,93 loads exclusively via serviceClient.memoryFiles(); it never reads the insights/memory_insights tables. get_insights exists only for MCP (MCPToolRegistry.swift:324 tool def, :852 handler, :1085 registry list); grep for getInsights/get_insights/memory_insights/'FROM insights' across Engram/ returned zero non-localization hits. EngramCoreRead only names the insight tables in SchemaManifest.swift:27-29,37 (schema-validation string list), exposing no insight read repository to the app. The curated DB insights are genuinely invisible in the app UI. Claim is accurate. I lower severity from high to medium because this is the read-side facet of the same root cause as memory-insights-1 (no insight UI at all); counting both as independent high double-weights one architectural gap. It remains a distinct, real issue (read surface vs write surface) and stays confirmed.

#### `skills-config-1` · 🟠 Medium · Skills page is a read-only informational dead-end — rows do nothing

- **Surface:** Skills page
- **What's wrong:** Every skill row is rendered as a plain VStack of Text (name, description, path) with no Button, onTapGesture, contextMenu, or link. There is no way to open the skill's file, reveal it in Finder, enable/disable it, or run it. The page surfaces a real on-disk path per row but offers zero affordance to act on it, so the user's journey ends at 'I can see a list and that's all.' The product owner's 'isolated island' concern is literally true here: it is a viewer with no exits.
- **User impact:** A user browsing their Claude skills/commands sees names, descriptions, and a file path, but clicking a row does nothing. To actually view or edit a skill they must manually copy the printed ~/... path and open it in a separate app. The page feels broken/incomplete relative to sibling pages (Repos, Source Pulse) where a path reveals in Finder.
- **Evidence:** skillRow renders only Text views with no interaction: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SkillsView.swift:51-64 (lines 53 name, 55 description, 57 path — all Text; the enclosing VStack has no .onTapGesture/.contextMenu/Button). Compare the established in-product affordance that reveals a path in Finder, unused here: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Workspace/RepoDetailView.swift:69 (NSWorkspace.shared.selectFile) and /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SourcePulseView.swift:181 (NSWorkspace.shared.selectFile). The path shown is a real ~-expanded filesystem location: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:284-289 (displayPath).
- **Suggested fix:** Add the smallest affordance already used elsewhere: make each row a Button (or add a .contextMenu) whose action expands the ~ path (NSString(string: skill.path).expandingTildeInPath) and calls NSWorkspace.shared.selectFile(expanded, inFileViewerRootedAtPath: ""), mirroring SourcePulseView.swift:181. No new backend command is required.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified the core claim is correct. SkillsView.swift:51-64 skillRow is a VStack of three Text views only (name :53, description :55, path :57) wrapped in padding/background/overlay/clipShape; grep for contextMenu|onTapGesture|NSWorkspace|selectFile|Button|sheet|popover|.open( inside the file returned exit 1 (zero matches). No action exists elsewhere: skillRow appears only in this file; there are no openSkill/revealSkill/runSkill symbols anywhere in Engram or Shared; the service surface is read-only (EngramServiceClient.swift:45 skills() -> [EngramServiceSkillInfo], EngramServiceProtocol.swift:9). The model EngramServiceSkillInfo (EngramServiceModels.swift:561-567) carries only name/description/path/scope with no enable/disable state, so even an enable/disable toggle has no backing field. MainWindowView.swift:104-105 renders a bare SkillsView() with no wrapping context menu or sheet. The cited reveal-in-Finder pattern is real and unused here: RepoDetailView.swift:69 and SourcePulseView.swift use NSWorkspace.shared.selectFile while SkillsView, which shows a real ~-expanded path, does not. The page is a genuine read-only dead-end. Downgrading high->medium: this is a small ancillary surface and sibling list pages (MemoryView, HooksView, AgentsView) share the same read-only no-affordance pattern, so it is not a unique regression; the practical low-cost fix is reveal-in-Finder/open-file (a pattern the product already has), while true run-the-skill is a Claude Code harness action the app cannot directly invoke. The gap is real but its impact does not rise to high.

#### `settings-ai-3` · 🟠 Medium · 'Embeddings' status row on HomeView and the Popover Embedding dot are wired to a value that is never set — permanently dead/misleading surfaces for a non-existent capability

- **Surface:** Settings: AI / embeddings / generation
- **What's wrong:** HomeView shows an 'Embeddings' service-state row and PopoverView shows an 'Embedding' status dot, both driven by EngramServiceStatusStore.embeddingStatus (a String?). That property is declared but never assigned anywhere in production code (only mock/test references exist). So HomeView's row permanently shows the fallback 'Check Advanced diagnostics' and the Popover dot stays the hollow grey nil-state forever. Combined with the fact that the product is keyword-only (SearchSupport.swift:9-11 hardcodes availableModes to [.keyword] regardless of embeddingAvailable, and CLAUDE.md states sqlite-vec is not implemented), these surfaces advertise an 'Embeddings' capability the product does not have and cannot ever report as active.
- **User impact:** The menu-bar popover and Home dashboard both display an 'Embedding(s)' status that never changes and never reflects anything real, implying the app does semantic/embedding work it does not. Users may believe embeddings/semantic search are running (or merely 'unavailable, fixable') when the capability simply does not exist in the product.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:225-230 ('Embeddings' row bound to serviceStatusStore.embeddingStatus); macos/Engram/Views/PopoverView.swift:66-73 (Embedding dot branches on serviceStatusStore.embeddingStatus); macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:37 (var embeddingStatus: String? — grep shows no production assignment); macos/Engram/Views/SearchSupport.swift:9-11 (availableModes always returns [.keyword]); the SearchPageView embedded-count badge at SearchPageView.swift:160-167 only renders when status.available, which embeddingStatus() returns false for whenever the session_embeddings table is absent (the normal product state, EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:679-687)
- **Suggested fix:** Either remove the Embeddings row/dot until a real embedding path ships (consistent with the already-removed inert embedding settings controls, AISettingsSection.swift:13-18), or have them honestly render 'Not supported' rather than a dead status bound to a never-populated field.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Two distinct surfaces, both verified dead/misleading. (1) EngramServiceStatusStore.embeddingStatus:String? (line 37) is NEVER assigned in production: none of the three apply() methods (event/status/refreshUsage, lines 64-111) set it, and a repo-wide grep for assignments found only mock/test references (MockEngramServiceClient is a different EngramServiceEmbeddingStatusResponse property, not the store String). So PopoverView.swift:66-76 embeddingStatusView stays the hollow grey nil branch forever, and HomeView.swift:225-230 permanently shows the 'Check Advanced diagnostics' fallback — and that fallback text points to a destination that doesn't exist (the only 'Advanced diagnostics' string in the app is that fallback literal at HomeView.swift:228). (2) The separate live path: SearchPageView's local @State embeddingStatus is fed by serviceClient.embeddingStatus() (SearchPageView.swift:481), whose backend EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:676-696 returns available:false whenever session_embeddings is absent (lines 679-681) — the normal product state since no Swift writer populates it — so the embedded-count badge gated on status.available (SearchPageView.swift:160) never renders. SearchSupport.swift:9-11 hardcodes availableModes to [.keyword] regardless of embeddingAvailable, and CLAUDE.md states sqlite-vec is not implemented. All claim points verified. Confirmed. Lowering severity from the tracer's framing to medium: these are misleading/dead status surfaces (no incorrect data is acted upon, no data loss) consistent with the existing AISettingsSection note that the Embeddings controls were already removed as a 'false UI promise' — same defect class, cosmetic-but-misleading rather than high-impact.

#### `usage-cost-3` · 🟠 Medium · Usage-pressure notification is non-actionable and cannot be acted on or deep-linked

- **Surface:** Usage / cost tracking
- **What's wrong:** UsagePressureNotifier posts a UNUserNotificationContent with title/body only (UsagePressureNotifier.swift:74-86): trigger is nil and no UNNotificationAction/category is attached. Tapping the notification does nothing beyond default app-foreground behavior; there is no action to open the usage view, snooze, raise the limit, or jump to settings. The only place a user can then see/manage usage is the menu-bar popover's USAGE section or Settings > Usage Limits — neither is reachable from the notification.
- **User impact:** When a user gets an 'Engram usage critical' notification, they are told there is a problem but given no way to act on it from the alert. They must independently remember to open the menu-bar popover or settings. The alerting half of the feature is disconnected from the management half.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/UsagePressureNotifier.swift:74-87 (content has no actions, trigger: nil, no category registered); no UNUserNotificationCenter delegate handling taps found; the actionable surfaces are PopoverView (PopoverView.swift:23) and SettingsView Usage Limits (SettingsView.swift:347-376), neither linked from the notification
- **Suggested fix:** Attach a UNNotificationAction (e.g. 'View Usage') and a delegate that opens the popover or a usage view on tap. Even just opening the main window to SourcePulseView would close the loop.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified UsagePressureNotifier.swift:74-86 builds a UNMutableNotificationContent with only title/body/sound, trigger:nil, and no categoryIdentifier. Grep for UNNotificationAction|UNNotificationCategory|setNotificationCategories|UNUserNotificationCenterDelegate|didReceive|userNotificationCenter across Engram+Shared returns ZERO hits, so no actions/category are registered and no delegate handles taps — a tap yields only default app-foreground behavior. The notifier IS wired and fires (MenuBarController.swift:17,78,349 call usagePressureNotifier.observe with serviceStatusStore.usagePressureSummary). The .openSettings NotificationCenter name exists (AppNotifications.swift:4) and PopoverView.swift:42 can post it, but that is in-app SwiftUI navigation, not connected to any OS-notification tap. So the notification is genuinely non-actionable / not deep-linkable. Severity medium is appropriate: the feature fires correctly; the gap is missing actionability/deep-link polish, not a broken core capability.

#### `command-palette-4` · 🟠 Medium · Palette session results are a dead end — can navigate to a session but cannot act on it

- **Surface:** Command palette
- **What's wrong:** When a user searches sessions in the palette, each hit's only action is `onSelectSession(hit.id)` → `navigateToSession` which opens the SessionDetailView (CommandPaletteView.swift:36-38, MainWindowView.swift:63-66,121-141). There is no secondary action available on a palette result: no 'Resume', no 'Export', no 'Hide/Skip', no 'Copy link', no 'Open in new context' — all of which the GUI session card / detail view expose (ExpandableSessionCard.swift, SessionDetailView.swift, TranscriptToolbar.swift). The palette therefore surfaces sessions but offers strictly less than the session list/cards a click away, so it is a quick-jump island rather than a true action hub.
- **User impact:** A user who finds the right session in ⌘K still cannot do anything to it from there (e.g. resume it in a terminal, export it) — they must navigate in, then locate the action. The palette adds a hop instead of removing one for any task beyond 'read this session'.
- **Evidence:** CommandPaletteView.swift:35-40 (only action is onSelectSession); MainWindowView.swift:63-66 + 121-141 (onSelectSession just opens detail). Compare GUI session affordances: ExpandableSessionCard.swift, SessionDetailView.swift, TranscriptToolbar.swift (export/resume), ResumeDialog.swift.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a right-side action hint and a modifier-key path on selected session rows (e.g. ⌘↩ = Resume, ⌥↩ = Export) wiring to the existing resume/export code paths, so the palette can complete a real session action end-to-end.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified directly. CommandPaletteView.swift:34-39 builds session rows whose only closure is onSelectSession(hit.id); MainWindowView.swift:58-67 wires onSelectSession to navigateToSession(id:) (MainWindowView.swift:121-141) which loads the session and sets selectedSession (opens detail). No secondary action is attached to a palette session row, and the palette only handles upArrow/downArrow/escape key presses (CommandPaletteView.swift:167-178) with no modifier/right-arrow/tab secondary-action handling. By contrast the GUI session card exposes richer affordances: ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-127 has a .contextMenu with Resume.../Copy Resume Command/Handoff/Replay. So the palette result is strictly a navigate-only jump that offers less than the card/detail view it lands on. Claim accurate; medium severity retained (navigate-only is a reasonable palette default; lack of inline session actions is a real but non-blocking enhancement gap since the same actions are one click away on the resulting card/detail view).

#### `home-today-5` · 🟡 Low · Changed Repos warning badges (Migrated / N changed / N unpushed) are signals with no matching action

- **Surface:** Today / Home landing page
- **What's wrong:** TodayProjectWarning computes a per-repo warning from live GitRepo dirty/untracked/unpushed counts and committed project migrations, surfaced as an orange 'Migrated' or 'N changed · N unpushed' badge in each ChangedRepoRow. But tapping the row only opens the first session's transcript (group.sessions.first -> open). There is no path from the warning to the Repos page, the project's git state, or the project migration history that produced the 'Migrated' flag, so the warning raises a concern the user cannot act on from here.
- **User impact:** A user sees 'myproj — 3 changed · 2 unpushed' or 'Migrated' on Today, wants to act on it (review uncommitted work, inspect the migration), clicks the row, and instead lands in an unrelated transcript with no way to reach the repo or migration detail.
- **Evidence:** Warning computed from real repo/migration data: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/TodayWorkbenchSupport.swift:121-165. Badge rendered as text only: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:478-481. Row tap opens first session, not repo/migration view: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:184-192 and ChangedRepoRow onOpen :459-461.
- **Suggested fix:** Route a warning tap (or add a trailing affordance) to the Repos page / project migration review for that project, instead of opening the first transcript; at minimum make the badge itself a link to the relevant detail surface.

#### `timeline-4` · 🟡 Low · Per-project timeline backend capability has no Timeline-page entry point

- **Surface:** Timeline page
- **What's wrong:** Two project-scoped timeline capabilities exist in the backend but the Timeline page exposes neither. The Timeline page shows only an all-projects, all-sources flat feed with no way to filter to a single project or source, so the project dimension of the backend is invisible from this surface.

MCP-only capability: macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPDatabase.swift:355 (project/since/until). TimelinePageView.swift has no project/source filter (grep for project/source/Filter in the file finds none).
- **Suggested fix:** Either add a project/source FilterPills row to TimelinePageView that calls a parameterized timeline query, or, if intentionally unused, flag `Database.projectTimeline(project:)`/`TimelineEntry` as dead app code (do not delete pre-existing orphans without owner sign-off).

#### `xc-deadends-7` · 🟡 Low · Workspace/Sources rows and live-session cards are non-interactive dead-ends

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** Several list rows display rich data but cannot be acted on or drilled into, unlike SessionCards which open a detail view. WorkGraphRow (repo activity) has no tap/Button. SourcePulseView's per-source rows have no tap to, e.g., filter sessions by that source. LiveSessionCard (the live-sessions list on the Sources page) has no onTapGesture/Button, so clicking an in-progress session does nothing — you cannot jump from a live session to its transcript.
- **User impact:** These pages read as dashboards you cannot navigate from: a user who sees an active repo, a high-volume source, or a live session has no way to click through to the underlying sessions, so the data is a visual island with no exit.
- **Evidence:** WorkGraphRow has no gesture/Button — macos/Engram/Views/Workspace/WorkGraphView.swift:103-153 (only accessibility, no onTap). SourcePulseView source rows are plain VStacks with no action — macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SourcePulseView.swift:78-124. LiveSessionCard body ends with styling + .onAppear only, no tap — macos/Engram/Components/LiveSessionCard.swift:41-103.
- **Suggested fix:** Make these rows tappable: post .openSession from LiveSessionCard, and have WorkGraphRow / source rows navigate to a filtered Sessions view (by repo / by source).
- **Verify:** partial — All three non-interactivity claims are factually confirmed: (1) WorkGraphRow (WorkGraphView.swift:103-153) has no Button/onTapGesture/onTap/NotificationCenter — grep returns 0 matches; only accessibility labels (:150-152). (2) SourcePulseView source rows (SourcePulseView.swift:80-122) are plain VStacks with styling and no tap action. (3) LiveSessionCard.swift:40-103 body ends with styling + .onAppear only, no tap, and the call site SourcePulseView.swift:200 passes no closure. So these rows do display rich data and are non-interactive. HOWEVER 'dead-end' overstates it — these are read-only dashboard/status widgets (repo activity bars, per-source health stats, live in-progress session pulse), not actions advertised as clickable that fail. They have no chevron, no button styling, no hover affordance suggesting interactivity, unlike SessionCard which visibly signals tappability. The LiveSessionCard case is weaker still: it renders EngramServiceLiveSessionInfo (a live, possibly-not-yet-indexed session) for which 'jump to transcript' may not be feasible. This is a discoverability/feature-completeness suggestion (could-be-clickable rows), not a broken or inert control. Downgrading medium->low: nothing here is wired-but-dead; it's simply not wired, and the rows don't claim to be.

### Backend-capability ↔ UI gaps (shipped backend, no UI entry) (43)

#### `onboarding-firstrun-4` · 🔴 High · No user-facing service recovery action when EngramService fails to start

- **Surface:** First run / onboarding / zero-state
- **What's wrong:** On launch, if serviceLauncher.start throws or the health monitor exhausts its 3-restart budget, the status store goes .error/.degraded (App.swift:147-150; EngramServiceLauncher.swift:229-237). The only surfacing is a menu-bar warning triangle with a tooltip (MenuBarController.swift:356-385) and a 'Degraded: …'/'Error: …' string in HomeView's status pill/Service State panel. There is NO UI control anywhere to restart/retry the service: serviceLauncher is referenced only in App.swift (grep shows EngramServiceLauncher used only in App.swift and its own file), and no 'Restart'/'Retry'/'Relaunch service' action exists in Settings (only a LaunchAgent login-item toggle at GeneralSettingsSection.swift:93-94).
- **User impact:** If the service is wedged on first run (helper missing, socket/lock contention, denied runtime dir), the user is left with a warning triangle and an error string but no button to recover — their only option is to quit and relaunch the whole app, which they may not know to do.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/App.swift:147-150,127-146; macos/Engram/Core/EngramServiceLauncher.swift:229-237; macos/Engram/MenuBarController.swift:356-385; grep 'serviceLauncher|restartService|Restart' found no user-facing restart control (only LaunchAgent toggle in GeneralSettingsSection.swift:93)
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Restart service' button to the HomeView Service State panel and/or the menu/Settings that calls into EngramServiceLauncher (stop + start), shown when status is .error/.degraded.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. serviceLauncher is referenced only in App.swift (declaration :74, init :87, start :131, startHealthMonitor :138, stopIfOwned :206) and a static secrets-writer in AISettingsSection.swift:316-317 (unrelated to restart). The health monitor auto-restarts up to a budget then emits .degraded and keeps polling (EngramServiceLauncher.swift:212-237). The only surfacing is the menu-bar warning triangle which is image+tooltip ONLY, no action (MenuBarController.updateStatusIndicator :356-385, sets btn.image/btn.toolTip), plus the HomeView status pill/Service State strings. The menu-bar NSMenu contains only Open Window / Open Web UI / Settings / Quit (MenuBarController.swift:149-167) — no Restart Service item. Settings 'Launch' GroupBox has only 'Launch at Login' + 'Show Dock Icon' toggles (GeneralSettingsSection.swift:91-104). grep for restart/relaunch/retry user controls finds only project-move/undo 'Retry' buttons (UndoSheet/ArchiveSheet/RenameSheet) and a static error string 'Restart Engram to recover' (ProjectMoveServiceError.swift:5) — none restart the service. No user-facing recovery action exists; high severity stands.

#### `session-actions-3` · 🔴 High · Export session: full export service exists but no in-app button

- **Surface:** Session actions: favorite / hide / rename / export / resume
- **What's wrong:** TranscriptExportService.exportSession is a complete feature: it writes Markdown or JSON to ~/.engram/exports/<source>-<id>-<date>.<ext>, redacts secrets, sets 0600 perms, and returns the output path (TranscriptExportService.swift:7-56). It is wired through the client (EngramServiceClient.swift:193), service handler (EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:339-344), the MCP 'export' tool (MCPToolRegistry.swift:422,888), and the web server. But there is NO export button anywhere in the SwiftUI app: the detail toolbar exposes Copy/Handoff/Replay/Resume only (TranscriptToolbar.swift), and no context menu calls exportSession (grep under Engram/ = 0). The only file-producing affordance in the app is 'Copy' to clipboard (SessionDetailView.copyAllTranscript).
- **User impact:** A user who wants a Markdown/JSON file of a session must use the MCP tool from an AI client; the desktop app gives them only clipboard copy. The shipped, redaction-aware export feature is completely hidden from app users, and even if exposed elsewhere the output path is never revealed in Finder.
- **Evidence:** TranscriptExportService.swift:7-56 (full export to ~/.engram/exports, returns outputPath); EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:339-344 + EngramServiceClient.swift:193 (wired); MCPToolRegistry.swift:422,888 (MCP 'export' tool); grep exportSession under Engram/ = 0 view callers; TranscriptToolbar.swift:23-32 (no export action)
- **Suggested fix:** Add an 'Export…' action to the detail toolbar/context menu that calls serviceClient.exportSession, then show the returned outputPath and offer NSWorkspace.activateFileViewerSelecting (Reveal in Finder) so the user knows where the file went.
- **Verify:** confirmed — exportSession wired through client (EngramServiceClient.swift:193), protocol (EngramServiceProtocol.swift:38), mock, capability token (ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:37) and MCP, but grep for '.exportSession' under Engram/ is empty — no view caller. TranscriptToolbar.swift only has onCopyAll/onHandoff/onReplay/onResume/onToggleFavorite (lines 23-32, 152-160); no export. Context menus carry no Export. The only file/clipboard affordance is Copy (onCopyAll). Confirmed; high stands (complete export service with no in-app trigger).

#### `sources-sync-1` · 🔴 High · No way to enable or disable a source — the entire enable/disable workflow does not exist

- **Surface:** Sources: enable/disable + trigger sync
- **What's wrong:** The product owner's named workflow ('Sources: enable/disable + trigger sync') has no enable/disable half. SourcesSettingsSection renders each source as a static DataSourceRow with a read-only path label and a green/red path-exists dot — there is no Toggle, switch, or any control to turn a source on or off. The DataSourceDef carries a `key: "path.<source>"` (e.g. "path.claude-code"), but grep across all Swift confirms these keys are never read or written anywhere — they are decorative dead config. The data model has no concept of an enabled/disabled source at all: EngramServiceReadProvider.sources() derives the source list purely from `GROUP BY source FROM sessions` (rows that already got indexed), so 'which sources are active' is an output of indexing, never a user-controllable input.
- **User impact:** A user who wants to stop indexing a noisy source (e.g. Cursor or VS Code), or who only wants Claude Code + Codex tracked, has no control whatsoever. Every detected source is indexed unconditionally and there is no UI affordance to change that.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Settings/SourcesSettingsSection.swift:78-93 (DataSourceRow is read-only: Text + PathExistsIndicator, no Toggle); :4-29 (DataSourceDef.key="path.*" never consumed — grep for path.claude-code etc. across non-test Swift returns nothing); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:564-572 (sources() = GROUP BY source FROM sessions, no enabled flag)
- **Suggested fix:** Either (a) ship a real per-source enabled flag: add a Toggle to DataSourceRow, persist to settings.json, and have the indexer skip disabled sources; or (b) if disabling is out of scope, remove the dead `path.*` keys and re-label the Settings section as 'Detected source paths (read-only)' so it stops implying configurability.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed real gap. SourcesSettingsSection.swift:78-93 DataSourceRow renders only Text(name) + Text(path) + PathExistsIndicator — no Toggle/switch/control. The DataSourceDef.key="path.*" values (lines 11-28) are never consumed: grep across Engram/Shared/EngramService for 'path.claude-code|path.codex|path.windsurf|path.antigravity' and '"path.' (excluding SourcesSettingsSection.swift) returned zero hits — decorative dead config. EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:564-572 sources() derives the list purely from 'SELECT source ... GROUP BY source FROM sessions WHERE hidden_at IS NULL', i.e. an output of indexing, with no enabled/disabled flag anywhere. Grep for sourceEnabled/disableSource/enableSource found nothing; the only 'enableLiveSync' references are hardcoded adapter-construction constants, not user-controllable. No enable/disable workflow exists. Severity high is correct — half the product-owner-named workflow is entirely absent.

#### `sources-sync-2` · 🔴 High · No 'Sync now' / re-index action — triggerSync has UI nowhere and the backend is a hardcoded 'not implemented' stub

- **Surface:** Sources: enable/disable + trigger sync
- **What's wrong:** The 'trigger sync' half of the workflow is also absent from the UI. triggerSync is declared on the service protocol/client (EngramServiceClient.triggerSync), but grep confirms zero non-test callers anywhere in the Engram app target — no button, menu item, or context action invokes it. Even if it were wired, the backend handler is a fixed stub returning ok:false / error:'Sync is not implemented in the Swift service', and it is peer-to-peer sync (takes a `peer` param), not a per-source re-index. There is no manual re-index/refresh-index action on either Sources surface; SourcePulseView's only buttons are 'reveal archive store in Finder' and a section refresh that merely re-reads existing DB counts (loadData), it does not trigger any indexing.
- **User impact:** If a user adds a new tool, or a source's path appears after launch, there is no way to force Engram to pick it up on demand — they must wait for the service's periodic loop with no feedback that anything is happening. A 'Sync now' button a user might expect simply does not exist.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:796-808 (triggerSync returns hardcoded error 'Sync is not implemented in the Swift service'); macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift:121-123 (client method exists); grep triggerSync across Engram/ non-test = no UI caller; macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SourcePulseView.swift:72-73 + :160-178 (SectionHeader onRefresh only calls loadData() which re-reads counts, no re-index)
- **Suggested fix:** Add a real per-source 'Re-index now' action wired to a service command that actually re-scans that adapter, with inline progress + result feedback. Do not surface the existing triggerSync (peer-sync stub) to users; either implement it or remove its client surface to avoid the appearance of a capability.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:796-808 triggerSync returns a hardcoded ResultItem with ok:false, pulled:0, pushed:0, error:'Sync is not implemented in the Swift service', keyed on request.peer (peer-to-peer sync, not per-source re-index). EngramServiceClient.swift:121-123 declares the client method. Full grep for 'triggerSync' across all Swift shows only: protocol decl (EngramServiceProtocol.swift:25), client (EngramServiceClient.swift:121-122), mock (MockEngramServiceClient.swift), and the handler dispatch/stub (CommandHandler.swift:201-205, 796) — ZERO non-test UI callers. SourcePulseView.swift SectionHeader onRefresh closures (lines 63, 73) call loadLiveSessions()/loadData(), which only re-read counts (loadData uses serviceClient.sources() + db.sourceDistribution()), no indexing trigger. The only other buttons in the view are revealArchiveStore (line 49) and the live-session expander (line 203). The 'reindex/rebuildIndexed' grep hits are in SessionDetailView (in-transcript find/match rescan), unrelated to source re-indexing. Severity high is correct.

#### `settings-general-1` · 🔴 High · Web UI cannot be enabled from any UI; the only switch is hand-editing settings.json

- **Surface:** Settings: General / Network / About
- **What's wrong:** The native Hummingbird web server (EngramWebUIServer) is fully built and wired into the service, but it only starts when settings.json contains `webUIEnabled: true` (EngramServiceRunner.swift:86, readWebUIEnabled at :662-679 defaults FALSE). No SwiftUI control anywhere writes `webUIEnabled` — grep across macos/ finds it only in the runner and tests, never in any settings section. So a normal user has no way to turn the web UI on/off; the backend capability has no UI.
- **User impact:** A user who wants the browser-based session viewer sees an 'Open Web UI' button in General > Runtime Infrastructure but has no toggle to start the server. They must quit the app, hand-edit ~/.engram/settings.json to add webUIEnabled:true, and relaunch. Most users will conclude the feature is broken.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceRunner.swift:86,88,118-122,662-679 (gate + default false); grep for `webUIEnabled` across macos --include=*.swift returns only the runner and EngramWebUIServerTests — no settings view writes it; NetworkSettingsSection.swift only handles Sync (not implemented) and mcpStrictSingleWriter.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Enable Web UI' toggle (likely in Network or General > Runtime Infrastructure) that writes `webUIEnabled` via mutateEngramSettings, and surface that a service restart is required (or signal the running service to start/stop webTask).
- **Verify:** confirmed — Grep for `webUIEnabled` across Engram/Shared/EngramService/EngramMCP/EngramCore* returns matches ONLY in EngramServiceRunner.swift (gate + readWebUIEnabled). readWebUIEnabled (EngramServiceRunner.swift:662-679) reads `~/.engram/settings.json` or env `ENGRAM_WEB_UI_ENABLED`, defaulting FALSE (lines 673,678); webTask is gated on it (lines 86-88,118-122). I checked every Settings section file: GeneralSettingsSection.swift (no webUIEnabled write — only @AppStorage appLanguage/contentFontSize/showDockIcon), NetworkSettingsSection.swift (only mcpStrictSingleWriter + Sync placeholder), SettingsView.swift Advanced (only httpHost/CIDR/token). No SwiftUI control writes webUIEnabled anywhere. Real gap, correctly rated high: the built backend capability has no UI on/off switch — user must hand-edit settings.json.

- **What's wrong:** The AI Summary section's first three GroupBoxes — Provider (Base URL / API Key / Model), Summary Prompt (language / max sentences / style / custom prompt), and Generation (preset / max tokens / temperature / sampling) — all persist to settings.json and feed ServiceAISettings.summaryConfig, which is consumed ONLY by generateSummary(). The configuration is real and wired to a real backend, but the action that consumes it lives only in MCP.
- **User impact:** A user spends time configuring an AI provider and tuning summary prompt/generation parameters in Settings, then has no way to produce a single AI summary from inside the app — there is no Summarize/Generate button on any session, list, or detail view. The settings look complete but the workflow dead-ends; the feature is only usable from an external MCP client.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Settings/AISettingsSection.swift:51-199 (Provider/Summary Prompt/Generation groups, all saved via saveAISettings); macos/Engram/Views/SessionDetailView.swift:28-31 (in-app generateSummary entry point removed; only MCP generate_summary remains); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:871-896 (generateSummary uses settings.summaryConfig); grep confirms zero in-app Generate/Regenerate-Summary buttons across macos/Engram and Shared/EngramCore
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Generate Summary' action on SessionDetailView (and/or a 'Regenerate All Summaries' button next to 'Regenerate All' titles in this section) that calls serviceClient.generateSummary, mirroring the title flow. Even a single per-session button would close the loop so the provider/prompt/generation config is reachable.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified the entire grep surface for generateSummary/generate_summary across macos/Engram and macos/Shared. AISettingsSection.swift:51-199 persists Provider/Summary Prompt/Generation groups via saveAISettings()/AIGenerationSettings.write (lines 324-366). The service-side EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:871-895 generateSummary reads ServiceAISettings.summaryConfig (line 876-879) and only runs ServiceAIClient.summarize when config is present, else falls back to extractive nativeSummary. The ONLY non-test caller of serviceClient.generateSummary is MCPToolRegistry.swift:914 (generate_summary tool). SessionDetailView.swift:28-31 documents the in-app summary state and generateSummary() call were removed. Grep across Engram/Views (excluding regenerateAllTitles) found zero in-app Generate/Regenerate-Summary buttons; no CommandPaletteView action and no NotificationCenter post triggers summary generation (only .openSession at SessionDetailView.swift:646). The configuration GroupBoxes are real and persist, but no in-app control ever consumes them. Real backend-UI gap; high severity appropriate since three full config groups have no in-app action.

- **Evidence:** Backend: EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:686-698 (bulk UPDATE hidden_at WHERE message_count=0 AND size_bytes<1024). Wrapper: EngramServiceClient.swift:189-190. Non-test referencing files (grep): only EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift, SettingsView.swift, EngramServiceClient.swift, MockEngramServiceClient.swift, EngramServiceProtocol.swift, ServiceCapabilityToken.swift — none of which actually call client.hideEmptySessions() except the mock/test path.

- **Verify:** confirmed — Backend exists: EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:686-698 bulk UPDATE sessions SET hidden_at WHERE message_count=0 AND size_bytes<1024 AND hidden_at IS NULL, returns hiddenCount. Dispatched at line 315-317. Wrapper EngramServiceClient.swift:189-190; protocol :37; token ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:35; mock MockEngramServiceClient.swift:245-246. Grep across whole macos tree for hideEmptySessions: every non-test reference is plumbing — the only app reference is SettingsView's UNRELATED @State boolean hideEmptySessions (lines 190/292/450/515), which never calls the command. #### `hygiene-5` · 🔴 High · No in-app way to hide or unhide an individual session — setSessionHidden() is MCP/tests only

- **Surface:** Hygiene / cleanup workflow
- **What's wrong:** The service `setSessionHidden(sessionId, hidden)` toggles hidden_at for a session (and exposes an unhide via hidden:false). But no app-target file calls setSessionHidden — the only non-test callers are the service handler (definition), the MCP registry, and the client/protocol/token plumbing. So a user can VIEW hidden sessions but can neither hide a session nor unhide one from the app.
- **User impact:** The cleanup loop is broken in both directions: a session the user wants gone cannot be hidden in-app, and one that got hidden (e.g. via MCP) can be viewed via 'Show hidden sessions' but never restored to normal — there is no unhide button. The reverse half of the hide/undo workflow does not exist in the UI.
- **Evidence:** Backend: EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:611-644 (UPDATE sessions SET hidden_at). Only non-test referencing files (grep -rln, app excluded): EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift, EngramMCP/Core/MCPToolRegistry.swift:972, EngramServiceClient.swift, MockEngramServiceClient.swift, EngramServiceProtocol.swift, ServiceCapabilityToken.swift — nothing under macos/Engram. UI affordance that implies the feature: SessionsPageView.swift:43 'Show hidden sessions' toggle; DB read-side at Database.swift:653/658 fetchHiddenSessions/countHiddenSessions.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Hide'/'Unhide' action (context menu or detail-view button) on session rows that calls serviceClient.setSessionHidden(sessionId:hidden:), and surface an Unhide action when 'Show hidden sessions' is on, so hide is reversible from the app.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Backend EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:611-644 setSessionHidden toggles hidden_at (and unhide via hidden:false at line 618). Grep: setSessionHidden is called only at EngramMCP/Core/MCPToolRegistry.swift:972 plus client/protocol/mock/token/tests — grep -rln over ./Engram returns NOTHING, so no app-target caller. App can VIEW hidden sessions: SessionsPageView.swift:43 'Show hidden sessions' toggle drives includeHidden into listSessions (lines 71/111/116). Context menus in ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-126/342-352 offer Resume/Copy/Handoff/Replay only — no Hide/Unhide. ProjectsView contextMenu (168-175) has no hide either. Minor tracer inaccuracy: the read facade is listHiddenSessions/countHiddenSessions at Database.swift:650/658 (not 'fetchHiddenSessions' as cited, which exists nowhere), and both facades are themselves uncalled. Core claim — no in-app hide/unhide of an individual session — is correct. Severity high accurate.

#### `observability-2` · 🔴 High · Log stream and Error dashboard cannot read the EngramService process logs (the indexer) — they only see the app's own log entries

- **Surface:** Observability: logs / errors / perf / traces / health
- **What's wrong:** LogStreamView and ErrorDashboardView read os_log via OSLogReader, which tries OSLogStore(scope: .system) and falls back to .currentProcessIdentifier when system scope is denied (OSLogReader.swift:42-52). A notarized, non-root third-party app cannot open .system scope (requires the private com.apple.logging.local-store.read entitlement, which is NOT in Engram.entitlements). So in production it always falls back to .currentProcessIdentifier — which contains ONLY the host app process's entries. But EngramService (subsystem com.engram.service) runs as a SEPARATE child Process (EngramServiceLauncher.swift:143-157, Helpers/EngramService), and it is the component that does all indexing/writer/IPC work and logs the errors a user would actually want to see. Those entries are unreachable from the app's currentProcess store. The dashboards will silently show only com.engram.app entries, missing the entire com.engram.service half they claim to cover (OSLogReader.swift:27).
- **User impact:** On a shipped build, the Logs and Errors tabs appear to work but quietly omit all service/indexer logs — the most important signal. A user debugging 'why is my session not indexing' will see an empty or misleadingly clean error dashboard because the indexer's errors live in a process the reader can't access, with no warning that coverage is partial.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Core/OSLogReader.swift:42-52 (system-scope fallback to currentProcessIdentifier); macos/Engram/Engram.entitlements:1-17 (no logging-read entitlement; hardened runtime, notarized); macos/Engram/Core/EngramServiceLauncher.swift:143-157 (EngramService spawned as separate Process); subsystem set at OSLogReader.swift:27
- **Suggested fix:** Have EngramService persist its own structured log/error ring to a file or table the app can read (or expose recent errors via the existing service IPC), and read service errors through that channel instead of relying on cross-process OSLogStore access the sandbox/entitlement model forbids.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified OSLogReader.makeStore() (OSLogReader.swift:42-52) tries OSLogStore(scope: .system) then falls back to .currentProcessIdentifier. Engram/Engram.entitlements is the ONLY app entitlements file (find . -name '*.entitlements' → only Engram/Engram.entitlements plus unrelated GRDB test fixtures) and it contains ONLY com.apple.security.automation.apple-events — no com.apple.logging.local-store.read / private-data entitlement; the file's own comments confirm Hardened Runtime + notarization. A non-root notarized app cannot open .system scope, so production falls back to .currentProcessIdentifier. EngramServiceLauncher.swift:14-25 + 143-157 confirms EngramService is spawned as a SEPARATE Process (Contents/Helpers/EngramService, proc.run() at :157) under its own PID, logging to subsystem com.engram.service (ServiceLogger.swift:15). currentProcessIdentifier store only contains the host app's (com.engram.app) entries, so the entire service half is unreachable by LogStreamView/ErrorDashboardView/SystemHealthView. NUANCE (does not refute): the launcher drains the service's stdout/stderr (EngramServiceLauncher.swift:151-156) and forwards structured index_error events to the status store (EventSink comment :35-40), and SystemHealthView's index-scan row reads serviceStatusStore — so SOME service-failure signal reaches a different surface. But the Log stream and Error dashboard specifically read only OSLogReader, so finding 2's core claim about those dashboards holds. High severity justified.

#### `usage-cost-1` · 🔴 High · Real per-dollar cost data (get_costs / session_costs) has no app UI at all — only MCP

- **Surface:** Usage / cost tracking
- **What's wrong:** The product has a real token-accounting cost backend: the session_costs table (SchemaManifest.swift:18) stores cost_usd, input_tokens, output_tokens, cache tokens, and MCPDatabase.getCosts() returns totalCostUsd plus a full breakdown by source/project/day/model. But this data is exposed ONLY through the MCP get_costs tool. No SwiftUI view reads session_costs or renders any dollar amount. The only cost-related app UI is a bare count pill '\(costedSessionCount) costed' in SourcePulseView (SourcePulseView.swift:100-102). The popover 'USAGE' section (PopoverUsageSection.swift) renders usage-pressure percentages and token-share metrics only; there is no $ cost dashboard, no 'spent today/this month', no per-project/per-model cost view.
- **User impact:** A user who wants to know 'how much have I spent across my AI tools' cannot answer that in the app. The data exists and is queryable by agents via MCP, but the desktop GUI exposes only a count of 'costed' sessions, never an actual dollar figure or a breakdown. The headline value proposition of cost tracking is invisible to a normal (non-MCP) user.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPDatabase.swift:196-251 (getCosts builds totalCostUsd + breakdown from session_costs); macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPToolRegistry.swift:112,778-780 (get_costs tool); macos/EngramCoreRead/Database/Schema/SchemaManifest.swift:18 (session_costs table); macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SourcePulseView.swift:100-102 (only count pill, no $); grep for session_costs/cost_usd across Engram views returns zero $ renderings
- **Suggested fix:** Add a minimal cost panel (e.g. in SourcePulseView or a new 'Costs' page) that calls the existing getCosts logic via the service to show total $ and a source/day breakdown. The backend query already exists; this is purely a UI/read-path wiring task.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified the app NEVER renders a dollar figure from the session_costs token-accounting backend. The app's only session_costs reads in EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:989-1014 (sourceTokenCounts, sourceCostedCounts) compute COUNT(DISTINCT c.session_id) only — line 1010-1014 filters cost_usd>0 but selects COUNT, never SUM(cost_usd). The dollar-summing getCosts() with SUM(c.cost_usd) AS costUsd / totalCostUsd lives ONLY in EngramMCP/Core/MCPDatabase.swift:196-251 (MCP-only, exposed via get_costs tool). SourcePulseView.swift:100-102 renders only the bare '\(costedSessionCount) costed' count pill, sourced from costedSessionCount (Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift:476). One nuance the tracer missed: SourcePulseView.swift:246-247 and PopoverUsageSection.swift:199-200 DO render '$' strings, but those come from the SEPARATE usage_snapshots table (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:1043 'FROM usage_snapshots', metric LIKE '%cost%share%' at line 1061) — provider-reported usage limits / cost-share with a '$' unit, NOT the session_costs backend. So a '$X/$Y' usage-limit bar exists, but there is no dashboard of actual accumulated per-dollar spend (spent today/this month, per-project/per-model totals) from session_costs. Core claim holds: the real token-accounting cost backend has no app UI; only MCP exposes it. Severity high upheld.

So the live data backing the badge has zero representation in the surface the badge points at. Real gap, high severity stands.

Grep for exportSession / EngramServiceExportSessionRequest across BOTH macos/Engram/ and macos/Shared/ returns matches ONLY in the service client/protocol/mock/models/capability — zero UI callers in Engram/. Additionally grep for 'Export', 'fileExporter', 'NSSavePanel', 'savePanel' across macos/Engram/ returns NOTHING (exit 1) — there is no export button, no save panel, no file-exporter anywhere in the app UI. SessionDetailView only offers copyAllTranscript (:182, :400, :726) plus Resume/Replay/Handoff. So a user genuinely cannot export a transcript to a file from the app; the complete markdown/json/html export backend is unreachable from the UI. Severity high stands: this is a fully-built backend capability with no UI entry point at all.

- **Surface:** X-cut: backend capability ↔ UI exposure matrix
- **What's wrong:** saveInsight and deleteInsight are fully implemented in the service (EngramServiceCommandHandler) and exposed as MCP tools (save_insight/delete_insight), but the app calls neither. grep across macos/Engram returns zero call sites for both. They can never view, add, or remove an insight from the app. Insights are an agent-only (MCP) feature, completely hidden from the human end-user.

No getInsights/getMemory method even exists in EngramServiceClient.swift or EngramServiceProtocol.swift, so the app cannot read the insights table either. Backend is real: EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:113 (saveInsight) and :123 (deleteInsight) dispatch to writer-backed implementations. The active-memory/insight system is fully invisible to a human app user. Note: the only insight string in any view is explanatory text in NetworkSettingsSection.swift:33 describing the save_insight MCP tool, which reinforces it is MCP-only. High severity stands.

Full-tree grep of macos for setSessionHidden (excluding Shared/Service definitions) yields only: EngramMCP/Core/MCPToolRegistry.swift:972 (the hide_session MCP tool) plus service handler and tests — NO app view, card, context menu, or detail toolbar calls it. No command palette / NotificationCenter event exposes hide either. So a user can reveal hidden sessions but has no in-app way to hide or unhide one; the only producer of hidden_at from the UI side is the MCP tool. Claim fully confirmed. Severity medium is appropriate (backend-ui-gap, not a crash/dead-end of a visible control — the toggle works; it just implies a non-existent hide action).

Full-tree grep of macos for renameSession (excluding Shared/Service defs) returns ONLY the service handler and tests (EngramServiceIPCTests.swift:2834) — no app view caller, and notably no MCP registry caller either (so it is even more orphaned than setSessionHidden, which at least has the hide_session MCP tool). The RenameSheet is for projects: it takes projectName: String (RenameSheet.swift:16) and runs runRename() via the project-move/rename path (:192-194), not session custom_name. No palette/NotificationCenter path exists. So the session-rename feature is plumbed to the service layer but has zero user-reachable entry point. Claim confirmed; severity medium (orphaned backend capability with a working display path but no write UI).

So last_accessed_at/access_count never populate. accessedDesc/accessedAsc exist in Database.swift:11-12 but the only sort picker UI (TimelinePageView TimelineSortMode, lines 4-27/57-64) offers only Active(.updatedDesc) and Created(.createdDesc); SessionsPageView.swift:119 hard-codes .updatedDesc. #### `agents-grouping-2` · 🟠 Medium · No UI surfaces pending suggestions for the user to find — review is incidental, not discoverable

- **Surface:** Agent sessions + parent/child link management
- **What's wrong:** The backend computes suggested_parent_id via the Layer-2 heuristic, and the app CAN act on it (confirm/dismiss is wired in SessionsPageView, TimelinePageView, and SessionDetailView). But there is no surface that aggregates or lists "sessions with a pending suggestion awaiting your review." The confirm/dismiss controls only appear when a user happens to expand the specific parent that owns the suggested child (ExpandableSessionCard only loads suggestedChildren on expand) or happens to open the specific child's detail view. A user has no way to discover that suggestions exist or are waiting. The natural home for such an inbox would be AgentsView, which shows none.
- **User impact:** Even though the heuristic produces suggestions and the confirm/dismiss machinery works, a user will rarely encounter a suggestion unless they manually expand the exact right parent. The grouping intelligence is effectively invisible, so most suggested links never get confirmed or rejected.
- **Evidence:** ExpandableSessionCard.swift:236-262 loads suggestedChildren only after the parent row is expanded; SessionDetailView.swift:300-329 shows the suggested-parent confirm/dismiss only inside one session's detail; no view queries an app-wide "pending suggestions" list — the only count-level reads are childCount/suggestedChildCount per parent (Database.swift:1104-1147). AgentsView.swift has no suggestion query at all.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a "pending suggestions" section (count badge + list) to AgentsView or HomeView that queries sessions with non-null suggested_parent_id and renders Confirm/Dismiss inline, reusing the existing serviceClient.confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion calls.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed no aggregated 'pending suggestions' surface exists. Grepped the whole Engram tree for suggestion surfacing: the only readers of suggested children are ExpandableSessionCard.loadChildren (only fires on expand — toggleExpand at line 232-238 calls loadChildren which reads db.suggestedChildSessions at 250-253) and SessionDetailView (per-child detail breadcrumb at lines 300-329, reading suggestedChildSessions at 573). HomeView/TimelinePageView/SessionsPageView only read suggestedChildCount (a per-parent count for the disclosure badge), never a flat 'awaiting review' list. No view queries an app-wide pending-suggestions inbox; Session.hasSuggestedParent (Session.swift:102) exists as a model flag but no screen filters/aggregates on it. So suggestion review is incidental (requires expanding the exact owning parent or opening the exact child). Medium severity is fair — the capability to act exists but discovery is effectively absent.

#### `agents-grouping-3` · 🟠 Medium · setParentSession (manual link to a chosen parent) has a backend + capability but no UI entry point anywhere in the app

- **Surface:** Agent sessions + parent/child link management
- **What's wrong:** The service exposes setParentSession (EngramServiceClient.setParentSession -> EngramServiceCommandHandler.setParentSession), and it is an authorized capability (ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27). There is no "Link to parent..." / "Set parent..." command, picker, or menu item. A core half of the "manage parent/child links" workflow is unreachable from the UI.
- **Evidence:** EngramServiceClient.swift:96-98 + EngramServiceProtocol.swift:21 + EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:149-157,521 implement setParentSession; ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27 authorizes it. Grep for setParentSession across macos/Engram (app views) yields NO call site — only EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/StartupBackfills.swift:806,1173 (automatic path-based backfill) uses it. SessionDetailView/SessionsPageView/TimelinePageView call only confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion/clearParentSession.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a "Link to parent..." affordance (e.g. a context-menu item on a session that opens a parent picker, or a field in SessionDetailView when no parent/suggestion exists) that calls serviceClient.setParentSession(sessionId:parentId:). The client method and service handler already exist.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed setParentSession has full backend/capability but no app UI entry point. Service plumbing exists: EngramServiceClient.swift:96-97, EngramServiceProtocol.swift:21, MockEngramServiceClient.swift:181-182, command handler EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:149-152,521, and it is authorized in ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27. confirmSuggestion is a SEPARATE command (EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:169,481) that only accepts a precomputed suggested_parent_id — verified distinct. Grep for setParentSession across the entire Engram app tree returns ZERO call sites; the only non-Shared usage is EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/StartupBackfills.swift:806 which calls a private static DB-write helper (defined at 1173), i.e. the automatic path-based backfill, not the service command. App views call only confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion (SessionDetailView, SessionsPageView, TimelinePageView) and clearParentSession (SessionDetailView.swift:617). Both context menus in ExpandableSessionCard (lines 116-129 parent, 342-355 child) offer only Resume/Copy/Handoff/Replay — no 'Set/Link to parent'. No picker/command/menu item exists. Users can only accept a machine suggestion or unlink, never manually establish an unsuggested link. Medium severity is appropriate.

#### `projects-migration-1` · 🟠 Medium · Migration history is never shown as history — only as an undo picker (last 5 committed)

- **Surface:** Projects: move / rename / archive / undo / history
- **What's wrong:** The backend stores a full migration_log with rich per-entry data (state, finishedAt, archived, auditNote, detail, rolledBack relationships) and projectMigrations accepts a state filter (committed/failed/etc.) plus arbitrary limit. The app never surfaces this as a browsable history. The only consumer that displays entries is UndoSheet.loadMigrations(), which hard-codes state:"committed", limit:5 (UndoSheet.swift:254-256). ProjectsView only uses projectMigrations to decide if the Undo button is enabled (ProjectsView.swift:241-244, limit:1), and HomeView only uses it to compute project warnings (HomeView.swift:272-274). There is no view that lists what was moved/renamed/archived, when, by whom, with audit notes, or which migrations failed or were rolled back.
- **User impact:** A user who moved/renamed/archived several projects cannot review what happened. They can't see audit notes they may have set, can't see failed or rolled-back migrations, and can't see more than the 5 most recent committed moves — and even those 5 only appear inside the Undo dialog, framed as 'pick one to reverse', not as a history log. The product owner's 'island feature' concern applies directly: the migration ledger exists in the backend but the user can't actually read their own project history.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Projects/UndoSheet.swift:254-257 (only committed, limit 5); macos/Engram/Views/Pages/ProjectsView.swift:241-244 (limit 1, enablement only); macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:272-274 (warnings only); DTO with full history fields incl. auditNote/detail/archived at macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift:891-904; request supports any state filter at EngramServiceModels.swift:882-885
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Migration History' panel in ProjectsView (or a sheet) that calls projectMigrations with a larger limit and no state restriction, rendering oldPath→newPath, timestamp, actor, state (committed/failed/rolled-back), and auditNote. Reuse UndoSheet's migrationRow rendering.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified all three consumers of projectMigrations in the app. UndoSheet.loadMigrations (UndoSheet.swift:254-256) hard-codes state:"committed", limit:5 and renders them only as an undo picker. ProjectsView.loadData (ProjectsView.swift:241-244) uses limit:1 purely to set hasRecentMigrations (Undo button enablement). HomeView (HomeView.swift:272-274) fetches limit:25 only to compute TodayProjectWarning via TodayWorkbenchSupport.swift:121. The DTO EngramServiceMigrationLogEntry (EngramServiceModels.swift:891-904) carries state/finishedAt/archived/auditNote/detail/actor and the request supports any state filter (EngramServiceModels.swift:882-885). Grep for MigrationLogEntry/migration-history across Engram/ returns only UndoSheet.swift and TodayWorkbenchSupport.swift — no browsable history view, no failed/rolled-back listing, no audit-note surface. The gap is real. One correction: the tracer's 'rolledBack relationships' framing overstates the DTO; the rolled_back_of linkage lives in MCPDatabase.swift:1365 (orderedPipelineResult) and EngramServiceCommandHandler+ProjectMigration.swift, not in the app-facing EngramServiceMigrationLogEntry DTO, so the app couldn't render rolled-back relationships even if it tried. Severity lowered high→medium: this is a missing read-only history view (informational), not a broken or unreachable core action — undo, the one destructive path, is fully wired.

#### `projects-migration-5` · 🟠 Medium · projectRecover / projectReview / projectTimeline backends exist but have no app surface

- **Surface:** Projects: move / rename / archive / undo / history
- **What's wrong:** The backend implements projectRecover (MCPDatabase.projectRecover, MCPToolRegistry.swift:1062), projectReview (MCPFileTools.projectReview, MCPToolRegistry.swift:873), and projectTimeline (Database.projectTimeline:558, MCPDatabase.projectTimeline:355, MCPToolRegistry.swift:804).
