This is the core 'partially built island' pattern: the destructive half (move/archive) is wired to the GUI, the inspect/recover half is wired only to MCP.
- **Evidence:** Backend implemented & MCP-exposed: macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPDatabase.swift:463 (projectRecover), macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPFileTools.swift:19 (projectReview), macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPToolRegistry.swift:873 & 1062; app Database.projectTimeline at macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift:558; no app view calls projectRecover/projectReview (grep of Engram/**/*.swift)
- **Suggested fix:** Surface projectReview output in the residual-refs warning boxes (RenameSheet residualWarningBox / ArchiveSheet) as an in-app 'Show remaining files' disclosure, and add a recover entry point that calls projectRecover, instead of telling users to use a nonexistent CLI.
- **Verify:** confirmed — projectRecover and projectReview exist only in EngramMCP: tool definitions at MCPToolRegistry.swift:368 (project_review) and 684 (project_recover), dispatch at 872 and 1060, implementations MCPFileTools.projectReview and MCPDatabase.projectRecover. Grep for projectRecover/projectReview across Engram/ and Shared/ returns ZERO non-MCP hits — no app view calls them. So when RenameSheet/ArchiveSheet/UndoSheet tell users to 'review' residual refs, the capability is built but has no app entry point. One refinement to the tracer's wording: the claim that app-side Database.projectTimeline (Database.swift:558) 'is only used by TimelinePageView' is inaccurate — grep shows projectTimeline has NO view callers at all (the TimelineEntry/ReplayTimelineEntry references in SessionReplayView are an unrelated replay type). This makes the app surface even thinner than stated but does not change the verdict. Confirmed; medium severity fits (advanced recovery/inspection reachable via MCP only).

#### `hooks-config-2` · 🟠 Medium · Backend knows each hook's source file URL but the DTO drops it, structurally blocking any 'jump to hook' action

- **Surface:** Hooks page
- **What's wrong:** The service already has the exact source file URL for every hook (it iterates ('global', ~/.claude/settings.json) and ('project', ~/.claude/settings.local.json) to read them), but EngramServiceHookInfo only carries event/command/scope. The file URL, the per-hook matcher, and the hook 'type' are all discarded before reaching the UI. So even if a developer wanted to add an 'open this hook's file' or 'jump to definition' button, the UI has no path to thread to feed it — the gap is baked into the DTO, not just missing UI.
- **User impact:** Users cannot be offered a real 'go to this hook in settings.json' action because the app literally never receives which file or where in it the hook lives. Any future hook-management UX requires a service+DTO change, not just a view tweak.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:195-210 (loop has `url` for each scope and reads it, but constructs EngramServiceHookInfo(event:command:scope:) — url never propagated); macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift:578-583 (DTO fields are only event, command, scope; id is a synthetic 'scope/event/command' string, no path). hookCommands at EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:266-282 also flattens object handlers (matcher/type) into a raw command/JSON string, losing structure.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a `path` (and optionally `matcher`/`type`) field to EngramServiceHookInfo and populate it from the `url` already in scope at EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:198-205. Then HooksView can open/reveal that path directly.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:195-210 — the loop binds (scope, url) per settings file and reads via dictionary(at: url), but constructs EngramServiceHookInfo(event: event, command: command, scope: scope); url is never propagated. EngramServiceModels.swift:578-583 confirms the DTO carries only event/command/scope with a synthetic id 'scope/event/command' (no path field). hookCommands at 266-282 confirms object handlers ({matcher,type,command}) are flattened to the raw command string or JSON-serialized when no command key — matcher and type structure are lost. All providers funnel to this single filesystem hooks() (SQLite provider line 49 returns [], line 626 delegates to fileSystemProvider.hooks()), so no alternate path preserves the URL. The structural gap is real and baked into the DTO. Severity correctly medium: a backend/DTO limitation that blocks a future 'jump to hook file' action — a latent enabler gap, not a user-facing broken flow on its own.

#### `settings-general-5` · 🟠 Medium · Advanced 'Web API & Security' (HTTP Host / Allowed CIDRs / Bearer Token) are stored but read by nothing

- **Surface:** Settings: General / Network / About
- **What's wrong:** The Advanced section persists httpHost, httpAllowCIDR, and httpBearerToken to settings.json (SettingsView.swift:445-447,493-511). These are the only network bind/port/token controls in Settings, and the task's 'Network settings (web UI port/bind/token)' maps to them. But no Swift service or shared code reads any of these keys — the running EngramWebUIServer hardcodes host '127.0.0.1', port 3457, and a per-launch provisioned token (EngramWebUIServer.swift:37 defaults; runner provisions webToken at EngramServiceRunner.swift:87,90,93). So the user-entered bind address, CIDR allowlist, and bearer token have zero runtime effect.
- **User impact:** A user who sets a bearer token or LAN CIDR allowlist to expose/secure the web API believes they configured access control, but the server ignores all of it — it always binds loopback:3457 with an internally generated token. This is a security-relevant false promise: the visible 'Bearer Token' field changes nothing.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/SettingsView.swift:445-447 (load), :493-511 (save httpHost/httpAllowCIDR/httpBearerToken); grep for httpHost/httpAllowCIDR/httpBearerToken across macos/EngramService + macos/Shared --include=*.swift returns NOTHING (no service reader); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramWebUIServer.swift:37 (host default 127.0.0.1, port 3457), macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceRunner.swift:87,90,93 (per-launch provisioned token, hardcoded 127.0.0.1:3457). Readers exist only in legacy TS src/web.ts.
- **Suggested fix:** Either wire EngramServiceRunner/EngramWebUIServer to read httpHost/httpAllowCIDR/httpBearerToken from settings.json (so bind/token/allowlist take effect), or remove these orphaned controls from the Advanced section since the Swift web server is loopback-only with its own token.
- **Verify:** confirmed — SettingsView.swift persists httpHost/httpAllowCIDR/httpBearerToken to settings.json (load 445-447, save 493-511). Grep for these keys (and allowCIDR/bearerToken/allowedHosts) across all .swift excluding /build/ and SettingsView returns NO service reader — the only hit is MCPConfig.swift:11, a comment stating the old bearerToken fields 'are gone.' The running web server hardcodes host '127.0.0.1' and port 3457 (EngramWebUIServer.swift:37 init defaults) and uses a per-launch provisioned token: runner calls provisionWebToken (EngramServiceRunner.swift:87,754) and passes it to init (line 90) — settings httpBearerToken is never read. The host gate is loopback-only via isLoopbackHost (EngramWebUIServer.swift:138-141,168); there is no httpAllowCIDR consumer at all. So user-entered bind/CIDR/token have zero runtime effect. Confirmed; medium is fair.

#### `activity-2` · 🟠 Medium · file_activity backend (session_files table) has zero UI on a page literally named 'Activity'

- **Surface:** Activity page
- **What's wrong:** Both the TypeScript reference (src/core/db/metrics-repo.ts:170 getFileActivity) and the shipped Swift MCP path (macos/EngramMCP/Core/MCPDatabase.swift:313 getFileActivity) expose a real per-file activity capability querying the session_files table (which files were touched, edit/read counts, distinct sessions). No Swift app view consumes it: grep across macos/Engram for session_files / getFileActivity / 'File Activity' / fileHotspot returns no UI hits. ActivityView only renders session-count aggregates (dailyActivity, hourlyActivity, sourceDistribution), never file-level data.
- **User impact:** An MCP agent can ask 'which files are hottest in this project' and get an answer, but a human using the app — on the page named Activity — sees no file activity at all. A whole backend dimension is invisible in the product UI.
- **Evidence:** MCPDatabase.swift:313-353 getFileActivity (real query over session_files JOIN sessions); metrics-repo.ts:170-203 getFileActivity; ActivityView.swift:59-66 loads only dailyActivity/hourlyActivity/sourceDistribution/countSessionsSince — no file query; grep for session_files/getFileActivity in macos/Engram/**.swift returns nothing
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Top Files' / 'File Hotspots' section to ActivityView backed by a Swift read facade over session_files (mirroring getFileActivity), or surface it per-project in ProjectsView. At minimum, expose it somewhere in the app so the capability isn't UI-orphaned.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed the backend exists in both paths exactly as cited: Swift MCPDatabase.swift:313-353 getFileActivity runs 'SELECT sf.file_path, sf.action, SUM(sf.count), COUNT(DISTINCT sf.session_id) FROM session_files sf JOIN sessions s ON s.id=sf.session_id ... GROUP BY file_path,action ORDER BY total_count DESC' (read at offset 305-353), and the TS reference src/core/db/metrics-repo.ts:170-203 getFileActivity has the identical query. Grepped the whole ./Engram (SwiftUI app) AND ./Shared tree for session_files / getFileActivity / fileActivity / 'File Activity' / fileHotspot — ZERO hits. The only Swift consumers are EngramMCP (MCPDatabase.swift + MCPToolRegistry.swift — the MCP tool surface for agents, not app UI) and schema/migration files (EngramCoreRead SchemaManifest.swift, EngramCoreWrite EngramMigrations.swift). ActivityView.loadData (ActivityView.swift:60-64) loads only dailyActivity/hourlyActivity/sourceDistribution/countSessionsSince — never any file-level query. So a page literally named 'Activity' surfaces zero of the per-file activity data the backend exposes. Confirmed. Kept medium: it is a genuine backend-to-GUI gap, though slightly mitigated by the capability being fully reachable through the EngramMCP tool path for agent consumers, so it is not strictly high.

#### `observability-5` · 🟠 Medium · Backend health() endpoint is a hardcoded stub; SystemHealthView never calls it and the response carries no real signal

- **Surface:** Observability: logs / errors / perf / traces / health
- **What's wrong:** There is a service health() command end-to-end (EngramServiceClient.health -> command 'health' at EngramServiceClient.swift:33-34, handler at EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:52-55), but ALL THREE read-provider implementations return an identical hardcoded literal EngramServiceHealthResponse(ok: true, status: 'healthy', message: 'Swift service ready') regardless of actual state (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:30, 105, 557). The response type itself has only ok/status/message (EngramServiceModels.swift:440-444). Meanwhile SystemHealthView never calls health() at all — it derives status from serviceStatusStore.status plus local DB pragmas and OSLogReader (SystemHealthView.swift:69-107). So the one backend 'health' capability named for this surface is a no-op stub, and the Health tab reuses the same OSLogReader error count that suffers from findings 2-4.
- **User impact:** The 'Health' tab's most reliable rows (DB size, journal mode, service running) are real, but its 'Recent Errors (24h)' count inherits the redacted/partial log problems, and the named backend health() endpoint reports a constant 'healthy' that no UI consumes — so there is no actual end-to-end health check a user can trust beyond DB existence.
- **Evidence:** Stub identical across providers: macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:30, 104-106, 556-558; thin response type macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift:440-444; SystemHealthView does not call health(): macos/Engram/Views/Observability/SystemHealthView.swift:69-107 (uses serviceStatusStore + db pragmas + OSLogReader only)
- **Suggested fix:** Make health() return real signal (last index time, pending job count, error count, last error) and have SystemHealthView consume it, OR remove the dead health() stub and document that Health is DB-pragma + service-status only. Don't ship a 'healthy'-constant endpoint that nothing reads.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified the health() command chain: EngramServiceClient.health() → command('health') (EngramServiceClient.swift:33-34); handler case 'health' → readProvider.health() (EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:52-55). All THREE read-provider implementations return the byte-identical hardcoded literal EngramServiceHealthResponse(ok: true, status: 'healthy', message: 'Swift service ready') (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:29-31, 104-106, 556-558) regardless of runtime state. The response type carries only ok/status/message (EngramServiceModels.swift:440-444). SystemHealthView never calls health() — grep for '.health()' across Engram/Shared returned ZERO matches; SystemHealthView derives status from serviceStatusStore.status (SystemHealthView.swift:69-86) + DB pragmas (dbSizeBytes/journalMode, :93-101) + OSLogReader.countErrors (:97). So the named 'health' backend capability is a no-op stub unused by the Health tab, and that tab reuses the OSLogReader error count that inherits the defects in findings 2-4. All sub-claims verified. Medium severity appropriate — the Health tab still shows real index-scan/DB signal via serviceStatusStore, so it is not a total dead-end, but the health() stub is genuinely dead and the error KPI is degraded.

#### `command-palette-1` · 🟠 Medium · Palette has no action commands at all — only page navigation and session search

- **Surface:** Command palette
- **What's wrong:** The command palette's '>' command mode only ever lists page-navigation entries. `filteredCommands` is built exclusively from `PaletteItem.navigationCommands(...)` (CommandPaletteView.swift:22), and `PaletteItem` is only ever constructed inside `navigationCommands` (PaletteItem.swift:18-29) which maps `Screen.allCases` to 'Go to X' rows. There is no way to trigger any real action from the palette: no Export, no Resume session, no Hide session, no Re-index / Refresh, no settings toggles, no 'Open Settings' as an action, no project-move/link actions. All of these capabilities exist elsewhere in the GUI (e.g. export/resume in SessionDetailView.swift and TranscriptToolbar.swift, resume in ResumeDialog.swift, project actions via EngramServiceClient). A power user who opens ⌘K expecting a real command runner (VS Code / Raycast style) finds only a glorified page switcher plus session search.
- **User impact:** A user expecting a command palette to run commands (export this, resume that, re-index, jump to Settings section, toggle a setting) can only navigate between pages or jump to a session. Every actual action still requires hunting through the GUI, defeating the main value proposition of a ⌘K palette.
- **Evidence:** CommandPaletteView.swift:21-27 (filteredCommands only uses navigationCommands); PaletteItem.swift:18-29 (navigationCommands is the only PaletteItem factory, all category .navigation); grep confirmed PaletteItem(...) is constructed in exactly one place (PaletteItem.swift:20). Backend actions exist but are unreachable from palette: SessionDetailView.swift / TranscriptToolbar.swift (export/resume), ResumeDialog.swift, EngramServiceClient (project move/link/hide).
- **Suggested fix:** Add an action tier to the palette: in command mode, append `PaletteItem`s with category `.action` for the high-value global actions (Open Settings, Re-index / Refresh, Export current session, Resume last session, Toggle theme). Wire each action's closure to the existing service/GUI call paths already used by the corresponding buttons.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified directly. CommandPaletteView.swift:21-27 builds command mode exclusively from PaletteItem.navigationCommands(navigate:); non-command mode (lines 34-39) is session search only. PaletteItem.swift:18-29 is the sole factory and maps Screen.allCases (16 screens, Screen.swift) to 'Go to X' rows, all category: .navigation. Grep confirms PaletteItem(...) is constructed in exactly one place (PaletteItem.swift:20) and the only [PaletteItem] factory is navigationCommands; the PaletteCategory .action and .session cases (PaletteItem.swift:6-7) are defined but never used anywhere in Engram/Shared. No Export/Resume/Hide/Re-index/settings-toggle/project-move command path exists in the palette. The keyboard handling (CommandPaletteView.swift:167-178) only binds upArrow/downArrow/escape, so there is no modifier-triggered action path either. The capabilities genuinely exist elsewhere in the GUI but unreachable from the palette: ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-127 contextMenu (Resume.../Copy Resume Command/Handoff/Replay), ResumeDialog.swift, SessionDetailView.swift, and EngramServiceClient.swift (hide/setParent). Claim is factually correct. Downgrading high->medium: the palette is functional as a page-switcher plus session search, so this is a missing power-user enhancement (no action-runner commands), not a broken or dead-end primary flow; impact is convenience, not a blocked capability since every action is reachable via context menus/detail view.

#### `xc-deadends-4` · 🟠 Medium · Manual parent linking (setParentSession) has no UI; only auto-suggestion confirm/dismiss is wired

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** The service supports setParentSession (manually link an arbitrary child session to a chosen parent) and clearParentSession, both in the capability token. Only confirmSuggestion / dismissSuggestion (acting on Layer-2 auto-suggested parents) are wired into the UI. There is no UI affordance to manually pick a parent for a session the heuristic did not suggest, so the documented Layer-3 manual linking workflow is unreachable from the app.
- **User impact:** Agent-session grouping is only partly user-controllable: you can accept or reject what the heuristic guesses, but you cannot manually attach a session to a parent it failed to detect, so misgrouped sessions stay misgrouped.
- **Evidence:** Client: macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceClient.swift:96 func setParentSession; capability token macos/Shared/Service/ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27 "setParentSession", :28 "clearParentSession". UI callers: grep setParentSession across macos/Engram/ returns no matches; only confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion are called (SessionDetailView.swift:592,599,607,625; TimelinePageView.swift:138,150; SessionsPageView.swift:156,168). SessionDetailView has an unlinkParent button (:287) but no set-parent picker.
- **Suggested fix:** Expose a 'Set parent...' action (e.g., a session picker sheet) in SessionDetailView wired to serviceClient.setParentSession, complementing the existing unlink/confirm/dismiss controls.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. setParentSession exists in service plumbing (EngramServiceClient.swift:96-97, protocol :21, mock :181, capability ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:27) but grep across macos/Engram/ shows NO UI caller of setParentSession. The only parent-link mutation wired in the UI is clearParentSession via unlinkParent (SessionDetailView.swift:287 button -> :615 unlinkParent -> :617 serviceClient.clearParentSession) and the auto-suggestion confirm/dismiss flow (confirmSuggestion/dismissSuggestion in SessionDetailView/TimelinePageView/SessionsPageView). There is no picker or affordance to manually choose an arbitrary parent for a session the heuristic did not suggest, so the documented Layer-3 manual linking workflow (CLAUDE.md cites EngramServiceClient.setParentSession as an app caller) is unreachable from the app UI. Severity medium is appropriate: clearParentSession/confirm/dismiss cover unlink + accept-suggestion, so it's a partial-coverage gap (cannot create a manual link from scratch) rather than a total dead-end.

- **What's wrong:** The only control on the page is an Active/Created sort segmented picker. - **User impact:** A user who wants to see activity beyond 30 days (last quarter, a specific week, "all time") cannot. There is no way to widen, narrow, or shift the window. Older sessions are simply invisible from this page with no affordance to reach them.

- **Suggested fix:** Add a range picker (e.g. 7d / 30d / 90d / All) next to the sort picker that updates the `days` argument and the badge label; the DB method already accepts the parameter.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified TimelinePageView.swift:120 hardcodes database.sessionTimeline(days: 30, sort: sort); the only interactive control is the Active/Created sort segmented picker at :57-64; badge '30d' at :55 is a static literal. Backend capability is real and unused: Database.swift:960 defines sessionTimeline(days: Int = 30, ...) parameterized; DatabaseManagerTests.swift:260/268/297 exercise days: 10_000; MCPToolRegistry.swift:199-200 confirms project_timeline accepts since/until. So a configurable window is a genuine backend-without-UI gap. However I downgrade severity from medium to low: a static 30-day window with no range picker is a minor UX/feature-completeness gap, not a misleading-promise or broken-flow issue; the page works correctly for its fixed window and the absence of a control is unsurprising/low-impact for users.

#### `xc-deadends-5` · 🟡 Low · Session rename backend (renameSession) has no UI — only project rename is reachable

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** The capability token whitelists renameSession (rename an individual session), but no app view calls it. The only rename UI in the app is PROJECT rename (RenameSheet / ProjectsView renameTarget), which is a different operation. There is no way to rename a session's title from the GUI even though titles are otherwise editable concepts (Regenerate All Titles exists in settings).
- **User impact:** A user who dislikes an auto-generated session title can regenerate ALL titles in settings but cannot rename one specific session, so per-session curation is impossible from the UI.
- **Evidence:** Capability token: macos/Shared/Service/ServiceCapabilityToken.swift:34 "renameSession". UI grep for renameSession in macos/Engram/ surfaces only project-rename code: ProjectsView.swift:123/171 renameTarget, RenameSheet.swift (project), UndoSheet.swift:94. No session-level rename call exists.
- **Suggested fix:** Add a 'Rename' action to the session context menu / detail view wired to serviceClient.renameSession, or remove the renameSession capability if per-session rename is out of scope.

#### `xc-capability-matrix-9` · 🟡 Low · recordSessionAccess is never called anywhere in the app or MCP, so app session access does not affect recency

- **Surface:** X-cut: backend capability ↔ UI exposure matrix
- **What's wrong:** recordSessionAccess is defined and has a real service handler, but grep across the entire macos tree (app AND MCP, excluding protocol/client/handler/test definitions) finds zero callers. Opening a session in the app does not record an access event, so any 'recently accessed' ordering or last_accessed-based behavior is never updated by app usage.
- **User impact:** If any list relies on recently-accessed ordering, a user opening sessions in the app won't influence it — recency reflects only indexing/other signals, making 'recent' feel stale or wrong.
- **Evidence:** EngramServiceClient.swift:182 recordSessionAccess; handler EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift (recordSessionAccess); grep 'recordSessionAccess' across macos excluding protocol/client/handler/token/tests returns no call site.
- **Suggested fix:** Call serviceClient.recordSessionAccess(sessionId:) when a session detail view opens (e.g., in SessionDetailView load), or remove the capability if recency is intentionally not access-based.

#### `xc-capability-matrix-10` · 🟡 Low · projectMoveBatch and manageProjectAlias backend capabilities have no app UI

- **Surface:** X-cut: backend capability ↔ UI exposure matrix
- **What's wrong:** projectMoveBatch (bulk project path rewrite) and manageProjectAlias (project alias management) are implemented in the service and exposed via MCP (project_move_batch, manage_project_alias), but the app calls neither. The Projects UI only supports single-project move (RenameSheet -> projectMove), archive (ArchiveSheet -> projectArchive), and undo (UndoSheet -> projectUndo). There is no batch-select UI and no alias management surface.
- **User impact:** A user relocating several projects at once must repeat single moves one by one; and project aliases (a feature agents can set via MCP) are invisible/unmanageable in the app. These are agent-only powers.
- **Evidence:** EngramServiceClient.swift:153 projectMoveBatch and :88 manageProjectAlias; zero app call sites for both (grep returns none in Engram). Handlers: EngramServiceCommandHandler+ProjectMigration.swift (projectMoveBatch), EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift (manageProjectAlias); MCP: MCPToolRegistry.swift. App Projects views only wire projectMove/projectArchive/projectUndo (RenameSheet.swift, ArchiveSheet.swift, UndoSheet.swift) with single-select pickers, no multi-select/batch.
- **Suggested fix:** Add multi-select + 'Move selected' in ProjectsView calling projectMoveBatch, and an alias-management field (per project) calling manageProjectAlias; lower priority than the insight/favorites/export gaps.

#### `xc-events-nav-3` · 🟡 Low · generate_summary is a backend/MCP-only capability with no app UI and no way to trigger or observe it in-app

- **Surface:** X-cut: notifications / events / deep-link wiring
- **What's wrong:** SessionDetailView explicitly removed its summary-generation UI (SessionDetailView.swift:28-31): the comment states the summary state and generateSummary() were deleted because 'there was no UI entry point' and the service summary is extractive, and that summary generation 'remains available via the MCP generate_summary tool.' Combined with finding xc-events-nav-1 (no summary_generated event reaches the app), the generate_summary service capability is fully MCP-only: a normal app user cannot request a summary for a session, and cannot see when one was produced.
- **User impact:** A desktop-app-only user (not using MCP) has no way to generate or trigger a session summary from the UI; the feature effectively does not exist for them even though the backend supports it.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/SessionDetailView.swift:28-31 (comment documenting removal of summary UI + generateSummary(), pointing users to MCP generate_summary); mcp__engram generate_summary tool exists; no generate_summary call site in Engram/Views
- **Suggested fix:** If summaries are intended for app users, add a 'Generate summary' action in SessionDetailView wired to serviceClient + a generate_summary service command; otherwise document it as intentionally MCP-only so it is not mistaken for an unfinished UI.

### Misleading controls (UI implies a capability the product lacks) (21)

#### `replay-2` · 🔴 High · Density bar is always empty and playback timing is always uniform (timestamps/durations never populated)

- **Surface:** Session replay
- **What's wrong:** The replay's two signature value-adds over a static transcript — a time-density heatmap and data-driven playback pacing — depend on per-entry timestamp and durationToNextMs. The production read provider hard-codes timestamp: nil, tokens: nil, durationToNextMs: nil for every entry. Consequently densityBuckets' guard on entries.first/last.timestamp always fails and it returns 100 zeros (a flat, meaningless bar), and scheduleNext always uses the `?? 500` fallback so every message advances at a fixed cadence regardless of the session's real rhythm. The per-message timestamp and token labels in messageView are also always absent.
- **User impact:** The density heatmap renders as a flat uniform strip conveying no information, and 'play' just steps through messages at a constant rate. The whole point of a temporal replay (seeing where the session sped up/stalled) is absent, so the feature looks built but delivers none of its differentiating value.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:905-914 (entry built with timestamp/toolName/tokens/durationToNextMs all nil); macos/Engram/Models/ReplayState.swift:62-67 (densityBuckets returns all-zero when timestamps nil) and :138 (delayMs = durationToNextMs ?? 500); macos/Engram/Views/Replay/SessionReplayView.swift:146-175 (densityBar) and :197-207 (timestamp/token labels gated on nil values)
- **Suggested fix:** Populate timestamp/tokens/durationToNextMs in the replay entry from session message metadata (the indexer already stores per-session costs and message timing); until then the density bar and speed picker imply capabilities the data layer doesn't provide.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified. Production replayEntries (EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:903-914) constructs every entry with timestamp/toolName/tokens/durationToNextMs all nil; no other path feeds entries (the replayTimeline at :53 and :212 are the Empty and filesystem providers returning entries: []). Consequently densityBuckets (Engram/Models/ReplayState.swift:62-67) hits the nil-timestamp guard and returns 100 zeros (flat bar). scheduleNext (:138) always uses durationToNextMs ?? 500 so pacing is fixed/uniform. messageView timestamp/token labels (SessionReplayView.swift:197-207) are gated on non-nil and never render. The view is reachable via the SessionDetailView sheet, so both advertised value-adds (density heatmap + data-driven pacing) are non-functional. Severity high upheld.

#### `hygiene-1` · 🔴 High · Hygiene backend is a hardcoded placeholder — the entire page shows a fake 'not implemented' result

- **Surface:** Hygiene / cleanup workflow
- **What's wrong:** The service `hygiene()` command never runs any real check. It unconditionally returns a single `info` issue with message 'Swift service hygiene checks are not implemented' and `score: 0`, regardless of database state. The `force` parameter only swaps the issue's `action` text to the literal string 'force-refresh requested'; it triggers no scan. So the whole HygieneView page (KPI cards, severity sections, issue cards) is a UI shell rendering a constant.
- **User impact:** A user opens Hygiene expecting a health report on their session library. They always see Score 0 with a single info note saying checks aren't implemented. Clicking Refresh (HygieneView.swift:85-102) changes nothing meaningful. The page is functionally inert.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:810-828 (hygiene() returns the fixed placeholder issue + score 0; action = request.force ? "force-refresh requested" : nil). HygieneView.swift:189 calls serviceClient.hygiene(force:) and renders whatever comes back.
- **Suggested fix:** Either implement real hygiene checks in the service (orphaned children, empty sessions, stale detections, FTS gaps) so issues/score reflect the DB, or hide the Hygiene screen from navigation (Screen.swift:13/MainWindowView.swift:94-95) until it does real work, instead of shipping a placeholder that reports a fake score.
- **Verify:** confirmed — EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:810-828 hygiene() unconditionally builds a single hard-coded info issue (message 'Swift service hygiene checks are not implemented', detail explaining it is an explicit placeholder) and returns score: 0, checkedAt: currentTimestamp(). No DB query, no scan, no branching on database state. The force param only sets action = request.force ? "force-refresh requested" : nil (line 820) — pure string swap, no scan trigger. HygieneView.swift:189 (result = try await serviceClient.hygiene(force: force)) feeds this constant into the KPI cards (lines 54-61), severity sections (143-172), and IssueCard (282-356). The whole page renders a constant. Severity high is accurate: the surface is misleading (KPI 'Score 0' / 'Info: 1' looks like a real scan result). Confirmed.

#### `hygiene-4` · 🔴 High · Settings 'Hide empty/usage/auto-summary' toggles are dead controls — their flags are read by nothing

- **Surface:** Hygiene / cleanup workflow
- **What's wrong:** SettingsView shows three toggles ('Hide usage-check sessions', 'Hide empty sessions', 'Hide auto-summary prompts') with caption 'These are low-level filters behind the simplified Session Filter control.' That claim is false. The toggles only persist JSON keys (hideUsageSessions/hideEmptySessions/hideAutoSummary) via saveAdvancedSettings, and those keys are never read anywhere outside SettingsView. The actual Session Filter is driven by a separate string setting `noiseFilter` (all/hide-skip/hide-noise), which the toggles do not affect. The 'Hide empty sessions' toggle does NOT call the hideEmptySessions() command either.
- **User impact:** A user toggles 'Hide empty sessions' expecting empty sessions to disappear (or be hidden). Nothing happens — the toggle is purely cosmetic and the caption misleads them into thinking it feeds the Session Filter. This is the visible 'act on noise' control and it is inert.
- **Evidence:** Toggles + caption: SettingsView.swift:290-296. Flags only written: SettingsView.swift:450/515 (read into local @State, written back to JSON). The real filter is noiseFilter: SettingsView.swift:273-279, consumed in PopoverView.swift:227-229/344. Grep for hideUsageSessions/hideAutoSummary/"hideEmptySessions" outside SettingsView/tests returns only the service command name strings, never a query that honors these booleans.
- **Suggested fix:** Either wire these toggles into the actual filter/query path (or make 'Hide empty sessions' invoke serviceClient.hideEmptySessions()), or remove the dead toggles and the false 'low-level filters' caption so Settings doesn't promise filtering it doesn't do.
- **Verify:** confirmed — SettingsView.swift:288-298 'Noise Details' GroupBox has the three toggles (Hide usage-check / Hide empty / Hide auto-summary) with caption 'These are low-level filters behind the simplified Session Filter control.' (line 296). Grep confirms hideUsageSessions/hideAutoSummary/hideEmptySessions booleans are referenced ONLY in SettingsView (state declare, onChange->saveAdvancedSettings, load at 450, write at 515) — nothing reads them on the query path. The real filter is noiseFilter (SettingsView.swift:188/273-279), consumed in PopoverView.swift:227/229/344 (readNoiseFilter default 'hide-skip'). SessionsPageView uses showHiddenSessions/listSessions, also independent of these booleans. The caption's 'behind the Session Filter control' claim is false; the toggles persist dead JSON keys. The 'Hide empty sessions' toggle does not call hideEmptySessions() (confirmed in hygiene-3). All sub-claims verified. Severity high accurate (three visible controls that do nothing).

#### `observability-3` · 🔴 High · All log message bodies are logged with privacy: .private, so OSLogStore reads them back as redacted <private>

- **Surface:** Observability: logs / errors / perf / traces / health
- **What's wrong:** Every Engram log call interpolates the message with privacy: .private — EngramLogger.info/warn/error/debug (EngramLogger.swift:24,28,33,37) and ServiceLogger.debug/info/notice/warn/error (ServiceLogger.swift:29,33,37,41,46), plus the indexer call sites (e.g. SwiftIndexer.swift:79,161,212,241). OSLogReader reads log.composedMessage (OSLogReader.swift:84). A process reading the unified log without special entitlements receives <private> in place of any .private-interpolated value — which here is the ENTIRE message string. So even for the app's own (com.engram.app) entries that the currentProcess store can reach, the message column will display '<private>' rather than the actual text.
- **User impact:** Even when log entries are found, the Logs and Errors tabs render rows whose message text is '<private>' — the timestamps/levels/modules appear but the actual content is unreadable. The dashboard looks populated but conveys nothing actionable, which is worse than an honest empty state.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Core/EngramLogger.swift:24,28,33,37 (privacy: .private on whole message); macos/EngramService/Core/ServiceLogger.swift:29,33,37,41,46; OSLogReader reads composedMessage at macos/Engram/Core/OSLogReader.swift:84; redacted values surface in LogRow message (LogStreamView.swift:145) and ErrorDashboard message (ErrorDashboardView.swift:73)
- **Suggested fix:** Log the human-readable summary portion with privacy: .public (keeping only genuinely sensitive interpolations .private), or read the entries with a level that preserves the message. Otherwise the entire Logs/Errors surface is cosmetically populated but content-redacted.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified every logging call wraps the WHOLE message with privacy: .private: EngramLogger.info/warn/error/debug (EngramLogger.swift:24,28,33,37) and ServiceLogger.debug/info/notice/warn/error (ServiceLogger.swift:29,33,37,41,46). OSLogReader builds LogEntry.message from log.composedMessage (OSLogReader.swift:85), surfaced in LogRow (LogStreamView.swift:145) and ErrorDashboard recent-errors (ErrorDashboardView.swift:73). It is correct macOS behavior that a process reading the unified log without the private-data entitlement (which the app lacks, per finding 2) receives '<private>' for .private-interpolated values. Since the entire message string is interpolated .private, the message column renders '<private>' even for the reachable com.engram.app entries. The claim is accurate and self-consistent with the entitlements verified in finding 2. The tracer rated this 'misleading'; I keep severity high because combined with findings 2 and 4 the Log/Error/Health surfaces show structurally degraded, mostly-redacted, app-only data while presenting as full observability — the message bodies being the primary payload of a log viewer.

#### `onboarding-firstrun-5` · 🟠 Medium · Indexing-aware empty-state copy exists in the catalog but is wired to no view; real empty states are misleading

- **Surface:** First run / onboarding / zero-state
- **What's wrong:** The localization catalog defines 'Sessions will appear here after indexing' (Localizable.xcstrings:1460), which would correctly tell a first-run user to wait. But no Swift view references it (grep for the string and 'after indexing' across Engram/*.swift returns nothing). The actually-rendered first-run copy on the Sessions page is 'No sessions' / 'No sessions match your filters' (SessionsPageView.swift:62), which implies the user has applied a filter that excluded results — when in reality the index simply hasn't produced data yet.
- **User impact:** On first run with no filters applied, the user is told their (nonexistent) filters matched nothing, mislabeling an empty/indexing state as a filtering problem and obscuring the real reason the list is empty.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Resources/Localizable.xcstrings:1460 ('Sessions will appear here after indexing'); no Swift usage (grep 'after indexing' over Engram .swift files empty); macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:62 (the misleading 'No sessions match your filters')
- **Suggested fix:** Use the existing 'Sessions will appear here after indexing' copy for the no-filter / indexing case, and reserve 'No sessions match your filters' for when a filter is actually active.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. Localizable.xcstrings:1460 defines 'Sessions will appear here after indexing' (translated to zh-Hans '索引完成后，会话会显示在这里' at line 1461), but grep for 'after indexing' and 'Sessions will appear here' across all Engram/ and Shared/ .swift files returns ZERO references — the string is orphaned, wired to no view. The actually-rendered first-run copy is SessionsPageView.swift:62 EmptyState(title: 'No sessions', message: 'No sessions match your filters'), which is misleading when the index simply hasn't produced data yet (the page gates this branch only on 'sessions.isEmpty && !isLoading', never on .starting status). Medium severity is appropriate — a misleading-copy/dead-string issue, the correct copy already exists and just needs wiring.

#### `replay-3` · 🟠 Medium · Replay omits tool calls entirely — only user/assistant messages are ever shown

- **Surface:** Session replay
- **What's wrong:** The replay timeline is built from sessions_fts, whose content is produced by buildSearchContent, which explicitly skips any message that is not .user or .assistant (`guard message.role == .user || message.role == .assistant else { continue }`). Tool-call/tool-result messages are therefore never indexed into FTS and can never appear in the replay. Yet the replay UI advertises tool support: replayRoleAndPreview checks a "Tool:" prefix and roleColor() has a tool branch — both unreachable.
- **User impact:** A user replaying an agentic session (lots of tool calls) sees a conversation with all the tool activity removed, so the replay misrepresents what actually happened in the session and silently drops the most informative steps.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/IndexJobRunner.swift:207 (filters to user/assistant only); replay's unreachable tool handling at macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:920 ("Tool:" branch) and macos/Engram/Views/Replay/SessionReplayView.swift:229 (tool color)
- **Suggested fix:** Either source replay from the full message stream (including tool messages) rather than FTS, or document that replay is conversation-only; remove the dead "Tool:" handling if tool messages are intentionally excluded.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified. buildSearchContent (EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/IndexJobRunner.swift:207) does guard message.role == .user || .assistant else continue, so tool-call/tool-result messages are never written into sessions_fts. Replay reads exclusively from sessions_fts (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:649), so tool entries can never appear. The 'Tool:' prefix branch (:920) and the tool color branch (SessionReplayView.swift:229) are unreachable dead code. Note: because replay-1 already makes everything render as 'unknown' with the default tool color, the practical 'omits tool calls' point stands. Medium upheld.

#### `projects-migration-4` · 🟠 Medium · UI repeatedly directs users to an `engram` CLI that does not ship with the app

- **Surface:** Projects: move / rename / archive / undo / history
- **What's wrong:** Multiple error/guidance strings in the Projects flow tell the user to drop to a CLI: RenameSheet shows 'Use `engram project move` from the CLI with an explicit path' when no cwd is recorded (RenameSheet.swift:81) and 'Run `engram project review <old> <new>` from the CLI' for residual refs (RenameSheet.swift:397); ArchiveSheet shows 'Run `engram project review` from the CLI' (ArchiveSheet.swift:177); UndoSheet shows 'Run `engram project review` from CLI to inspect' (UndoSheet.swift:314). But no `engram` CLI binary ships: package.json has no `bin` field, there is no bin/ directory, and project.yml defines no CLI install/symlink. The `engram project review` surface is TypeScript dev/reference tooling per CLAUDE.md, not a user-installed command.
- **User impact:** When a rename/archive/undo leaves residual references (a real, surfaced outcome the UI even has dedicated warning boxes for), or when a project has no recorded cwd, the only remediation the app offers is a command the user almost certainly cannot run. The user hits a true dead-end: the GUI says 'go fix it in the CLI', but there is no CLI to go to. This actively misleads and blocks completing the workflow.
- **Evidence:** CLI-deferral copy: macos/Engram/Views/Projects/RenameSheet.swift:81 & 397, macos/Engram/Views/Projects/ArchiveSheet.swift:177, macos/Engram/Views/Projects/UndoSheet.swift:314; No shipping CLI: package.json has no "bin" field, no bin/ directory exists, project.yml defines no engram CLI install
- **Suggested fix:** Either ship/install an `engram` CLI and document it, or replace the CLI deferrals with an in-app 'Review residual references' action backed by the existing projectReview/projectRecover backend (already implemented in EngramMCP/MCPFileTools.projectReview and MCPDatabase.projectRecover), so remediation stays inside the app.
- **Verify:** partial — The four CLI-deferral strings exist verbatim: RenameSheet.swift:81 ('Use `engram project move` from the CLI'), RenameSheet.swift:397 ('Run `engram project review <old> <new>` from the CLI'), ArchiveSheet.swift:177, UndoSheet.swift:314. The tracer's premise ('no engram CLI binary ships; package.json has no bin, no bin/ dir') is mostly right about the Node side but MISSES a Swift CLI target: project.yml:217-231 defines an EngramCLI tool target (com.engram.cli). However that target does NOT refute the finding — I read EngramCLI/main.swift (102 lines): it only parses a `resume` subcommand (EngramCLIResumeOptions/EngramCLIResumeCommand in Shared/Service/EngramCLIResumeCommand.swift) and otherwise execs into the EngramMCP stdio helper. Grep for a 'project'/'move'/'review' ParsableCommand/CommandConfiguration in EngramCLI/ returns nothing — there is no `engram project move` or `engram project review` subcommand in the shipped Swift CLI. Additionally EngramCLI has SKIP_INSTALL: YES (project.yml:231) and no script symlinks it as `engram` into PATH. So the UI directs users to commands no shipped binary provides. Core claim (misleading CLI guidance) stands; I mark it partial only because the supporting evidence ('no engram CLI at all') is imprecise — an engram-adjacent CLI binary exists, it just lacks these subcommands. Severity high→medium: misleading dead-end copy in fallback/error states, but the primary happy-path actions (rename/archive/undo) work in-app; the CLI text only appears in edge cases (no recorded cwd, residual refs).

#### `sources-sync-5` · 🟠 Medium · Windsurf/Antigravity show as normal sources with no honest 'live sync disabled' status

- **Surface:** Sources: enable/disable + trigger sync
- **What's wrong:** Both adapters are constructed with enableLiveSync:false (Windsurf is cache-only, Antigravity reads brain transcripts / legacy cache), per CLAUDE.md and the adapter factory. Neither the SourcesSettingsSection list nor the SourcePulseView dashboard communicates this. In Settings they appear as ordinary rows with a green path-exists dot (implying 'working'); in the Pulse dashboard they only appear if sessions were already indexed, with the same generic health badges as fully-live sources. A user has no way to learn that live capture is intentionally off for these two and that data is limited to cached/transcript content.
- **User impact:** A Windsurf/Antigravity user assumes their latest sessions are being captured live like Claude Code, sees a green dot or 'healthy' badge, and is silently missing recent data — a trust gap.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Core/MessageParser.swift:128-129 (WindsurfAdapter/AntigravityAdapter enableLiveSync:false); macos/Shared/EngramCore/Adapters/SessionAdapterFactory.swift:25-26 (same); macos/Engram/Views/Settings/SourcesSettingsSection.swift:25-26 (Windsurf/Antigravity rows identical to all others, no live-sync indicator); SourcePulseView healthBadge :287-304 (no live-vs-cache distinction)
- **Suggested fix:** Surface an explicit per-source mode (e.g. a 'Cache only' / 'Live sync off' tag) on both the Settings row and the Pulse health line for Windsurf and Antigravity.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. MessageParser.swift:128-129 and SessionAdapterFactory.swift:25-26 (and 70-71) construct WindsurfAdapter/AntigravityAdapter with enableLiveSync:false. In SourcesSettingsSection.swift:25-26 the Windsurf/Antigravity rows are structurally identical to all other sources (name + path + green/red PathExistsIndicator) — a green dot implies 'working' with no live-vs-cache distinction. SourcePulseView healthBadge (lines 287-304) only maps critical/healthy/attention/partial/empty, with no live-vs-cache field. Grep for 'live sync|cache-only|cache only|transcript-only|live capture|liveSync' across both Sources surface files returned zero matches, confirming neither surface communicates that live capture is intentionally off for these two. Medium severity (misleading) is appropriate.

#### `settings-general-3` · 🟠 Medium · 'MCP HTTP endpoint' row shows a wrong/non-existent URL (http://host:3457/mcp)

- **Surface:** Settings: General / Network / About
- **What's wrong:** General > Runtime Infrastructure renders mcpEndpointText as `http://<host>:<port>/mcp` using serviceStatusStore.endpointPort (GeneralSettingsSection.swift:74-82,126-132). But endpointPort is the WEB UI port (3457), and the web server (EngramWebUIServer) exposes only `/`, `/session/:id`, and `/health` — there is no `/mcp` route. The product MCP is stdio-only (EngramMCP/main.swift runs MCPStdioServer; no HTTP listener exists). So the displayed 'MCP HTTP endpoint' points at a URL that 404s and conflates the web UI port with a non-existent HTTP MCP server.
- **User impact:** A user trying to wire an MCP client copies http://127.0.0.1:3457/mcp and it does not work — that path is not served and MCP is not HTTP. The setting actively misinforms anyone configuring MCP integration.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Settings/GeneralSettingsSection.swift:74-82 (row), :126-132 (text = http://host:port/mcp from endpointPort); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramWebUIServer.swift:62-79 (only /, /session/:id, /health routes; port 3457 at :93-94); macos/EngramMCP/main.swift:31-36 (MCPStdioServer — stdio only, no HTTP).
- **Suggested fix:** Remove the '/mcp' suffix and the 'MCP HTTP endpoint' label, or replace the row with the real stdio MCP invocation (the EngramMCP binary path). Do not derive an MCP endpoint from the web UI port.
- **Verify:** confirmed — GeneralSettingsSection.swift:126-131 builds mcpEndpointText as `http://<host>:<port>/mcp` from serviceStatusStore.endpointPort. That endpointPort is exclusively the WEB UI port populated by web_ready (EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:81-83), and the web server binds port 3457 with ONLY routes `/`, `/session/:id`, `/health` (EngramWebUIServer.swift:62-79) — no `/mcp` route (grep for /mcp in EngramService/EngramMCP finds only `actor:"mcp"` strings, no route registration). The product MCP is stdio-only: EngramMCP/main.swift:31-36 runs `MCPStdioServer()`, and grep for any Hummingbird/HTTPServer/listen/bind in EngramMCP finds none — its only network transport is a Unix socket (MCPConfig.swift). So the row labels a web-UI port + nonexistent /mcp path as an 'MCP HTTP endpoint' that 404s. Confirmed; medium is fair (misleading label, but only visible when web UI is enabled).

#### `settings-general-4` · 🟠 Medium · Network section's only functional toggle (Strict single writer) is a no-op in the shipped product

- **Surface:** Settings: General / Network / About
- **What's wrong:** NetworkSettingsSection's 'Strict single writer' toggle persists `mcpStrictSingleWriter` to settings.json (NetworkSettingsSection.swift:31-32,60-65) and its help text claims 'remaining MCP write tools such as save_insight also fail if the Swift service can't be reached... Takes effect on the next Swift MCP spawn.' But the value is read by NOTHING in the Swift product — grep finds readers only in the legacy TypeScript src/index.ts (the Node MCP that CLAUDE.md states is removed from the product path). The shipped Swift EngramMCP (MCPToolRegistry, MCPInsightsTool, etc.) never reads mcpStrictSingleWriter.
- **User impact:** The only switch in Network that looks operational does nothing in the actual app, while its description explicitly promises behavior ('takes effect on next Swift MCP spawn') that no Swift code implements. A user toggling it for safety gets a false sense of a guarantee that isn't enforced.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Settings/NetworkSettingsSection.swift:31-33,60-65; grep for `mcpStrictSingleWriter`/`strictSingleWriter` across macos --include=*.swift returns ONLY NetworkSettingsSection.swift; the only functional readers are in src/index.ts / src/core/config.ts (TypeScript reference/legacy Node MCP, removed from product per CLAUDE.md 'Service Runtime').
- **Suggested fix:** Either implement the strict-single-writer gate in the Swift EngramMCP write path (reading mcpStrictSingleWriter at spawn) or remove the toggle and its claim from NetworkSettingsSection until the Swift behavior exists.
- **Verify:** confirmed — NetworkSettingsSection.swift:31-33 toggles `mcpStrictSingleWriter`, saved to settings.json at line 63 and loaded at line 50. A whole-tree grep (case-insensitive) for strictsinglewriter/single.writer across .swift finds the symbol `mcpStrictSingleWriter` ONLY in NetworkSettingsSection.swift; all other 'single-writer' hits are about the ServiceWriterGate lock (a different concept) or test strings. No Swift MCP code (MCPToolRegistry/MCPInsightsTool/MCPConfig) reads it. MCPConfig.swift:8-21 (the MCP startup config) loads only dbPath + serviceSocketPath; no strict-writer branch. The help text promises behavior 'on the next Swift MCP spawn,' but the Swift MCP never consults the flag — only the legacy TS src/index.ts did. Confirmed no-op toggle; medium is appropriate.

- **What's wrong:** The page is titled "Timeline" with a bar-chart icon (`chart.bar.xaxis`) and a "30d" badge, but the body renders no chart at all. The header at :55 uses icon 'chart.bar.xaxis', title 'Timeline', badge '30d', setting a chart visual-language expectation. ExpandableSessionCard.swift renders no inline chart/sparkline/graphic (grep for Sparkline/BarMark/Chart()/import Charts returned nothing), so cards are plain expandable rows with no clickable bars/points/hover-to-inspect. By contrast ActivityView.swift:27,31 genuinely renders ActivityChart and HeatmapGrid. TimelinePageView is referenced only once (MainWindowView.swift:89) with no chart-rendering wrapper. Severity medium is appropriate: it is a misleading visual-language gap, not a functional/security defect.

#### `search-3` · 🟡 Low · Embedding-status pill advertises semantic capability the UI can never invoke

- **Surface:** Keyword search → results → open
- **What's wrong:** When embeddingStatus().available is true, SearchPageView renders a green dot plus 'N/M embedded' (SearchPageView.swift:160-167). The real service provider reports `available: embedded > 0` (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:696), so if any historical session_embeddings rows exist in ~/.engram/index.sqlite, this pill lights up. But availableModes is hardcoded to [.keyword] (SearchSupport.swift:9-11), so the user can never run a semantic/embedding-powered search. The pill therefore signals an embedding-search capability that has no UI path. The service does at least surface a warning string when a semantic mode is requested over IPC (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:440-441), but the UI never requests that mode, so the user only sees the encouraging 'embedded' count with no way to act on it.
- **User impact:** A user with legacy embedding rows sees 'embedded' progress and reasonably expects semantic search, but there is no control to use it — the product is keyword-only. The indicator promises something the app cannot deliver.
- **Evidence:** SearchPageView.swift:160-167 (green dot + 'N/M embedded' shown when available); EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:696 (available: embedded > 0 — reachable when legacy embedding rows exist); SearchSupport.swift:9-11 (no semantic mode ever offered)
- **Suggested fix:** Hide the embedding-status pill (and the embeddingStatus() call) until semantic search actually ships, or relabel it so it does not imply an available search capability (e.g. omit it entirely in the keyword-only product).
- **Verify:** partial — The literal claim is accurate but the severity is overstated. Verified the pill chain: SearchPageView.swift:160-167 renders the green dot + 'N/M embedded' when embeddingStatus.available is true; loadEmbeddingStatus (line 481) calls serviceClient.embeddingStatus() -> EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:676/696 which returns available: embedded > 0 by COUNT(DISTINCT session_id) on session_embeddings (lines 688-693). And availableModes is hardcoded [.keyword] (SearchSupport.swift:9-11) so there is indeed no UI to run a semantic search; the service only surfaces the warning over IPC (lines 440-441) for a mode the UI never requests. HOWEVER, reachability is narrow: grep across EngramCoreWrite/EngramCoreRead/EngramService/Shared shows NO INSERT/upsert into session_embeddings anywhere — the Swift product only DELETEs from it (SessionSnapshotWriter.swift:602, StartupBackfills.swift:731/758, VectorRebuildPolicy.swift:35) and, critically, FTSRebuildPolicy.swift:35-37 (wired into the migration runner) DELETEs ALL session_embeddings rows whenever the FTS rebuild version advances. So in a normal/fresh install embedded==0 and the pill never shows; it can only light up from leftover legacy TypeScript-era rows that survive until the next FTS rebuild wipes them. Misleading-state cosmetic issue with low real-world exposure -> low, not medium.

#### `session-detail-transcript-4` · 🟡 Low · currentMatchIndex is not reset when the query changes, leaving a stale position

- **Surface:** Open session → read transcript → find-in-page
- **What's wrong:** `currentMatchIndex` is reset to -1 only on session switch (SessionDetailView.swift:427), never when `searchText` changes. The match-scan token re-runs on query change (SessionDetailView.swift:134,459) and replaces `matchIndices`, but `currentMatchIndex` keeps its previous value. The find bar masks this by clamping the *displayed* number via `displayedFindMatchIndex` (SessionDetailView.swift:684-687), yet the next Prev/Next press computes from the stale `currentMatchIndex` (SessionDetailView.swift:689-695): e.g. you were on match 9/20 of query A, retype to query B with 3 matches; the label clamps to 3/3, and pressing Next wraps you to 1/3 instead of starting from the top of the new result set. The position is decoupled from the matches it indexes.
- **User impact:** After changing the search term, the first Next/Prev press jumps to an arbitrary position relative to the new matches rather than the top, so navigation order feels unpredictable.
- **Evidence:** SessionDetailView.swift:427 (currentMatchIndex reset only per-session); SessionDetailView.swift:134,459 (matchScanToken re-runs scan on query change, rebuilding matchIndices); SessionDetailView.swift:684-695 (displayed index clamped, but navigateFind reads raw currentMatchIndex)
- **Suggested fix:** In updateMatchIndicesDebounced (or an onChange of searchText), reset currentMatchIndex to -1 when the query string changes so navigation restarts from the first match of the new result set.
- **Verify:** partial — Mechanism confirmed: `currentMatchIndex` is reset to -1 only on session switch (SessionDetailView.swift:427); there is NO onChange(of: searchText) (grep of all onChange in the file shows only scrollTarget/typeVisibility/showSystemPrompts/showAgentComm at lines 380,456,457,458). The match scan re-runs on query change and replaces matchIndices (matchScanToken, line 134; task, line 459) while currentMatchIndex keeps its stale value, masked by `displayedFindMatchIndex` clamping (lines 217-220, 684-687). The position is indeed decoupled. HOWEVER the headline example is wrong: with stale current=9 and new count=3, pressing Next computes nextNavPosition(9,+1,3)=`(min(9,2)+1)%3`=0 → lands on index 0 (the TOP of the new set), which is correct, not a bug. The real artifact is subtler: pressing Prev computes nextNavPosition(9,-1,3)=`min(9,2)-1`=1 → lands on 2/3 (a stale-derived middle position) instead of the last/first, and the pre-navigation label shows a clamped '3/3' that corresponds to no real selection. So the decoupling is real but the visible impact is a single mildly-wrong Prev landing plus a transient meaningless label — not the wrap-to-wrong-place described. Downgrading to low: overstated example, small real residual issue.

#### `replay-5` · 🟡 Low · Session summary is appended as a phantom final 'message' in the replay timeline

- **Surface:** Session replay
- **What's wrong:** buildSearchContent appends the session summary as an extra FTS content line after the real messages. Replay reads FTS rows in rowid order and treats each as a timeline entry, so the summary becomes an additional trailing entry indistinguishable from a real message — labeled "Unknown" (no role prefix) and counted in the progress indicator (e.g. shows N+1 / N+1).
- **User impact:** At the end of replay the user hits an extra entry that is the auto-generated summary, presented as if it were the last thing said in the session, and the message count is inflated by one. Minor but confusing.
- **Evidence:** macos/EngramCoreWrite/Indexing/IndexJobRunner.swift:212-215 (appends summary to contents); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:646-664 (each FTS row → one replay entry, ORDER BY rowid); progress label macos/Engram/Models/ReplayState.swift:51-53
- **Suggested fix:** Exclude the summary line from the replay timeline query (e.g. tag summary rows or source replay from messages rather than FTS), so replay reflects only real conversation turns.

- **What's wrong:** The dataSources array in SourcesSettingsSection is a hand-maintained list of 18 entries that has drifted from the actual adapter registration. - **Suggested fix:** Drive the Settings list from the same adapter source-of-truth (SessionAdapterFactory) instead of a hand-edited array, so it cannot drift.

- **What's wrong:** WorkGraphView is named 'Work Graph', uses the graph icon `point.3.connected.trianglepath.dotted`, and its empty state says 'Work Graph builds as repos are discovered'. Caveat that slightly lowers severity: the visible SectionHeader title at :32 reads 'Repo Activity' (not 'Work Graph'), so within the screen the bar-chart content is labeled honestly; only the screen/tab name, icon, and empty-state copy carry the misleading 'graph' framing. This is a naming/iconography mismatch with no functional breakage or dead-end, so it is a low-severity cosmetic/expectation issue rather than medium.

#### `workspace-repos-3` · 🟡 Low · Related-sessions matching over-matches by project substring (LIKE %name%), surfacing unrelated repos' sessions

- **Surface:** Workspace: Repos / RepoDetail / WorkGraph
- **What's wrong:** RepoDetailView loads related sessions via `db.getContext(cwd: repo.path)`. getContext derives `project = URL(fileURLWithPath: cwd).lastPathComponent` and matches `project LIKE %project% ` — a substring match. A repo named 'app' (or 'web', 'api', 'core') will match sessions whose project is 'myapp', 'app-v2', 'webhook', etc. So the 'Recent Sessions' shown under a repo can include sessions from entirely different repos that merely share a path-component substring. The cwd-LIKE fallback only runs when the project match returns empty, so the over-broad project match usually wins.
- **User impact:** Users with short/common repo names see sessions that don't belong to that repo listed as its 'Recent Sessions', undermining trust in the drill-down's accuracy.
- **Evidence:** /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Workspace/RepoDetailView.swift:138 (getContext(cwd: path)); /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Core/Database.swift:611-622 — `project LIKE '%\(project)%'` where project is just `lastPathComponent`.
- **Suggested fix:** Prefer exact cwd-prefix matching for the repo drill-down (e.g. `cwd LIKE repo.path || '%'`, consistent with sparklineData at Database.swift:1026) instead of the fuzzy project substring, or add a dedicated repo-scoped query rather than reusing the general getContext heuristic.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed at the source. RepoDetailView.swift:138 calls db.getContext(cwd: path, limit: 10). Database.swift:611-616: project = URL(fileURLWithPath: cwd).lastPathComponent, then `WHERE project LIKE ?` with arguments ['%project%'] — an unanchored substring match, so a repo named 'app' matches projects 'myapp','app-v2', etc. :617-620 the cwd LIKE fallback only runs when the project match returns empty (results.isEmpty), so when the broad project match yields rows it wins — exactly as claimed. The bug is real but bounded in impact: it only affects which sessions appear in the read-only 'Recent Sessions' list (advisory context), produces no data corruption, and in practice lastPathComponent collisions are uncommon and the limit is 10. Given low blast radius and that the surfaced rows are currently non-interactive anyway (see finding 1), low severity is more appropriate than medium.

#### `xc-deadends-6` · 🟡 Low · Observability has 5 tabs but Performance and Traces are permanently inert panels

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** ObservabilityView presents a 5-tab segmented control (Logs, Errors, Performance, Traces, Health). Two of the five — Performance and Traces — are hardcoded EmptyState panels that always state the data is not collected, because the Swift runtime emits no spans/metrics (os_log only). They can never show content. The honest copy is good, but the product still advertises 40% of its Observability surface as tabs the user can select that structurally do nothing.
- **User impact:** Users click into Performance and Traces expecting metrics and instead always hit a 'not collected' wall — two tabs that look like features but are placeholders, making the Observability section feel half-finished.
- **Evidence:** Tabs defined at macos/Engram/Views/Pages/ObservabilityView.swift:5-11 (logs/errors/performance/traces/health). PerformanceView is a pure EmptyState 'Performance metrics not collected' (macos/Engram/Views/Observability/PerformanceView.swift:11-26). TraceExplorerView is a pure EmptyState 'Tracing not collected' (macos/Engram/Views/Observability/TraceExplorerView.swift:11-26); its TraceEntry/HourlyMetric models (:51-82) are defined but unused by any read path.
- **Suggested fix:** Hide the Performance and Traces tabs until span/metric instrumentation exists (gate them on a capability flag), rather than offering selectable tabs that can only show 'not collected'.
- **Verify:** partial — The structural facts are confirmed but the framing 'inert panels that do nothing' is overstated. ObservabilityView.swift:5-11 defines a 5-tab segmented control (logs/errors/performance/traces/health) and :32-35 routes Performance->PerformanceView, Traces->TraceExplorerView. PerformanceView.swift:11-26 and TraceExplorerView.swift:11-26 are indeed pure EmptyState views with NO read path. The models claim is mostly right: TraceEntry/HourlyMetric (TraceExplorerView.swift:51-82) are referenced only by Database.swift read methods fetchTraces/slowTraces/recentHourlyMetrics (:1239/:1271/:1300), and grep confirms those three read methods have ZERO callers anywhere in Engram/ or Shared/ — so they ARE effectively orphaned/dead read paths, supporting 'unused by any read path' in practice. BUT the tabs are NOT structurally broken or misleading: both panels show explicit, honest EmptyState copy explaining the runtime emits no spans/metrics ('Performance metrics not collected' / 'Tracing not collected', with the OBS-C1 comments documenting this was a deliberate fix to a previously-misleading false-empty view). The user is clearly told why the tab is empty. So this is a minor product-completeness nit (two advertised tabs that can never show data) — not a dead-end or no-op bug. Downgrading medium->low; the honest disclosure substantially mitigates it, and the dead trace read methods are flag-worthy dead code (pre-existing, not introduced).

#### `xc-capability-matrix-8` · 🟡 Low · triggerSync is a stub that always returns 'not implemented' (no app UI calls it, and it would fail if it did)

- **Surface:** X-cut: backend capability ↔ UI exposure matrix
- **What's wrong:** triggerSync has zero app call sites, AND its service handler is a hardcoded failure returning ok:false / error:'Sync is not implemented in the Swift service'. So even the MCP-exposed sync path is non-functional. No app sync/refresh-now button targets it (the only 'Refresh' buttons reload local data: HygieneView refresh calls hygiene; SourcePulseView refresh reloads liveSessions). This is dead backend surface, not a real capability.
