Handler stub: EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:796-808 always returns ok:false error:'Sync is not implemented in the Swift service'. Local refresh buttons unrelated: HygieneView.swift:95 (hygiene), SourcePulseView.swift:63 (loadLiveSessions).
- **Suggested fix:** Either implement sync or remove triggerSync from the protocol/MCP surface so it doesn't present as an available capability.

### Missing empty/loading/error states (25)

#### `onboarding-firstrun-2` · 🟠 Medium · No 'first index in progress' state — empty DB looks identical to 'no data found'

- **Surface:** First run / onboarding / zero-state
- **What's wrong:** After onboarding completes, the service auto-started at launch (App.swift:127-151) begins the first index, which for a real user can take a while. During that window the main surfaces cannot distinguish 'indexing not finished yet' from 'genuinely empty'. HomeView shows SkeletonRow only while kpi==nil (HomeView.swift:81-85); as soon as the still-empty DB returns 0 it flips to terminal empty states 'No recent work' / 'No follow-ups found' / 'No project activity' (HomeView.swift:107-180). SessionsPageView shows 'No sessions' / 'No sessions match your filters' (SessionsPageView.swift:61-63). None of these views read serviceStatusStore.status for a .starting/indexing case — grep shows the pages only consult isRunning, never .starting.
- **User impact:** A brand-new user opens Engram while the first index is still running and is told they have 'No sessions' / 'No recent work' — making the app look empty/broken precisely when it is actually working. They may quit before indexing finishes.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:81-85,107-113,140-145,174-179; macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:61-63; status .starting handling absent in pages (only isRunning used at HomeView.swift:60,205,237)
- **Suggested fix:** When serviceStatusStore.status == .starting (or totalSessions==0 and the service hasn't reported a completed index yet), render an 'Indexing your sessions…' state with a spinner instead of the terminal empty states.
- **Verify:** partial — Partly confirmed, partly refuted. CONFIRMED: HomeView's three workbench panels show terminal empty copy during first-run indexing — 'No recent work' (HomeView.swift:107-113), 'No follow-ups found' (140-145), 'No project activity' (174-179) all gate ONLY on '&& !isLoading' where isLoading is the local DB-query flag (line 22,248), never on serviceStatusStore.status .starting. SessionsPageView.swift:61-63 same pattern. REFUTED part: the claim 'empty DB looks identical to no data found' is overstated. EngramServiceStatusStore HAS a distinct .starting case rendering 'Starting...' and .running rendering '\(total) sessions indexed' (EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:40-53, 64-71). HomeView surfaces this in TWO places a first-run user sees: the header ServiceStatusPill (HomeView.swift:59-62, displayString) and the Service State panel 'Indexer' row (line 204-209). App.swift:128 applies .starting at launch. Also '.task(id: serviceStatusStore.totalSessions)' (HomeView.swift:41, SessionsPageView.swift:98) re-runs loadData as indexed counts grow, so panels self-refresh. So there IS an indexing signal, just not inside the empty-state panels. Real but narrower gap; downgrade high->medium.

#### `onboarding-firstrun-3` · 🟠 Medium · Menu-bar popover shows a blank timeline area with no empty state for a zero-data user

- **Surface:** First run / onboarding / zero-state
- **What's wrong:** The menu-bar popover is the most likely first surface a new user clicks after onboarding. Its timelineSection iterates groupedByDate(recentSessions) inside a ScrollView with no fallback: when recentSessions is empty it renders an empty VStack — no 'no sessions yet' / 'indexing' message, unlike the main window pages which at least use EmptyState. PopoverView contains no EmptyState usage at all (not in the EmptyState user list).
- **User impact:** A new user clicking the menu-bar icon sees an empty void where activity should be, with no indication that indexing is pending or that no data exists yet.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/PopoverView.swift:136-152 (ScrollView { ForEach(groups)… } with no empty branch); PopoverView.swift absent from the list of files using EmptyState
- **Suggested fix:** Add an empty/indexing placeholder in PopoverView.timelineSection when recentSessions.isEmpty, mirroring the main window's EmptyState (and the .starting status case).
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed exactly as stated. PopoverView.swift:136-152 timelineSection = ScrollView { VStack { ForEach(groupedByDate(recentSessions)) {...} } } with NO else/empty branch — when recentSessions is empty, groupedByDate returns [] (lines 315-335) and ForEach renders nothing, leaving a blank scroll region. grep confirms PopoverView.swift has 0 occurrences of 'EmptyState', while 14 other views use EmptyState (HomeView, SessionsPageView, SearchPageView, ProjectsView, TimelinePageView, etc.; component defined at Engram/Components/EmptyState.swift). No 'indexing'/'no sessions yet' fallback in the popover. Severity medium is appropriate — it is a cosmetic zero-state gap on the menu-bar surface, not a broken workflow.

#### `session-detail-transcript-3` · 🟠 Medium · Entering a query shows a match count but never scrolls to the first match

- **Surface:** Open session → read transcript → find-in-page
- **What's wrong:** When the user types in the find field, the off-main scan populates `matchIndices` and the bar shows e.g. "0/12" (TranscriptFindBar.swift:40-44, currentMatch derived from `displayedFindMatchIndex` which clamps to 0). But nothing sets `scrollTarget` on query entry — `scrollTarget` is only assigned inside `navigateFind` (SessionDetailView.swift:699) and `navigateType` (SessionDetailView.swift:666). The match-scan task `updateMatchIndicesDebounced` only updates `matchIndices`, never `scrollTarget` or `currentMatchIndex` (SessionDetailView.swift:141-154). So a user typing a query sees a count but the transcript view stays where it was; they must press Next to move to the first hit.
- **User impact:** User searches for a term, sees '12 matches', but the view doesn't move to any of them — it looks like the highlighted match might be off-screen, so the find feels half-wired until they press the next arrow.
- **Evidence:** SessionDetailView.swift:141-154 (scan updates only matchIndices); SessionDetailView.swift:689-701 (scrollTarget set only in navigateFind); SessionDetailView.swift:459 (.task(id: matchScanToken) only calls updateMatchIndicesDebounced)
- **Suggested fix:** After a scan that yields matches with a fresh query, auto-select the first match: set currentMatchIndex=0 and scrollTarget to displayIndexed[matchIndices[0]].id so the view jumps to the first hit on type, matching native find behavior.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified. The match-scan path `updateMatchIndicesDebounced` assigns only `matchIndices` (SessionDetailView.swift:143,153) and never `scrollTarget` or `currentMatchIndex`. `.task(id: matchScanToken)` (SessionDetailView.swift:459) calls only that function. `scrollTarget` is written in exactly 3 places (grep-confirmed): reset to nil on session switch (line 429), navigateType (line 666), navigateFind (line 699) — none triggered by typing. So typing a query updates the count but does not scroll the transcript to the first hit; the user must press Next. (In Session mode inline highlighting does appear via ColorBarMessageView, but the view does not auto-scroll to bring the first match into view, which is the claim.) Medium is fair.

#### `settings-ai-2` · 🟠 Medium · 'Regenerate All' titles reports only 'started' and never shows progress or completion

- **Surface:** Settings: AI / embeddings / generation
- **What's wrong:** The 'Regenerate All' button calls serviceClient.regenerateAllTitles(), which returns immediately with status 'started' (the backend runs in a detached background task). The button maps that to TitleRegenerationStatus.service("started"), rendered as 'Service status: started'. The backend does emit progress (completed=/total=) but only via os_log (ServiceLogger.notice), never back to the UI. There is no polling, no progress bar, and no terminal 'completed/N titles updated' state in the view. The status label is left showing 'Service status: started' indefinitely.
- **User impact:** After clicking Regenerate All, the user sees 'Service status: started' and nothing else — no spinner, no count, no 'done'. They cannot tell whether titles are being regenerated, how far along it is, or when it finished. Titles silently change in other views with no feedback here.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Settings/AISettingsSection.swift:283-300 (button sets .queued then .service(response.status) and stops); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:1081-1099 (returns status:"started" synchronously, work runs in background); :1113-1132 (progress + completion only logged via ServiceLogger, not returned to caller)
- **Suggested fix:** Poll a status/progress command (or surface the existing completed/total progress through the service status events) and update the label to a real terminal state like 'Updated N titles' or a progress indicator, instead of leaving 'started' as the final message.
- **Verify:** confirmed — AISettingsSection.swift:283-300: the Regenerate All button sets titleRegenerateStatus=.queued, awaits serviceClient.regenerateAllTitles(), then sets .service(response.status) and stops — no polling loop. TitleRegenerationStatus.service renders 'Service status: <status>' (AISettingsSection.swift:530-531). Backend EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:1081-1099 returns status 'started' (or 'running') synchronously while regenerateAllTitlesInBackground runs detached (line 1084-1086). Progress (lines 1113-1120) and completion 'completed total=N' (line 1132) are emitted ONLY via ServiceLogger.notice (os_log), never returned to the caller. EngramServiceRegenerateTitlesResponse carries only status/total/message with no progress channel back to UI, and the status store has no title-regeneration progress field/event. So the label is left at 'Service status: started' with no terminal completion or progress bar. Confirmed; medium is correct (cosmetic/missing-state, not a functional break — the regeneration does complete in the background).

#### `xc-states-1` · 🟠 Medium · ActivityView has no empty state and no loading state — fresh installs see a misleading all-zeros dashboard

- **Surface:** X-cut: empty / loading / error state consistency
- **What's wrong:** ActivityView is the only metrics page that renders its KPI cards, ActivityChart, HeatmapGrid and 'By Source' list unconditionally, with no `isLoading` branch and no empty-state branch. The `isLoading` flag is set (line 12, 52-53) but never read in `body`. While data is loading, and on a fresh install / empty DB, the page shows KPI cards reading '0 / 0 / 0', a blank ActivityChart (which renders an empty HStack on empty data — ActivityChart.swift has no empty guard), an empty HeatmapGrid, and an empty source list — with no skeleton and no 'No activity yet' message. Compare to HomeView (SkeletonRow at line 83) and HygieneView (skeletonSection at 34-35, emptyState at 36-37) which both handle these states.
- **User impact:** A new user (or any user whose service is still indexing) opens the Activity page and sees a fully-rendered dashboard of zeros and blank charts that looks broken or implies they have no history, instead of a 'loading' or 'no activity yet' affordance. There's no signal that data is on its way.
- **Evidence:** /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/ActivityView.swift:15-49 (body has no `if isLoading` and no `if dailyActivity.isEmpty` branch; isLoading set at :52-53 is never read); ActivityChart renders nothing on empty data at /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Components/ActivityChart.swift:13-31
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror HygieneView: wrap the body content in `if isLoading { SkeletonRow×N } else if dailyActivity.isEmpty && todayCount == 0 { EmptyState(icon:"chart.bar", title:"No activity yet", message:"Indexed sessions will appear here") } else { ...existing... }`. The loadError AlertBanner at :18-19 already covers the error case.
- **Verify:** partial — Core claim CONFIRMED: ActivityView.swift body (15-49) never reads isLoading (so no skeleton) and has no `if dailyActivity.isEmpty` empty-state branch, unlike siblings HomeView (SkeletonRow at :83, EmptyState at :108/:141/:175) and HygieneView (skeletonSection at :35/:108, emptyState at :37/:121). isLoading is set at :52-53 but indeed never read in body. ActivityChart.swift (10-33) has no empty guard and renders an empty HStack on empty data. KPICard.swift (12) renders `value` verbatim, so fresh-install KPIs do read '0'. HOWEVER the finding is OVERSTATED on two points: (1) it repeatedly frames ActivityView as having 'no feedback', but ActivityView DOES handle the error state — loadError @State at :13, AlertBanner at :18-20, catch sets loadError at :73-76 — so it is not as deficient as implied; the finding's title scopes only to empty/loading, but its 'misleading dashboard' framing ignores that the shown zeros are factually correct for an empty DB, just unfriendly. (2) The 5 GRDB reads run off-main and are fast, so the loading flash is brief. Real gap remains (no empty-state / skeleton, inconsistent with siblings) but it is polish-level, not high — downgrading to medium.

#### `xc-states-2` · 🟠 Medium · TimelinePageView swallows load errors silently — failed load leaves a blank/stale page with no feedback

- **Surface:** X-cut: empty / loading / error state consistency
- **What's wrong:** TimelinePageView is the only list page whose load failure path only logs and never surfaces an error to the user. It has an EmptyState (line 66-68) for the genuinely-empty case but NO `loadError`/AlertBanner state at all. In `loadData()` the catch block (line 130-132) calls only `EngramLogger.error` and returns; `timeline` stays at its previous value (empty on first load). The same silent-swallow pattern repeats in `confirmSuggestion` (line 140-142) and `dismissSuggestion` (line 156-158): if confirming/dismissing a suggested parent link fails over IPC, nothing tells the user. Every sibling page (SessionsPageView:27-28, ProjectsView:38-39, ActivityView:18-19, AgentsView:20-21, SourcePulseView:69-71, HomeView:32-33) renders an AlertBanner on load failure; Timeline is the lone exception.
- **User impact:** If the timeline query fails (DB locked during reindex, corrupt row, IPC failure), the user sees the 'No activity / No sessions in the last 30 days' empty state — which falsely implies they have no sessions — or a stale list, with zero indication anything went wrong. Confirming or dismissing a suggested agent link can also silently no-op.
- **Evidence:** /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/TimelinePageView.swift:130-132 (load catch only logs, no @State error, no AlertBanner in body); :140-142 and :156-158 (confirm/dismiss catches only log); body at :51-104 has no error UI
- **Suggested fix:** Add `@State private var loadError: String?`, render `if let loadError { AlertBanner(message: "Failed to load timeline: \(loadError)") }` near the top of the VStack, set it in the catch (and clear on success), and surface confirm/dismiss failures the same way (or show a transient banner).
- **Verify:** confirmed — CONFIRMED by direct read. TimelinePageView.swift declares NO error @State (vars at :45-49 are timeline/confirmedCounts/suggestedCounts/sortMode/isLoading only). loadData() catch at :130-132 calls only EngramLogger.error and returns — no error surface in body (:51-104). confirmSuggestion catch at :140-142 and dismissSuggestion catch at :156-158 likewise only log. The sibling comparison is fully verified: SessionsPageView:27-28, ProjectsView:38-39, AgentsView:20-21, SourcePulseView:70, ActivityView:18-20, and HomeView:33 all render AlertBanner on load failure — Timeline is the lone list page without it. Aggravating detail I confirmed: on a first-load failure timeline stays [] AND isLoading flips false (defer at :115), so the EmptyState 'No activity / No sessions in the last 30 days' at :66-68 WOULD render, actively mislabeling a load error as 'no data'. The silent confirm/dismiss IPC failures (user clicks confirm/dismiss link, it silently fails) are real no-feedback dead-ends. I checked the whole Engram tree — there is no NotificationCenter/global error toast that would catch these; the swallow is genuine. Adjusting severity from high to medium: the read-path failure degrades to an existing (if mislabeled) EmptyState rather than a raw blank, and the mutation failures are advisory parent-link operations, not data loss.

#### `xc-events-nav-2` · 🟠 Medium · AgentsView loads agent sessions once and never refreshes when indexing adds new ones

- **Surface:** X-cut: notifications / events / deep-link wiring
- **What's wrong:** AgentsView fetches db.listSessions(subAgent: true, limit: 200) inside a plain `.task { await loadData() }` (AgentsView.swift:45,48-54). Unlike its peer session-list pages (HomeView, SessionsPageView, TimelinePageView, ProjectsView, ActivityView all use `.task(id: serviceStatusStore.totalSessions)`), AgentsView has no id dependency on totalSessions, no .onReceive, and no manual refresh/refreshable affordance. So once the page is loaded, new agent/subagent sessions indexed by the service while the page stays visible never appear.
- **User impact:** A user watching the Agents page while running dispatched agent sessions sees a stale list and stale KPI counts ('Agent Sessions', 'Active 7d'); they must navigate away and back to see newly indexed agent activity.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Pages/AgentsView.swift:45 (.task { await loadData() }), :48-54 (loadData → db.listSessions(subAgent: true, limit: 200)); contrast macos/Engram/Views/Pages/ProjectsView.swift:191 and HomeView.swift:41 which use .task(id: serviceStatusStore.totalSessions); no Button/refreshable/onReceive in AgentsView.swift
- **Suggested fix:** Change to `.task(id: serviceStatusStore.totalSessions) { await loadData() }` (it already has serviceStatusStore in scope via the same pattern as peers) so it re-loads when the index grows.
- **Verify:** partial — Core claim verified: AgentsView.swift:45 uses plain '.task { await loadData() }' with NO id, no .onReceive, no .refreshable, and does not even hold @Environment(EngramServiceStatusStore.self) (only @Environment(DatabaseManager.self) at line 5). Its five session-list peers all live-refresh: HomeView.swift:41, ProjectsView.swift:191, ActivityView.swift:48 use .task(id: serviceStatusStore.totalSessions); SessionsPageView.swift:94-98 and TimelinePageView.swift:108 include serviceStatusStore.totalSessions in a composite task id. serviceStatusStore is injected at App.swift:164, so the fix is trivially available. Marked PARTIAL because the tracer's phrasing 'new agent/subagent sessions ... never appear' is mildly overstated: MainWindowView.swift:106-107 mounts AgentsView via a @ViewBuilder switch keyed on Screen, so navigating away from .agents and back tears down and recreates AgentsView, re-firing .task and reloading. New agent sessions DO appear on page re-entry; the real gap is only that they don't appear LIVE while the page stays continuously visible (peers update without leaving). Still a genuine missing-live-refresh consistency gap on a secondary page; medium is appropriate.

#### `session-detail-transcript-6` · 🟡 Low · No jump-to-top / scroll-to-top affordance for long transcripts

- **What's wrong:** The transcript is a ScrollView+LazyVStack with a ScrollViewReader proxy (SessionDetailView.swift:359-385). The proxy is used only for find/chip navigation via `scrollTarget` (SessionDetailView.swift:380-384). There is no toolbar control or gesture to scroll back to the top after the user has scrolled deep into a long (paged) session, and no scroll-to-bottom either. The 'Load all' affordance can materialize thousands of messages, but the only way back to the top is manual scrolling.

- **Suggested fix:** Add a small 'scroll to top' button (e.g. in the toolbar or a floating control) that sets scrollTarget to displayIndexed.first?.id, reusing the existing ScrollViewReader proxy.

#### `usage-cost-4` · 🟡 Low · Popover USAGE section silently shows nothing when there is no usage data — no empty/unconfigured state

- **Surface:** Usage / cost tracking
- **What's wrong:** PopoverUsageSection renders its entire body only inside `if !usageData.isEmpty` (PopoverUsageSection.swift:19). When usage collection hasn't run, the source doesn't report limits, or no usageTokenLimits are configured, the section disappears entirely with no placeholder, hint, or 'configure usage limits' affordance. Combined with the Settings 'Usage Limits' editor being the only way to make pressure metrics appear, a user who never opens that editor sees no usage UI and gets no nudge that the feature exists or needs setup.
- **User impact:** New users see no usage/cost section in the popover and have no indication that configuring per-source token limits would light it up. The feature is effectively invisible until manually configured, with no discovery path.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Usage/PopoverUsageSection.swift:18-77 (whole view gated on non-empty usageData, no else branch); SettingsView.swift:347-376 (Usage Limits is opt-in editor; 'Leave a limit at 0 to disable pressure alerts')
- **Suggested fix:** Add a lightweight empty/unconfigured state (e.g. a single muted row 'No usage data — set token limits in Settings') with a tap to open Settings > Usage Limits, so the feature is discoverable and its empty state is intentional.

#### `menubar-popover-4` · 🟡 Low · Popover data never refreshes while open; stale on a long-lived popover

- **Surface:** Menu bar popover + live sessions
- **What's wrong:** PopoverView loads everything once via .task { await loadData() } (PopoverView.swift:31) and has no Timer, no .onReceive, and no Observation-driven reload of recentSessions/stats (grep shows .task is the only refresh trigger). Stats like todayParentSessions and usageData come from the observable serviceStatusStore so they update live, but the recentSessions timeline, sourceCount, projectCount, dbSize, and health-summary are snapshotted at open time. Because the popover is .transient (MenuBarController.swift:45) it usually closes quickly so this is minor — but if the user pins focus or the popover stays open, the recent-activity list and "last Xm" indexed label silently go stale.
- **User impact:** During an active coding session, the popover's recent list and 'last Nm' freshness label can be minutes out of date relative to what's actually happening, undercutting its role as a quick-glance monitor.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/PopoverView.swift:31 (single .task load); macos/Engram/MenuBarController.swift:45 (popover.behavior = .transient); loadData populates recentSessions/sourceCount/etc once at PopoverView.swift:281-287
- **Suggested fix:** Mirror SourcePulseView's pattern: add a lightweight Timer (e.g. 10s) in PopoverView to re-run loadData while visible, or re-trigger on popover show, so the recent list and freshness label stay current.

#### `command-palette-5` · 🟡 Low · Search-backend failure is indistinguishable from genuine 'No results'

- **Surface:** Command palette
- **What's wrong:** The palette's search runs `serviceClient.search(...)` and, on any thrown error, silently falls back to `try? db.search(...)` (CommandPaletteView.swift:203-228). If the local DB read also fails or returns nothing, `sessionResults` becomes `[]` and the UI renders the same 'No results' empty state used for a legitimately empty match (CommandPaletteView.swift:104-115). There is no error surface (no toast, no 'Search unavailable' message). A user whose service socket is down or whose index is broken sees 'No results' and concludes their data is missing rather than that search failed.
- **User impact:** When search is actually broken, the palette lies by omission — the user is told there are no matching sessions when in fact the search never ran, eroding trust in the index.
- **Evidence:** CommandPaletteView.swift:215-229 (catch → `try? db.search` → `?? []`, errors swallowed); CommandPaletteView.swift:104-114 ('No results' empty state covers both true-empty and error-empty).
- **Suggested fix:** Track a search-error flag in the catch block and render a distinct 'Search unavailable' state (with the underlying reason) separate from the genuine 'No results' empty state.

#### `xc-states-4` · 🟡 Low · SearchPageView swallows a double-fault (service + local FTS both fail) with no error UI

- **Surface:** X-cut: empty / loading / error state consistency
- **What's wrong:** SearchPageView's primary search path catches a service-search failure and falls back to local FTS (line 429-451). That's good defensive design. But if the local FTS fallback ALSO throws (line 452-454), the inner catch only logs via EngramLogger and returns — `results` keeps its previous value and no warning/empty-state change is shown. The page has a `warning` text field (line 187-191) that could carry this but isn't set on the double-fault path.
- **User impact:** In the rare case both the service round-trip and the local DB read fail (e.g. DB locked/corrupt), a search appears to do nothing — stale results stay on screen with no 'search failed' indication. Low-probability since FTS is local, but the user gets no signal.
- **Evidence:** /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SearchPageView.swift:452-454 (inner catch only logs; `warning`/`results` untouched)
- **Suggested fix:** In the inner catch, set `warning = "Search unavailable — could not reach the index."` (and optionally `results = []`) so the failure is visible.

#### `xc-events-nav-4` · 🟡 Low · MemoryView / SkillsView / HooksView load filesystem-backed data once with no refresh on change

- **Surface:** X-cut: notifications / events / deep-link wiring
- **What's wrong:** MemoryView (memoryFiles()), SkillsView (skills()), and HooksView (hooks()) each load via a plain `.task { await loadData() }` with no .task(id:), no .onReceive, no refreshable, and no refresh button. These read mutable on-disk config (memory files, ~/.claude skills, hooks). If the underlying files change while the page is open, the view shows stale content until the user navigates away and back.
- **User impact:** A user who edits a memory file, adds a skill, or changes a hook outside the app and switches back to an already-open Memory/Skills/Hooks page sees stale data with no obvious way to refresh besides leaving and returning.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Pages/MemoryView.swift:87 (.task { await loadData() }), :93 (serviceClient.memoryFiles()); SkillsView.swift:48,69 (skills()); HooksView.swift:33,59 (hooks()); no refreshable/Button-refresh/onReceive in any of the three
- **Suggested fix:** Add a `.refreshable` or a small refresh button to these three pages (lowest-effort) so users can re-pull on demand.

### Dead-ends & orphan views (13)

#### `sessions-browse-1` · 🔴 High · Per-card context menu (Resume / Copy Resume Command / Handoff / Replay) is a dead, no-op menu on the Sessions page

- **Surface:** Browse sessions → filter → open
- **What's wrong:** ExpandableSessionCard always renders a 4-item context menu (Resume..., Copy Resume Command, Handoff, Replay) at Components/ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129 (parent) and :342-355 (child rows). Those buttons call optional closures onResume/onCopyResumeCommand/onHandoff/onReplay. But SessionsPageView constructs the card WITHOUT passing any of those four callbacks (SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 only wires onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion). Because the closures are nil, every menu item is `nil?(session)` and does nothing. The backend capability is real (EngramServiceClient.resumeCommand/handoff/replayTimeline all exist) and is correctly wired in SessionDetailView and HomeView, so this page is the broken surface. TimelinePageView (TimelinePageView.swift:84-96) has the identical defect.
- **User impact:** On the main Sessions browse page, right-clicking any session offers Resume, Copy Resume Command, Handoff, and Replay — the core 'pick up where I left off' actions — and selecting any of them silently does nothing. The user gets no feedback, no clipboard change, no resume. This is the primary value action of the whole app and it is dead exactly on the page built for browsing.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Components/ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129 and :342-355 (context menu always shown); macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 (card built with no on-Resume/Handoff/Replay/Copy callbacks); contrast macos/Engram/Views/SessionDetailView.swift:188-190 where the same actions ARE wired to real service calls
- **Suggested fix:** Pass the same callbacks SessionsPageView already has access to (it holds serviceClient): onResume / onCopyResumeCommand / onHandoff / onReplay, reusing HomeView's resumeSession sheet + copyResumeCommand helpers. Alternatively, gate the contextMenu builder in ExpandableSessionCard so items only render when their closure is non-nil.
- **Verify:** confirmed — ExpandableSessionCard declares onResume/onCopyResumeCommand/onHandoff/onReplay as optional closures defaulting to nil (ExpandableSessionCard.swift:30-33) and unconditionally renders the 4-item contextMenu on the parent row (:116-129) and on every CompactChildRow (:342-355), each calling the optional closure (e.g. onResume?(session)). Both call sites that construct ExpandableSessionCard omit all four callbacks: SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 wires only onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion, and TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 wires only onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion. So on both pages every menu item is a no-op. The capability is real and reachable elsewhere: SessionDetailView.swift:188-190 wires onHandoff/onReplay/onResume to performHandoff()/showReplay/showResume, and HomeView uses a different card (TodaySessionRow) that wires onResume/onCopyCommand (HomeView.swift:122-124,155-158). No command palette, .commands menu, or NotificationCenter event provides an alternate resume/handoff/replay/copy path for these cards (only openSettings/openWindow/openSession/navigateToScreen/projectsDidChange exist; AppNotifications.swift:4-7). Tracer is correct including the TimelinePageView claim; severity high stands (a context menu rendered to the user that silently does nothing is a true dead-end, and it is the primary browse surface).

#### `settings-general-2` · 🔴 High · 'Open Web UI' button is permanently disabled in the default (web-disabled) configuration

- **Surface:** Settings: General / Network / About
- **What's wrong:** GeneralSettingsSection's 'Open Web UI' button is `.disabled(webUIURL == nil)`, and webUIURL is non-nil only when `serviceStatusStore.endpointPort != nil` (GeneralSettingsSection.swift:64-69,134-138). endpointPort is set ONLY by the `web_ready` service event (EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:81-83), which the runner emits only when webUIEnabled is true (EngramServiceRunner.swift:88,94). Because there is no UI to set webUIEnabled (see settings-general-1), in a stock install endpointPort stays nil forever, so this button is always greyed out.
- **User impact:** The most visible web-UI affordance in Settings is a button the user can never click in a default install. It looks like a feature, but clicking is impossible, giving the impression the app is half-built.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/Settings/GeneralSettingsSection.swift:64-69 (button + .disabled(webUIURL==nil)), :134-138 (webUIURL needs endpointPort); macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:81-86 (endpointPort only from web_ready/cleared on web_error); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceRunner.swift:88,94 (web_ready only fires when webUIEnabled).
- **Suggested fix:** Once a webUIEnabled toggle exists (settings-general-1), this button becomes usable. Until then, either hide the button when web UI is disabled or show inline text explaining how to enable it, instead of a dead disabled control.
- **Verify:** confirmed — GeneralSettingsSection.swift:64-69 shows the `Open Web UI` button is `.disabled(webUIURL == nil)`; webUIURL (lines 134-138) is non-nil only when serviceStatusStore.endpointPort != nil. EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:81-83 sets endpointPort ONLY on the `web_ready` event; web_error clears it (lines 84-86). The runner only emits web_ready inside the webUIEnabled-gated webTask (EngramServiceRunner.swift:88,91-94 — emitWebReady is inside the `webUIEnabled ? Task {...}` block). Combined with finding 1 (no UI to set webUIEnabled), endpointPort stays nil in a stock install, so the button is permanently greyed. Chain verified end-to-end. High is appropriate (permanent dead-end control in default config).

#### `workspace-repos-1` · 🔴 High · RepoDetail "Recent Sessions" rows are dead-ends — drill-down shows sessions you cannot open

- **Surface:** Workspace: Repos / RepoDetail / WorkGraph
- **What's wrong:** The repo drill-down ends in a dead-end. RepoDetailView renders each related session as a styled card (colored source dot, title, source label, date, surface background, rounded corners) that visually matches the clickable session cards used elsewhere, but the rows are plain HStacks with NO Button/onTapGesture/navigation. A user clicks a repo -> sees 'Recent Sessions' -> taps one expecting the transcript -> nothing happens. The app already has the navigation primitive for exactly this: SessionsPageView posts `NotificationCenter.default.post(name: .openSession, object: SessionBox(session))` and MainWindowView handles `.openSession` to open the transcript. RepoDetailView simply never wires it.
- **User impact:** The Repos -> RepoDetail journey looks like it links to the repo's sessions but cannot complete: clicking a listed session does nothing. The single most useful action in the drill-down (read what happened in that repo) is missing, making the related-sessions list purely informational decoration.
- **Evidence:** /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Workspace/RepoDetailView.swift:105-126 (ForEach renders HStack with no tap action); grep confirms only Button handlers in the file are the back button (line 15) and quickActionButton (lines 55-71,148). Working pattern exists at /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:73 (.openSession post) and handler at /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/MainWindowView.swift:45 (.onReceive .openSession).
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap each related-session row in a Button (or .onTapGesture) that posts `NotificationCenter.default.post(name: .openSession, object: SessionBox(session))`, mirroring SessionsPageView.swift:73.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed real dead-end. RepoDetailView.swift:105-126 renders each related session as an HStack styled like a clickable card (source dot, title, source, date, Theme.surface bg, rounded corners) with NO Button/onTapGesture/NavigationLink. grep over the whole file (RepoDetailView.swift) shows the only Button/action handlers are the back button (:15) and quickActionButton (:55-71,148) — none wraps the session rows, and `.openSession`/SessionBox/NavigationLink never appear in this file. The navigation primitive exists and is used everywhere else: SessionsPageView.swift:73 posts NotificationCenter.default.post(name:.openSession, object:SessionBox(session)) and is handled at MainWindowView.swift:45-50 (sets selectedSession to open the transcript). Same pattern in HomeView:302, TimelinePageView:89/92, ProjectsView:69, AgentsView:35, SearchPageView:222. RepoDetailView simply never wires it, so the repo drill-down ends in non-interactive rows that visually promise navigation. High severity is appropriate (orphaned drill-down on a primary surface).

#### `usage-cost-2` · 🔴 High · Cost budget + cost-threshold + long-session settings are write-only orphans (no consumer)

- **Surface:** Usage / cost tracking
- **What's wrong:** The 'Monitor & Budgets' settings group lets the user set a Daily Budget, Monthly Budget, Long Session minutes, and toggle 'Notify on cost threshold' and 'Notify on long session'. saveAdvancedSettings() persists these to ~/.engram/settings.json under monitor{dailyCostBudget,monthlyCostBudget,longSessionMinutes,notifyOnCostThreshold,notifyOnLongSession} and costAlerts{dailyBudget,monthlyBudget}. But a grep across EngramService, EngramCoreWrite, EngramMCP, and the app finds NO reader of any of these keys. Only notifyOnUsagePressure is actually consumed (by UsagePressureNotifier via UsagePressureNotificationSettings.current, UsagePressureNotifier.swift:11-12). So setting a daily budget or enabling 'Notify on cost threshold'/'Notify on long session' does nothing.
- **User impact:** A user who sets a $20 daily budget and turns on 'Notify on cost threshold' expecting an alert when they overspend will never get one — the feature looks fully built (labeled toggles, USD fields, persisted) but silently does nothing. Same for 'Notify on long session'. This actively misleads the user into believing cost guardrails are active.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Views/SettingsView.swift:308-342 (UI controls), 517-528 (persisted to costAlerts + monitor), 337,341 (notifyOnCostThreshold / notifyOnLongSession toggles); grep 'dailyCostBudget|monthlyCostBudget|notifyOnCostThreshold|notifyOnLongSession|longSessionMinutes|costAlerts' across macos (excluding build/tests/SettingsView) returns no consumer; UsagePressureNotifier.swift:8-14 reads ONLY monitor.enabled + monitor.notifyOnUsagePressure
- **Suggested fix:** Either implement the consumers (service-side check of accumulated cost_usd vs dailyCostBudget that posts a notification, and a long-session detector), or remove/disable the Daily/Monthly Budget, 'Notify on cost threshold', Long Session, and 'Notify on long session' controls until backed. At minimum gate them behind a 'coming soon' state so they don't imply working guardrails.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified by exhaustive grep across the ENTIRE macos tree (Engram, Shared, EngramCoreRead, EngramCoreWrite, EngramService, EngramMCP, incl tests). For dailyCostBudget|monthlyCostBudget|notifyOnCostThreshold|notifyOnLongSession|longSessionMinutes|costAlerts, the ONLY hits are inside Engram/Views/SettingsView.swift itself (state vars 193-198, UI controls 308-342, load 452-463, persist 517-528). Zero consumers anywhere else. UsagePressureNotifier.swift:9-12 reads ONLY monitor.enabled and monitor.notifyOnUsagePressure; it is the sole reader of the monitor dict outside SettingsView. The 'budget'/'longSession' grep hits in EngramServiceLauncher.swift:186,230 and UnixSocketEngramServiceTransport.swift:7,258 are restart/timeout 'budgets', confirmed unrelated to cost. So Daily/Monthly budget, Long Session minutes, Notify-on-cost-threshold, and Notify-on-long-session are write-only orphans with no consumer. Severity high upheld (multiple user-facing settings that silently do nothing).

#### `search-2` · 🟠 Medium · Mode selector (keyword/semantic/hybrid) is permanently dead — it never renders and its cases are unreachable

- **Surface:** Keyword search → results → open
- **What's wrong:** SearchMode.availableModes(embeddingAvailable:) hardcodes a return of [.keyword] and ignores its parameter (SearchSupport.swift:9-11). SearchPageView gates the mode-selector pills on `if availableModes.count > 1` (SearchPageView.swift:141), which is therefore always false, so the keyword/semantic/hybrid buttons never appear. As a result the `selectedMode` @State, the `selectedMode = mode; triggerSearch()` button action (line 143), the `.semantic` and `.hybrid` enum cases (SearchSupport.swift:4), and the 'keyword + semantic'/purple/green branches of matchBadge and modeColor (SearchPageView.swift:503-518) are all unreachable in the shipped product. This is leftover UI for a capability (semantic/hybrid search) the Swift product does not implement (CLAUDE.md: product is keyword-only; SQLiteVecSupport reports 'not implemented yet').
- **User impact:** No direct user-visible bug (the buttons simply never show), but the code carries a half-built feature that implies a search-mode choice the product cannot offer. Maintenance hazard: a future change to availableModes would surface non-functional semantic/hybrid modes.
- **Evidence:** SearchSupport.swift:9-11 (availableModes always returns [.keyword]); SearchPageView.swift:141 (`if availableModes.count > 1` always false); SearchPageView.swift:143-157 (mode pill buttons never reachable); SearchPageView.swift:503,516 ('both'/'semantic' badge branches never hit)
- **Suggested fix:** Either delete the unreachable mode-selector UI and the .semantic/.hybrid enum cases until vector search ships, or gate them behind an explicit feature flag. Keep the keyword path as the single mode.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified the mode selector is permanently dead. SearchSupport.swift:9-11 SearchMode.availableModes ignores embeddingAvailable and returns [.keyword] unconditionally (count==1). SearchPageView.swift:141 gates the mode pills on `if availableModes.count > 1`, which is therefore always false, so the keyword/semantic/hybrid Buttons (lines 142-157) with action `selectedMode=mode; triggerSearch()` never render. The .semantic/.hybrid enum cases (SearchSupport.swift:4) are never selectable from UI. The 'both'->'keyword + semantic' branch (line 503) and modeColor purple/green branches (lines 515-516) are unreachable because the service hardcodes matchType:"keyword" (EngramServiceReadProvider.swift:1174) and searchModes:["keyword"] (line 484, plus offline fallback 'keyword (offline)' at SearchPageView.swift:447); no service path emits 'semantic'/'both'/'hybrid'. Confirmed leftover UI for the unimplemented semantic/hybrid capability (CLAUDE.md: keyword-only; SQLiteVecSupport not implemented). Cosmetic dead code with no broken user workflow — medium is fair.

#### `menubar-popover-2` · 🟠 Medium · Live session cards are display-only dead-ends — cannot open a live session

- **Surface:** Menu bar popover + live sessions
- **What's wrong:** LiveSessionCard renders source, project, title, model, activity and elapsed time but has no onTapGesture, no Button, and no navigation — it is purely presentational (LiveSessionCard.swift:40-103). In SourcePulseView the only Button is the "Show more" expander (SourcePulseView.swift:203) and the reveal-archive button (line 49); the session cards themselves are not wrapped in any tap/navigation. Yet the backing DTO EngramServiceLiveSessionInfo carries a sessionId (EngramServiceModels.swift:452-454) which the rest of the app uses to deep-link via SessionBox/.openSession (e.g. HomeView.swift:302, SessionsPageView.swift:73). So opening the live session's transcript is technically wired everywhere else but deliberately absent here.
- **User impact:** A user watching a session go "active" in the live view cannot click it to read its transcript or jump to its detail — the live monitor is a wall of glanceable rows with no way to act on any of them. The journey "see something interesting happening → open it" dead-ends.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Components/LiveSessionCard.swift:40-103 (no gesture/button); macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SourcePulseView.swift:198-201 (cards rendered without tap); macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceModels.swift:451-463 (DTO has sessionId); contrast with macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:302 which posts .openSession for normal sessions
- **Suggested fix:** Make LiveSessionCard tappable: when session.sessionId is non-nil, on tap look it up (db.getSession(id:)) and post .openSession (or .openWindow with the resolved SessionBox), matching the pattern used in HomeView/SessionsPageView. Show a non-interactive style when sessionId is nil.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Read LiveSessionCard.swift:40-103 in full: body has no onTapGesture, no Button, no navigation — only .onAppear { isPulsing = true } at line 102, purely presentational. SourcePulseView.swift:198-201 renders cards inside ForEach with no tap wrapper; the only Buttons in that view are the Show-more expander (203) and reveal-archive (49). DTO EngramServiceLiveSessionInfo carries sessionId at EngramServiceModels.swift:454 and .openSession deep-link is wired everywhere else (HomeView.swift:302, SessionsPageView.swift:73, TimelinePageView.swift:89). The dead-end is real. Downgraded high->medium: sessionId is Optional (id falls back to filePath at line 452), so an in-progress live session may not be openable through the existing transcript path even if a tap were added, and a display-only live monitor is a defensible design choice rather than a broken core flow.

#### `xc-deadends-1` · 🟠 Medium · Session card right-click menu (Resume/Handoff/Replay/Copy) is dead on the Sessions and Timeline pages

- **Surface:** X-cut: dead-ends, no-op buttons, TODO/stub markers, orphan views
- **What's wrong:** ExpandableSessionCard always renders a .contextMenu with four items — "Resume...", "Copy Resume Command", "Handoff", "Replay" — that invoke onResume?/onCopyResumeCommand?/onHandoff?/onReplay? (optional-chained, so nil = silent no-op). SessionsPageView and TimelinePageView instantiate the card WITHOUT passing any of those four closures, so all four menu items render but do nothing when clicked. The same nil closures flow down into every CompactChildRow context menu in those pages too.
- **User impact:** On the two main session-browsing pages, right-clicking a session shows Resume/Handoff/Replay/Copy commands that appear actionable but produce zero effect. The same actions work from HomeView (TodaySessionRow) and SessionDetailView, so behavior is silently inconsistent and looks broken.
- **Evidence:** Card menu defined at macos/Engram/Components/ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-130 and :342-355 (calls onResume?/onHandoff?/onReplay?/onCopyResumeCommand?). SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 instantiates the card passing only onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion. TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 same omission. Callbacks default to nil at ExpandableSessionCard.swift:30-33 and :295-298.
- **Suggested fix:** Pass onResume/onCopyResumeCommand/onHandoff/onReplay from SessionsPageView and TimelinePageView (post .openSession + reuse the resume/handoff handlers already present), or conditionally hide each context-menu Button when its closure is nil.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Code confirms the structural claim: ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129 (parent) and :342-355 (CompactChildRow) always render a 4-item .contextMenu wired to onResume?/onCopyResumeCommand?/onHandoff?/onReplay? (optional-chained, nil = silent no-op; defaults nil at :30-33 and :295-298). SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 and TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 instantiate the card passing ONLY onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion — so all four menu items on those two pages, and on their CompactChildRows, do nothing when clicked. Grep across Engram/ confirms these closures are NEVER passed to ExpandableSessionCard (only instantiations are those two pages). So the right-click menu items are genuinely dead on Sessions and Timeline. HOWEVER the tracer overstates impact by framing it as the action being dead: the capabilities themselves are fully reachable. onTap posts .openSession (SessionsPageView.swift:73) opening SessionDetailView, whose TranscriptToolbar wires onHandoff/onReplay/onResume (SessionDetailView.swift:188-190 -> performHandoff / showReplay sheet :460 / showResume ResumeDialog :464). HomeView's TodaySessionRow also wires onResume and onCopyCommand (HomeView.swift:122-124). So this is a broken/confusing affordance (dead menu entries), not a missing feature. Downgrading high->medium: the four actions are one click away in the detail view; the menu just shouldn't render inert items.

#### `xc-events-nav-1` · 🟠 Medium · summary_generated event handler + lastSummarySessionId are dead: service never emits, no view ever reads

- **Surface:** X-cut: notifications / events / deep-link wiring
- **What's wrong:** EngramServiceStatusStore handles a 'summary_generated' event (EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:88-90) by setting lastSummarySessionId. But (a) the production service never emits this event — EngramServiceRunner only writes 'ready', 'web_ready', 'usage', 'web_error', 'index_error' to stdout, never 'summary_generated' (verified: no occurrence in EngramService/), and (b) lastSummarySessionId is declared at EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:33 and written only at line 90, but grep across Engram/ + Shared/ finds zero readers. So the whole 'a summary was just generated for session X' signal path is wired in the store but is fed by nothing and consumed by nothing.
- **User impact:** No direct user-visible breakage, but it means the app has no live channel to learn that a session summary finished. A SessionDetailView open while the service generates that session's summary will never refresh to show it. The dead field/handler also misleads future maintainers into thinking summary push is wired.
- **Evidence:** macos/Shared/Service/EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:33 (var lastSummarySessionId), :88-90 (case "summary_generated": ... lastSummarySessionId = event.sessionId); macos/EngramService/Core/EngramServiceRunner.swift emits only ready/web_ready/usage/web_error/index_error (no summary_generated); zero readers of lastSummarySessionId in Engram/ or Shared/
- **Suggested fix:** Either emit 'summary_generated' from EngramServiceRunner and add a SessionDetailView .onReceive that refreshes when lastSummarySessionId == session.id, or delete lastSummarySessionId and the 'summary_generated' case as dead code.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified both halves of the dead-path claim. (a) NO EMITTER: grep for exact string 'summary_generated' across EngramService/, Shared/, EngramCoreWrite/, EngramCoreRead/ returns ONLY EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:88 (the consumer). EngramServiceRunner emits ready/fatal/checkpoint/web_ready/indexed/usage plus StartupBackfill events (EngramServiceRunner.swift:69,125,186,373,645,802,824); none is summary_generated. The 'generateSummary' command (EngramServiceCommandHandler.swift:105,871-895) is a request/response: it returns a synchronous EngramServiceGenerateSummaryResponse(summary:) over the socket and never writes a stdout event. The production event stream UnixSocketEngramServiceTransport.events() (lines 90-135) only yields Self.event(from:status) (line 105) or a 'warning' on transient errors (line 121); event(from:status) (lines 148-161) can only produce indexed/warning/error/starting. So case 'summary_generated' at line 88-90 is unreachable in production. (b) NO READER: grep for lastSummarySessionId across the tree returns only the declaration (EngramServiceStatusStore.swift:33), the single writer (line 90), and the unit test (EngramServiceStatusStoreTests.swift:39). Zero view/UI readers. The whole 'a summary was just generated for session X' signal is wired but fed by nothing and consumed by nothing. Severity medium is correct: harmless dead code / orphan in a store, not a functional regression.

#### `home-today-1` · 🟡 Low · KPI cards on Today look clickable but navigate nowhere

- **Surface:** Today / Home landing page
- **What's wrong:** The four KPI cards at the top of the Today page (Today / Sessions / Projects / Service) are rendered as bare KPICard views inside an HStack. KPICard is a pure VStack with no Button, NavigationLink, onTapGesture, or simultaneousGesture, and HomeView does not wrap them. A card-shaped, bordered tile is a strong affordance for tapping (e.g. 'Sessions' -> go to Sessions list, 'Projects' -> go to Projects, 'Service' -> jump to Service State / Settings), but clicking any of them does nothing.
- **User impact:** A user lands on Today, sees 'Sessions 1.2K' / 'Projects 34' as card tiles, clicks expecting to drill into that list, and nothing happens. The headline metrics are read-only decoration with no path to act on them.
- **Evidence:** KPICard has no interactive modifier: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Components/KPICard.swift:4-43 (only VStack + accessibility). HomeView renders them bare with no Button/NavigationLink: /Users/bing/-Code-/engram/macos/Engram/Views/Pages/HomeView.swift:70-79. Grep for onTapGesture/Button/NavigationLink in KPICard.swift returned nothing.
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the Sessions/Projects/Service KPI cards in a Button (or post .navigateToScreen) so they jump to the Sessions page, Projects page, and Service State / Settings respectively; or visually de-emphasize them so they don't read as tappable tiles.
- **Verify:** partial — Factually accurate: KPICard.swift:4-43 is a pure VStack with only accessibility modifiers (no Button/NavigationLink/onTapGesture/simultaneousGesture). HomeView.swift:70-79 renders the four cards in a plain HStack with only .accessibilityIdentifier, no gesture wrapping (verified full kpiSection :67-86). A navigation channel exists that they could use but don't: .navigateToScreen notification (AppNotifications.swift:7) is consumed in MainWindowView.swift:51-54 to switch screens. However, the 'looks clickable -> dead-end' framing is overstated: KPICard is a display-only stat tile used identically across 10+ views (ReposView.swift:31-34, ProjectsView.swift:42-44, SessionsPageView.swift:31-35, ActivityView.swift:22-24, AgentsView, WorkGraphView, SystemHealthView, ErrorDashboardView, HygieneView, SourcePulseView) and NONE of them are interactive. So this is an app-wide convention (summary readouts), not an orphaned affordance specific to Today. It's a reasonable enhancement (make Sessions/Projects/Service cards navigate) but not a broken workflow. Downgraded medium -> low.

#### `replay-4` · 🟡 Low · "Replay" context-menu item on session cards is a dead no-op in the two list views that use it

- **Surface:** Session replay
- **What's wrong:** ExpandableSessionCard exposes a context-menu "Replay" action that calls onReplay?(session), and child rows wire onReplay through too. But the only two screens that instantiate ExpandableSessionCard — SessionsPageView and TimelinePageView — never pass an onReplay closure (nor onResume/onHandoff/onCopyResumeCommand). Because the closures are optional and default to nil, right-clicking a session card and choosing Replay (or Resume/Handoff) does nothing at all.
- **User impact:** From the Sessions and Timeline lists, a user who right-clicks a session and picks Replay (a clearly offered menu item) gets zero response and no feedback — a broken affordance. Replay is only actually reachable via the toolbar button after drilling into a session's detail view.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Components/ExpandableSessionCard.swift:126-128 (context menu Replay → onReplay?(session)); call sites omit onReplay: macos/Engram/Views/Pages/SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 and macos/Engram/Views/Pages/TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 (only onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion passed)
- **Suggested fix:** Either wire onReplay (and Resume/Handoff) in SessionsPageView/TimelinePageView to post a notification / open the replay sheet, or conditionally hide the context-menu items when their closures are nil so the app doesn't advertise dead actions.
- **Verify:** partial — The factual core is correct: ExpandableSessionCard's context menu (Engram/Components/ExpandableSessionCard.swift:116-129) wires Resume/Copy Resume Command/Handoff/Replay to optional closures, and both call sites SessionsPageView.swift:67-80 and TimelinePageView.swift:84-96 pass only onTap/onChildTap/onConfirmSuggestion/onDismissSuggestion, omitting onReplay/onResume/onHandoff/onCopyResumeCommand. So those four context-menu items are inert no-ops in both list views (and propagate inert to child rows at :153,:180). BUT the implicit framing that this orphans Replay is overstated: Replay, Resume, and Handoff are fully wired and reachable from the primary SessionDetailView transcript toolbar (SessionDetailView.swift:188-190 -> TranscriptToolbar.swift:104-114 Replay button -> showReplay sheet -> SessionReplayView at :460-461). The real, narrower issue is a redundant dead context-menu affordance in two list views, not a missing feature; medium is too high, downgraded to low.

#### `command-palette-2` · 🟡 Low · PaletteCategory.action and .session cases are defined but never instantiated (dead model surface)

- **Surface:** Command palette
- **What's wrong:** `PaletteCategory` declares three cases — `.navigation`, `.session`, `.action` (PaletteItem.swift:4-8) — implying the palette supports session items and action items as first-class categories. In practice only `.navigation` is ever produced (the sole `PaletteItem` factory hard-codes `category: .navigation`, PaletteItem.swift:25). Session results are not `PaletteItem`s at all; they are a separate ad-hoc `AnyPaletteRow` built inline in `visibleItems` (CommandPaletteView.swift:35-40). So `.session` and `.action` are unreachable enum cases — model surface that signals capability the code never delivers.
- **User impact:** No direct user-facing impact, but it confirms the palette was scaffolded for a richer model (sessions + actions as palette items) that was never finished — corroborating finding command-palette-1.
- **Evidence:** PaletteItem.swift:4-8 (enum has .navigation/.session/.action); PaletteItem.swift:25 (only category produced is .navigation); CommandPaletteView.swift:29-41 (sessions handled via AnyPaletteRow, not PaletteItem/PaletteCategory).
- **Suggested fix:** Either implement `.action` (and route session hits through `.session` PaletteItems) so the categories carry meaning, or trim the enum to the single `.navigation` case actually used.

#### `command-palette-3` · 🟡 Low · Dead palette state in MainWindowView (paletteItems / paletteSelection never used)

- **Surface:** Command palette
- **What's wrong:** `MainWindowView` declares `@State private var paletteItems: [PaletteItem] = []` and `@State private var paletteSelection: Int = 0` (MainWindowView.swift:8-9). Neither is ever read or written anywhere in the file or codebase — a grep for both names returns only the declarations. The actual palette manages its own `query`, `selectedIndex`, and results internally in `CommandPaletteView`. These two vars are leftover scaffolding from an earlier design where the parent owned palette state.
- **User impact:** None directly; dead state that misleads future maintainers into thinking the parent drives palette selection, and is a residue of an unfinished palette design.
- **Evidence:** MainWindowView.swift:8-9 (declarations); grep for paletteItems/paletteSelection across macos/Engram returns only these two lines (no reads, no writes).
- **Suggested fix:** Remove `paletteItems` and `paletteSelection` from MainWindowView; they are orphaned by the current CommandPaletteView-owns-its-state design.

### UX / visual consistency (15)

#### `session-detail-transcript-2` · 🟠 Medium · Pressing Return in the find field does not advance to the next match

- **Surface:** Open session → read transcript → find-in-page
- **What's wrong:** TranscriptFindBar's TextField has no `.onSubmit` handler (TranscriptFindBar.swift:19-22; confirmed by absence of onSubmit/onKeyPress in the file). On macOS, Return in a find field universally means "go to next match" (Safari, Xcode, TextEdit, every native find bar). Here, after typing a query the user must move the mouse to the small chevron buttons or know the ⌘G shortcut (registered on a hidden background button at SessionDetailView.swift:396-399). Return does nothing.
- **User impact:** Users hit Return expecting to jump to the next match (the macOS-standard gesture) and nothing happens, making find feel broken until they discover the chevrons or ⌘G.
- **Evidence:** TranscriptFindBar.swift:19-22 (TextField with no onSubmit); grep for onSubmit/keyboardShortcut/onKeyPress in TranscriptFindBar.swift returns no matches; next-match is only reachable via onNext button (TranscriptFindBar.swift:53-58) or ⌘G hidden button (SessionDetailView.swift:396-397)
- **Suggested fix:** Add `.onSubmit { onNext() }` to the TextField (and consider Shift-Return → onPrev) so Return advances matches like every native find bar.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Verified. TranscriptFindBar's TextField (TranscriptFindBar.swift:19-22) has no `.onSubmit`, `.onKeyPress`, `.submitLabel`, or `keyboardShortcut`. Grepped onSubmit across all of Engram+Shared: the only hit is SearchPageView.swift:127 (global search box), unrelated to the transcript find bar. Next-match is reachable only via the chevron Button(action: onNext) (TranscriptFindBar.swift:53-58) or the hidden ⌘G background button (SessionDetailView.swift:396-397). Return in the find field does nothing — contrary to the universal macOS find-bar idiom. Workarounds (⌘G, chevron buttons) exist, so medium/ux-consistency is the right rating.

#### `sources-sync-3` · 🟠 Medium · Two different surfaces both called 'Sources' that overlap and neither lets the user act

- **Surface:** Sources: enable/disable + trigger sync
- **What's wrong:** There are two 'Sources' surfaces that a user must reconcile. (1) The Workspace nav item literally labeled 'Sources' (Screen.sourcePulse) renders SourcePulseView — a read-only status dashboard: KPI counts, per-source health badge, search/token coverage pills, 'N issues' counts. (2) Settings > 'Data Sources' renders SourcesSettingsSection — a read-only list of adapter paths with a path-exists dot. They show overlapping-but-different subsets of source info (Pulse shows indexed sources with health; Settings shows a hardcoded path list) and neither offers an action — no toggle, no sync, no 'open failed jobs'. A user looking for 'where do I manage my sources' will bounce between two read-only panes and find no controls in either.
- **User impact:** Confusion about where to configure sources, and a dead end at both: the dashboard implies management but offers none, the settings pane implies configuration but is non-editable.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/Models/Screen.swift:39 (.sourcePulse title = "Sources"); :103 (in Workspace group); macos/Engram/Views/MainWindowView.swift:98-99 (.sourcePulse -> SourcePulseView); macos/Engram/Views/SettingsView.swift:105 (SourcesSettingsSection mounted under Settings); SourcePulseView.swift:72-124 vs SourcesSettingsSection.swift:31-50 (both read-only, disjoint info)
- **Suggested fix:** Consolidate: make the Settings 'Data Sources' section the single management surface (toggle + re-index + per-source error link), and have the nav 'Sources' dashboard deep-link into it for any actionable item (e.g. tapping 'N issues').
- **Verify:** confirmed — Confirmed. Screen.swift:39 maps .sourcePulse title to 'Sources' and line 103 places it in the .workspace group ([.projects, .sourcePulse, .repos, .workGraph]). MainWindowView.swift:98-99 renders SourcePulseView for .sourcePulse. SettingsView.swift:105 mounts SourcesSettingsSection (a section titled 'Data Sources'). The two surfaces are disjoint and read-only: SourcePulseView shows indexed sources with health badges/coverage pills (lines 78-124), SourcesSettingsSection shows a hardcoded 18-entry adapter path list with a path-exists dot (lines 36-43, 78-93). Neither offers an action control. Both naming 'Sources'/'Data Sources' overlap is real and confirmed. Medium severity (consistency/discoverability) is appropriate.

#### `menubar-popover-3` · 🟠 Medium · Popover timeline double-click-to-open is undiscoverable (no affordance, no hint)

- **What's wrong:** The only way to open a session from the popover is a hidden 2-count tap on a timeline row: timelineRow uses .onTapGesture(count: 2) to post .openWindow(SessionBox(session)) (PopoverView.swift:177-181). Elsewhere the app opens sessions on single interactions, so the double-click-only popover row is also inconsistent.

No .help, no onHover, no chevron on rows — nothing signals interactivity and there is no single-tap behavior. Inconsistency confirmed against the rest of the app: HomeView opens via single-click Button(action: onOpen) (HomeView.swift:401,460) and ExpandableSessionCard exposes its open action as a Button. Medium stands.

#### `session-detail-transcript-5` · 🟡 Low · No distinct highlight for the 'current' match — every match is the same yellow

- **Surface:** Open session → read transcript → find-in-page
- **What's wrong:** `highlightedText` paints every occurrence with the same yellow background / black foreground (ColorBarMessageView.swift:74-96). The find bar reports a current position like '3/12' (TranscriptFindBar.swift:40-44) and Prev/Next move `currentMatchIndex`, but there is no visual differentiation of the active match — `ColorBarMessageView` receives only `searchText`, not the current match index, so all 12 hits look identical. Native find bars highlight the active match in a stronger color (orange) vs. the rest (yellow).
- **User impact:** After pressing Next several times the count says '5/12' but the user can't tell which highlighted span on screen is #5 — every highlight looks the same, so the position counter feels disconnected from the page.
- **Evidence:** ColorBarMessageView.swift:74-96 (all matches get .yellow/.black, no current-match concept); ColorBarMessageView.swift:4-7 (view receives searchText only, no current match index); TranscriptFindBar.swift:40-44 (UI advertises a current position N/M)
- **Suggested fix:** Thread the current match's message id (and ideally character range) into ColorBarMessageView and render the active match with a distinct accent (e.g. orange) so the '/N' counter maps to a visible highlight.

#### `session-detail-transcript-7` · 🟡 Low · Searching swaps rich Session-mode rendering for flat highlighted text, dropping markdown/code formatting

- **Surface:** Open session → read transcript → find-in-page
- **What's wrong:** In Session view, assistant and code messages normally render through SegmentedMessageView (markdown, code blocks with syntax highlighting + copy, tables, lists). But when a find query is active, ColorBarMessageView falls back to a flat highlighted Text for `.assistant`/`.code` (ColorBarMessageView.swift:108-115): `if searchText.isEmpty { SegmentedMessageView } else { Text(highlightedText(...)) }`. So the moment a user starts a find, the entire transcript loses its formatted rendering (code blocks become plain text, the per-code-block Copy buttons vanish, tables flatten) and reverts on clearing the query.
- **User impact:** As soon as a user searches inside a session, all formatted content (code blocks, syntax highlighting, copy-code buttons, tables, lists) collapses into plain monospace-free text, which is jarring and removes the copy-code-block affordance exactly when a user is hunting for a specific snippet.
- **Evidence:** ColorBarMessageView.swift:108-115 (assistant/code: SegmentedMessageView only when searchText is empty, else flat highlighted Text); ContentSegmentViews.swift:99-140 (SegmentedMessageView is the rich renderer that is skipped during search)
- **Suggested fix:** Apply highlighting within the segmented renderer (e.g. pass searchText into SegmentedMessageView/MarkdownText/CodeBlockView and highlight ranges per-segment) instead of replacing the whole rich view with flat highlighted Text during search.

#### `hygiene-7` · 🟡 Low · Hygiene page never explains its relationship to tiering (skip/lite) or hidden state

- **Surface:** Hygiene / cleanup workflow
- **What's wrong:** The product has overlapping noise concepts: tiering (skip/lite/normal/premium), the noiseFilter Session Filter, and hidden_at. The Hygiene page surfaces none of this — it shows generic severity buckets (Errors/Warnings/Info) with no link to tiering or to the hidden/noise controls. A user cannot tell how a 'hygiene issue' relates to a session being skip-tiered, lite, or hidden, nor navigate from a hygiene issue to the relevant session or filter.
- **User impact:** Even once hygiene is real, the user gets context-free issue cards disconnected from the tiering/filtering model they actually use to manage noise, so they can't reason about or act on the relationship.
- **Evidence:** HygieneView.swift only renders kind/severity/message/detail/action with a Copy button (IssueCard, HygieneView.swift:269-356); there is no tier label, no link to a session, and no reference to noiseFilter or hidden state. Tiering lives separately in SessionTier.swift and the Session Filter in SettingsView.swift:271-284.
- **Suggested fix:** When implementing real issues, attach session ids / tier context to issues and make issue cards deep-link to the affected session or to the relevant Session Filter / tier setting, and add a one-line explainer tying hygiene to skip/lite/hidden.

#### `menubar-popover-6` · 🟡 Low · Badge live-count and popover 'Today' can diverge from each other and lag

- **Surface:** Menu bar popover + live sessions
- **What's wrong:** The badge derives its live count from a filesystem scan (serviceClient.liveSessions filtered to activityLevel == 'active', MenuBarController.swift:408-409) that is rate-limited to once per 5s and polled every 10s (MenuBarController.swift:25-26,82-84,401-405), while the popover's 'Today' stat reads serviceStatusStore.todayParentSessions (PopoverView.swift:83) which is a different metric (today's parent sessions) sourced from service status events. These are two unrelated numbers computed on different cadences. The badge shows " {today} ● {liveCount}" mixing the today-parents count and the live FS-scan count, but the popover only surfaces 'Today' and never the live count — so a user reading "●5" in the menu bar has no corresponding "5" anywhere in the popover to reconcile against.
- **User impact:** The menu bar's '●N' has no explanation or matching figure inside the popover, so users can't tell what the live number means or trust it; the two surfaces present different, un-cross-referenced counts of 'how much is going on'.
- **Evidence:** macos/Engram/MenuBarController.swift:396-419 (badge: today-parents + FS-scan live count, 5s/10s cadence); macos/Engram/Views/PopoverView.swift:83 (popover 'Today' = todayParentSessions only, no live count shown)
- **Suggested fix:** Surface the same live count in the popover (tie to finding menubar-popover-1's live section) and label the badge components, so '●N' in the menu bar corresponds to a visible, identically-computed 'N active' figure in the popover.

#### `command-palette-6` · 🟡 Low · Keyboard selection can scroll off-screen — no scroll-into-view on arrow navigation

- **Surface:** Command palette
- **What's wrong:** Arrow keys move `selectedIndex` (CommandPaletteView.swift:167-174) but the results `ScrollView`/`LazyVStack` has no `ScrollViewReader`/`scrollTo` (confirmed absent via grep). With up to 10 session hits or 16 navigation commands in a 360pt-tall sheet (MainWindowView.swift:69), arrowing past the visible rows moves the highlighted selection out of view; the user keeps the highlight off-screen and can't see what Enter will activate. Mouse hover does not drive `selectedIndex` either, so there's no alternate way to reconcile visible vs selected.
- **User impact:** A keyboard-only power user arrowing through a longer result set loses sight of the current selection and may activate the wrong item with Enter.
- **Evidence:** CommandPaletteView.swift:167-174 (arrow handlers mutate selectedIndex only); CommandPaletteView.swift:127-162 (ScrollView/LazyVStack with no ScrollViewReader); grep for ScrollViewReader/scrollTo in the file returns 0 matches; MainWindowView.swift:69 (sheet fixed at height 360).
- **Suggested fix:** Wrap the results list in a `ScrollViewReader` and call `proxy.scrollTo(visibleItems[selectedIndex].id)` whenever `selectedIndex` changes so the highlighted row stays visible.

#### `xc-states-3` · 🟡 Low · List/metrics pages render KPI cards and chrome during initial load with no skeleton — momentary all-zeros flash

- **Surface:** X-cut: empty / loading / error state consistency
- **What's wrong:** SessionsPageView, AgentsView, ProjectsView, SourcePulseView and TimelinePageView all gate only the *list body* on `!isLoading` (e.g. SessionsPageView:61 `if sessions.isEmpty && !isLoading`), but render the KPI cards / headers / filter chrome immediately with default zero values during the first async load. There is no SkeletonRow loading state for these (only HomeView and HygieneView use skeletons). Because the empty-state is also `&& !isLoading`, the first frame shows KPI cards of '0' with neither list, empty-state, nor skeleton.
