- **Suggested fix:** Optional polish: show SkeletonRow placeholders (as HomeView:83 does) for the KPI row while `isLoading && firstLoad`, or render KPI values as '—' until the first load completes.

#### `xc-visual-1` · 🟡 Low · Secondary text uses two different gray tokens: 111 raw `.secondary` vs 46 `Theme.secondaryText`

- **Surface:** X-cut: visual / theme / layout consistency
- **What's wrong:** Theme defines `secondaryText` as a hand-tuned dark-mode gray `NSColor(0xA0,0xA1,0xA8)` (Theme.swift:50-54) specifically because the system `.secondaryLabelColor` looked wrong on the app's custom `0x1A1D24` dark background. But 111 call sites still use the raw system `foregroundStyle(.secondary)` instead of `Theme.secondaryText` (46 sites). The system surfaces (Settings, Projects sheets, Popover, Replay/Resume dialogs) use `.secondary`; the dashboard Pages use `Theme.secondaryText`. In dark mode these are two visibly different grays for the same 'secondary label' role.
- **User impact:** Walking from the dashboard (Home/Sessions/Search) into Settings or a project-rename/archive sheet, the body/label gray shifts shade in dark mode. The app looks like two different products stitched together rather than one coherent surface.
- **Evidence:** Theme.swift:50-54 defines the custom secondaryText gray; raw `.secondary` concentrated in Views/Settings/GeneralSettingsSection.swift (6), Views/SettingsView.swift:315/325/335/397/411/421/729/736, Views/Projects/RenameSheet.swift (15), Views/Projects/ArchiveSheet.swift (11), Views/PopoverView.swift:100/115/118/143/161/175. Count: 111 raw `.secondary` vs 46 `Theme.secondaryText` across Views+Components.
- **Suggested fix:** Replace `foregroundStyle(.secondary)` with `Theme.secondaryText` (and `.tertiary`→`Theme.tertiaryText`) in the Settings/, Projects/, Popover, Resume/, Replay/ views, or add a SwiftUI lint rule. Pick one token per role app-wide.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Theme.swift:50-54 defines secondaryText as a hand-tuned dark-mode gray NSColor(0xA0,0xA1,0xA8) falling back to secondaryLabelColor in light mode — confirmed. All specifically cited raw .secondary sites verified present: GeneralSettingsSection.swift (6 hits), SettingsView.swift lines 315/325/335/397/411/421/729/736 all contain .secondary), RenameSheet.swift (15), ArchiveSheet.swift (11), PopoverView.swift lines 100/115/118/143/161/175 all contain .secondary. My own tree-wide grep found 126 raw .secondary vs 49 Theme.secondaryText (finding stated 111 vs 46 — slightly conservative, same direction). The dual-gray-for-one-role claim is real: in dark mode the custom 0xA0A1A8 token vs SwiftUI's hierarchical .secondary style produce visibly different grays for the same secondary-label role on the 0x1A1D24 background. This is a genuine cosmetic-consistency gap, but it is purely visual polish with no functional/accessibility impact, and SwiftUI's .secondary is a contrast-aware system style that remains legible — so I downgrade severity from medium to low.

#### `xc-visual-2` · 🟡 Low · Theme.green/red/orange/accent/gray tokens exist but components re-hardcode the same hex literals

- **Surface:** X-cut: visual / theme / layout consistency
- **What's wrong:** Theme exposes semantic accent tokens — `green = 0x30D158`, `red = 0xFF453A`, `orange = 0xFF9F0A`, `accent = 0x4A8FE7`, `gray = 0x636366` (Theme.swift:81-85). Yet shared components bypass these tokens and re-spell the identical hex literals inline. KPICard hardcodes `Color(hex: 0x30D158)`/`Color(hex: 0xFF453A)` for its delta instead of `Theme.green`/`Theme.red`; AlertBanner repeats `Color(hex: 0xFF9F0A)` four times instead of `Theme.orange`; TierBar re-spells all four accent hexes. This is the exact duplication the token enum was created to prevent — any future palette tweak now has to be found-and-replaced across files.
- **User impact:** No immediate visual break (the hexes happen to match today), but it guarantees future drift: edit Theme.orange and AlertBanner stays the old orange, so status banners diverge from the rest of the app's warning color.
- **Evidence:** Theme.swift:81-85 (token definitions). Duplicates: Components/KPICard.swift:21 `Color(hex: 0x30D158) : Color(hex: 0xFF453A)`; Components/AlertBanner.swift:11,23,29,32 all `Color(hex: 0xFF9F0A)`; Components/TierBar.swift:13-16 `0x4A8FE7 / 0x30D158 / 0xFF9F0A / 0x636366`.
- **Suggested fix:** Swap the literals for `Theme.green/red/orange/accent/gray` in KPICard.swift:21, AlertBanner.swift:11/23/29/32, and TierBar.swift:13-16. Zero visual change today, prevents drift.
- **Verify:** confirmed — Theme.swift:81-85 defines accent/green/orange/red/gray tokens (0x4A8FE7/0x30D158/0xFF9F0A/0xFF453A/0x636366) — confirmed. KPICard.swift:21 hardcodes deltaPositive ? Color(hex: 0x30D158) : Color(hex: 0xFF453A) instead of Theme.green/Theme.red — confirmed verbatim. AlertBanner.swift repeats Color(hex: 0xFF9F0A) at lines 11, 23, 29, and 32 (four times) instead of Theme.orange — confirmed. TierBar.swift:13-16 re-spells all four hexes 0x4A8FE7/0x30D158/0xFF9F0A/0x636366 instead of Theme.accent/green/orange/gray — confirmed verbatim. This is exactly the maintenance-duplication the token enum exists to prevent. Real finding, but it is a code-maintainability/DRY issue with zero user-visible effect today (the literals are currently identical to the tokens), so I downgrade severity from medium to low.

#### `xc-visual-3` · 🟡 Low · Card corner radius is inconsistent (4/6/8/10) with no shared token; KPICard=10, SessionCard=8

- **Surface:** X-cut: visual / theme / layout consistency
- **What's wrong:** There is no `Theme.cornerRadius` token. Across Views+Components there are 9 distinct corner-radius literals (8×48, 6×25, 4×18, 3×11, 10×6, plus 1/2/5/7). The two primary card components disagree: KPICard rounds at `cornerRadius: 10` (KPICard.swift:28/31) while SessionCard and ExpandableSessionCard round at `cornerRadius: 8` (SessionCard.swift:48/51, ExpandableSessionCard.swift:110/113). Even within the shared 'Theme.surface card' recipe the radius varies (28× use 8, 3× use 10, 2× use 6, 1× use 4). The KPI grid and the session list sit on the same Home page, so a user sees stat cards with visibly rounder corners than the session cards directly below them.
- **User impact:** On Home/Activity the KPI cards (r=10) and session cards (r=8) sit side by side with mismatched corner roundness — subtle but reads as unpolished/misaligned.
- **Evidence:** KPICard.swift:28,31 cornerRadius 10; SessionCard.swift:48,51 cornerRadius 8; ExpandableSessionCard.swift:110,113 cornerRadius 8; grep of RoundedRectangle radii yields 9 distinct values (8:48, 6:25, 4:18, 3:11, 10:6, 5:2, 2:2, 1:2, 7:1). No Theme corner-radius token exists (Theme.swift has none).
- **Suggested fix:** Add `Theme.cornerRadius` (and maybe `cornerRadiusSmall`) tokens and apply them to KPICard/SessionCard/ExpandableSessionCard so cards on the same page share one radius (standardize on 8 or 10).

#### `xc-visual-4` · 🟡 Low · Settings re-implements source display names, diverging from SourceColors.label (same source shows two names)

- **Surface:** X-cut: visual / theme / layout consistency
- **What's wrong:** SourceColors.label(for:) is documented as the 'single source of truth' for source → label (SourceColors.swift:4-5,31-54) and is used by SourcePill (SourcePill.swift:8). But SettingsView has its own private `displayName(for:)` switch (SettingsView.swift:694-708) that returns different strings for the same source IDs: `claude-code` → 'Claude Code' (SourceColors says 'Claude'), `gemini-cli` → 'Gemini CLI' (SourceColors says 'Gemini'), `iflow` → 'Iflow' (SourceColors says 'iFlow'). So the same backend source is labeled one way on session cards/pills and a different way in Settings.
- **User impact:** A user sees a source called 'Claude' on every session card but 'Claude Code' in Settings, and 'iFlow' vs 'Iflow' (different capitalization) — looks like a typo/inconsistency and undermines trust that the two refer to the same thing.
- **Evidence:** Canonical map: SourceColors.swift:33 (`claude-code`→'Claude'), :36 (`gemini-cli`→'Gemini'), :50 (`iflow`→'iFlow'). Divergent duplicate: SettingsView.swift:694-708 displayName — :697 'Claude Code', :700 'Gemini CLI', :701 'Iflow'. SourcePill.swift:8 uses the canonical label.
- **Suggested fix:** Delete SettingsView.displayName(for:) and call `SourceColors.label(for:)` everywhere, or if Settings genuinely needs longer names, add a single `SourceColors.longLabel(for:)` and use it consistently.
- **Verify:** confirmed — SourceColors.swift:4-5 documents label(for:) as the single source of truth; canonical labels at :33 claude-code->'Claude', :36 gemini-cli->'Gemini', :50 iflow->'iFlow'. SourcePill.swift:8 uses SourceColors.label(for:) so session pills show the canonical names — confirmed. SettingsView.swift:694-708 has a private static displayName(for:) returning divergent strings: :697 claude-code->'Claude Code', :700 gemini-cli->'Gemini CLI', :701 iflow->'Iflow' — confirmed verbatim. Verified it is NOT dead code: displayName is invoked at SettingsView.swift:633 and :646 to populate UsageTokenLimitEditableRow.name, and the same divergent strings are ALSO hardcoded in defaultRows at :600-609 ('Claude Code','Gemini CLI','Iflow'). So the divergence is genuinely rendered. However, the scope is narrower than 'session cards/pills vs Settings broadly': it only affects the per-source usage-token-limit editor rows, a niche Settings sub-panel, not the general Settings source list. The same backend source IS labeled two ways across surfaces (real inconsistency, and 'Iflow' vs 'iFlow' is an objective casing defect), but the blast radius is one minor editor table, so I downgrade severity from medium to low.

#### `xc-visual-5` · 🟡 Low · Semantic status colors hardcoded as raw `.green/.red/.orange/.blue` instead of Theme tokens, mixing two color systems

- **Surface:** X-cut: visual / theme / layout consistency
- **What's wrong:** Status/semantic colors are spelled as raw SwiftUI system colors in several main views instead of the matching Theme tokens, so 'success green' and 'error red' have two definitions in the app: Theme.green=0x30D158 / Theme.red=0xFF453A / Theme.orange=0xFF9F0A vs the system `.green/.red/.orange` (which are different shades). HygieneView uses `.foregroundStyle(.green)` (HygieneView.swift:125) for an all-clear state while TierBar uses Theme's green hex; ErrorDashboard uses `.red` (ErrorDashboardView.swift:47,80); the Projects sheets use `.orange`/`.red` for warnings (RenameSheet/ArchiveSheet/UndoSheet). The same 'warning orange' therefore differs between an AlertBanner (Theme.orange hex) and a project sheet (.orange system).
- **User impact:** Warning/error/success colors shift shade depending on which screen you're on (e.g. a warning is one orange in the home alert banner and a slightly different orange in the project-rename sheet), reducing visual coherence of status signaling.
- **Evidence:** Raw chromatic system colors: Views/Pages/HygieneView.swift:125 `.green`; Views/Observability/ErrorDashboardView.swift:47,80 `.red`; Views/Pages/SourcePulseView.swift:214 `.blue`; Views/Workspace/RepoDetailView.swift:21,35,84,87 `.blue`/`.green`; Views/Projects/RenameSheet.swift:85,149,289,303,310 `.orange` and :237,280,333 `.blue`; ArchiveSheet.swift:60,124,175 `.orange`. Contrast with Theme.swift:81-84 tokens and AlertBanner using Theme-equivalent orange.
- **Suggested fix:** Map semantic uses to Theme.green/red/orange/accent in HygieneView:125, ErrorDashboardView:47/80, SourcePulseView:214, RepoDetailView, and the Projects sheets so one 'success/warning/error' color is used app-wide.
